The Linguistic and Technical Definition of Fatwa
Defining 'fatwa' linguistically and technically

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the linguistic and technical meanings of 'fatwa' and cite Quranic evidence for both.

Core Idea
Fatwa linguistically means answering any question; technically, it is answering a question about Sharia rulings.

This passage opens the book by clarifying the very term 'fatwa'. Understanding its dual meaning—linguistic vs. technical—is essential for any student of iftaa, because the term carries a broader sense in the Quran that later became specialized. The author uses Quranic verses to show both usages, setting the stage for the serious responsibility of issuing fatwas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic meaning
Look at the language definition: 'fatwa' means answering any question, regardless of subject. The text gives three Quranic examples where it is used for non-Sharia matters (the king's dream, Yusuf's interpretation, the Queen of Sheba).
Note that the plural forms 'fatawa' and 'fatawa' are both acceptable.
2
Isolate the technical specialization
Observe how the term became specific to Sharia rulings. The text cites verses from Surah al-Nisa' where 'fatwa' is used for legal rulings about women and kalalah.
The Prophet (PBUH) also used it in this technical sense.
3
Compare the two meanings
Contrast the general linguistic usage (any question) with the technical usage (Sharia rulings). The same word evolved in meaning without losing its original root.
This evolution is common in Islamic terminology (naql).
4
Recognize the Quranic evidence for each
Sort the Quranic verses cited into two categories: those showing linguistic meaning (Yusuf 43, 46; al-Naml 32) and those showing technical meaning (al-Nisa' 127, 176).
This parsing exercise trains you to read Quranic usage contextually.
5
Apply the definition to a hypothetical
Given a scenario (e.g., someone asks about a dream interpretation vs. someone asks about zakat calculation), determine which is a fatwa linguistically and which technically.
Both are fatwas in the linguistic sense, but only the zakat question is a fatwa in the technical sense.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفتوى بفتح الفاء (وقيل: بضم الفاء أيضاً، كما في تاج العروس؛ ولكن الأوّل أصح وأشهر) والفتيا بضم الفاء، كلاهما يُجمع على الفتاوى (بكسر الواو) والفتاوى (بفتح الواو والألف المقصورة). وكل من الجَمْعين سائع مستعمل في كلام العلماء.
و "الفتوى" و"الفتيا" تُستعملان كحاصل مصدر من قولهم : أفتى يُفتى إفتاء، ومعناه في اللغة: الإجابة عن سؤال، سواء أكان متعلقاً بالأحكام الشرعية أم بغيرها، كما في قوله تعالى حكاية عن ملك مصر: وَقَالَ الْمَلَأُ أَفْتُونِي فِي رُؤْيَايَ إِن كُنتُمْ لِلرُّؤْيَا تَعْبُرُونَ (يوسف: 43) وحكايةً عن صاحب يوسف عليه السلام: يُوسُفُ أَيُّهَا الصِّدِيقُ أَفْتِنَا فِي سَبْعِ بَقَرَاتٍ سِمَانٍ يَأْكُلُهُنَّ سَبْعٌ عِجَافٌ وَسَبْعِ سُنُبُلَاتٍ خُضْرٍ وَأُخَرَ يَابِسَاتٍ لَّعَلَّي أَرْجِعُ إِلَى النَّاسِ لَعَلَّهُمْ يَعْلَمُونَ (يوسف: 46) وكما في قوله تعالى حكاية عن ملكة سبأ: وَقَالَتْ يَا أَيُّهَا الْمَلَأُ أَفْتُونِي فِي أَمْرِي مَا كُنتُ قَاطِعَةً أَمْرًا حَتَّى تَشْهَدُونِ (النمل: 32) وفي كلا الموضعين استعملت الكلمة للإجابة عن سؤال لا يتعلّق بالأحكام الشرعية. ثم قد خصت الكلمة للإجابة عن سؤال شرعي، وفى هذا المعنى استعملها القرآن الكريم حيث قال: وَيَسْتَفْتُونَكَ فِي النِّسَاءِ قُلِ اللَّهُ يُفْتِيكُمْ فِيهِنَّ (النساء: 127) وحيث قال: يَسْتَفْتُونَكَ قُلِ اللَّهُ يُفْتِيكُمْ فِي الْكَلَالَةِ (النساء: 176) وفي هذا المعنى استعملها النبي الكريم صلى الله عليه و سلّم في غيرِ واحدٍ
Fatwa (with fatha on the fa', and it is said also with dammah on the fa' as in Taj al-‘Arus, but the first is more correct and more famous) and fatya (with dammah on the fa'), both are pluralized as fatawa (with kasrah on the waw) and fatawa (with fatha on the waw and alif maqsurah). Both plurals are permissible and used in the speech of scholars. 'Fatwa' and 'Fatya' are used as a verbal noun from the saying 'afta yafti ifta', and its meaning in language is: answering a question, whether it pertains to legal rulings or not, as in the saying of Allah Most High narrating from the king of Egypt: 'The chiefs said: Give us a ruling concerning my dream, if you can interpret dreams' (Yusuf:43), and narrating from the companion of Yusuf peace be upon him: 'Yusuf, O truthful one, give us a ruling concerning seven fat cows which seven lean ones devour, and seven green ears and seven dry ones, that I may return to the people so that they may know' (Yusuf:46), and as in the saying of Allah Most High narrating from the queen of Sheba: 'She said: O chiefs, give me a ruling concerning my affair; I am not going to decide a matter until you witness' (al-Naml:32). In both places the word is used for answering a question not related to legal rulings. Then the word came to be specifically used for answering a legal question, and in this sense the noble Qur'an used it where He said: 'They seek a ruling from you concerning women. Say: Allah gives you a ruling concerning them' (al-Nisa':127) and where He said: 'They seek a ruling from you. Say: Allah gives you a ruling concerning kalalah' (al-Nisa':176). And in this sense the noble Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him) used it in more than one instance.
Source pages p. 6

Commentary
This passage is a definitional opening to the book. The author first clarifies the pronunciation and plural forms of the word 'fatwa', noting that both 'fatawa' and 'fatawa' (with different vowelizations) are used. He then explains the linguistic origin: 'fatwa' is a verbal noun from 'ifta', meaning simply to answer a question, regardless of subject. He proves this with three Quranic examples: the king of Egypt's dream, Prophet Yusuf's interpretation, and the Queen of Sheba's consultation. In all these, the word 'fatwa' is used for non-Sharia matters. However, the term later became specialized in Islamic usage for answering questions about Sharia rulings, as evidenced by verses from Surah al-Nisa'. This establishes the technical meaning of fatwa as a legal opinion. The author ends by noting that the Prophet (PBUH) used it in this technical sense. The passage thus sets the foundation for the book's discussion by clarifying the term itself.

Key Terms
الفتوى (al-fatwa): In language: answering any question; in Sharia: answering a question about legal rulings.
الفتيا (al-fatya): Synonym of fatwa, same meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the linguistic meaning of 'fatwa' according to this passage?
A) A binding legal ruling
B) Answering any question, whether legal or not
C) A judicial verdict
D) A type of oath

Key Takeaway
Fatwa has a broad linguistic meaning (answering any question) and a specialized technical meaning (answering a Sharia question), as shown in Quranic usage.

Definition of Fatwa and Its Three Types
Defining fatwa linguistically and terminologically, introducing its three types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the linguistic and terminological definitions of fatwa and identify the three categories of fatwa with examples from the Quran and Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
Fatwa means answering a religious question; legislative fatwa from the Lawgiver becomes binding law for all.

The term 'fatwa' is foundational in Islamic jurisprudence. Before a mufti can issue a fatwa, we must understand what a fatwa is and its sources. This lesson clarifies the linguistic roots, the technical meaning, and the three types of fatwa, with special emphasis on the legislative type that originates directly from the Quran and Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic meaning
Examine the Arabic roots and Quranic usage of 'fatwa' to see that it simply means 'answering a question' in a general sense, as shown in Surah Yusuf and an-Naml.
Note the two plural forms: fatawa and fatawa.
2
Distinguish technical from linguistic usage
Recognize that in Shariah and modern terminology, fatwa is specialized to mean answering a religious question, not limited to legal rulings but including beliefs and hadith sciences.
The term 'religious' is preferred over 'legal' in the definition.
3
Learn the threefold classification
Memorize the three categories: legislative fatwa (from the Lawgiver), jurisprudential fatwa (from scholars), and particular fatwa (specific cases). Understand that the text elaborates only on legislative fatwa.
This classification highlights the authority level of each type.
4
Analyze a Quranic example of legislative fatwa
Read the verses from Surah an-Nisa (127 and 176) provided in the text; note how Allah responds to a question and the ruling becomes general law.
These verses are considered primary sources of law in Hanafi usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفتوى بفتح الفاء (وقيل: بضم الفاء أيضاً، كما في تاج العروس؛ ولكن الأوّل أصح وأشهر) والفتيا بضم الفاء، كلاهما يُجمع على الفتاوى (بكسر الواو) والفتاوى (بفتح الواو والألف المقصورة). وكل من الجَمْعين سائع مستعمل في كلام العلماء.
و "الفتوى" و"الفتيا" تُستعملان كحاصل مصدر من قولهم : أفتى يُفتى إفتاء، ومعناه في اللغة: الإجابة عن سؤال، سواء أكان متعلقاً بالأحكام الشرعية أم بغيرها، كما في قوله تعالى حكاية عن ملك مصر: {وَقَالَ الْمَلَأُ أَفْتُونِي فِي رُؤْيَايَ إِن كُنتُمْ لِلرُّؤْيَا تَعْبُرُونَ} [يوسف: 43] وحكايةً عن صاحب يوسف عليه السلام: {يُوسُفُ أَيُّهَا الصِّدِيقُ أَفْتِنَا فِي سَبْعِ بَقَرَاتٍ سِمَانٍ يَأْكُلُهُنَّ سَبْعٌ عِجَافٌ وَسَبْعِ سُنُبُلَاتٍ خُضْرٍ وَأُخَرَ يَابِسَاتٍ لَّعَلِّي أَرْجِعُ إِلَى النَّاسِ لَعَلَّهُمْ يَعْلَمُونَ} [يوسف: 46] وكما في قوله تعالى حكاية عن ملكة سبأ: {وَقَالَتِ الْمَلَأُ أَفْتُونِي فِي أَمْرِي مَا كُنتُ قَاطِعَةً أَمْرًا حَتَّى تَشْهَدُونِ} [النمل: 32] وفي كلا الموضعين استعملت الكلمة للإجابة عن سؤال لا يتعلّق بالأحكام الشرعية. ثم قد خصت الكلمة للإجابة عن سؤال شرعي، وفى هذا المعنى استعملها القرآن الكريم حيث قال: {وَيَسْتَفْتُونَكَ فِي النِّسَاءِ قُلِ اللَّهُ يُفْتِيكُمْ فِيهِنَّ} [النساء: 127] وحيث قال: {يَسْتَفْتُونَكَ قُلِ اللَّهُ يُفْتِيكُمْ فِي الْكَلَالَةِ} [النساء: 176] وفي هذا المعنى استعملها النبي الكريم صلى الله عليه و سلّم في غيرِ واحدٍ من أحاديثه الشريفة، كما ورد في قوله عليه السلام: "أَجْرَوْكُمْ عَلَى الْفُتْيَا أَجْرَؤُكُمْ عَلَى النَّارِ" (1) فمعنى الكلمة في اصطلاح اليوم : "الجواب عن مسئلة دينية." وإنّما اخترنا لفظ "الدينية"، دونَ "الشرعية" لأن المفتي لا يُجيب عن الأحكام الشرعيّة العملية فحسب، بل ربما يُجيب عن مسائل دينية اعتقادية، وعن معنى الأحاديث، وكيفية إسنادها وما إلى ذلك من المسائل التي تتعلق بالدين وعلومه.
ثمّ إنّ كلمة الفتوى والإفتاء أطلق فى كلام القوم على معانٍ ثلاثة يُمكن أن نقسمها على ثلاثة أقسام الفتوى التشريعية، والفتوى الفقهية، والفتوى الجزئية.
الفتوى التشريعية
أمّا الفتوى التشريعيّة، فهى التى صدرت من الشارع، إما بوحي متلو في القرآن الكريم أو بوحى غير متلو فى سنة النبي الكريم صلى الله عليه وسلّم فى الجواب عن سؤال، أو لبيان نازلةٍ فى عهد النبي الكريم صلى الله عليه وسلّم، فأصبحت شرعاً عاما. وذلك مثل قوله تعالى المذكور فيما سبق: {وَيَسْتَفْتُونَكَ فِي النِّسَاءِ قُلِ اللَّهُ يُفْتِيكُمْ فِيهِنَّ} [النساء: 127] وقوله تعالى: {يَسْتَفْتُونَكَ قُلِ اللَّهُ يُفْتِيكُمْ فِي الْكَلَالَةِ} [النساء: 176] وقوله تعالى: {يَسْأَلُونَكَ عَنِ الْأَهِلَّةِ قُلْ هِيَ مَوَاقِيتُ لِلنَّاسِ وَالْحَجِّ} [البقرة: 189]
Fatwa with fatha on the fa (and it is said with dhamma on the fa as well, as in Taj al-Arus; but the first is more correct and famous) and fatya with dhamma on the fa, both pluralize as fatawa (with kasra on the waw) and fatawa (with fatha on the waw and alif maqsura). Both plurals are permissible and used in the speech of scholars. "Fatwa" and "fatya" are used as a verbal noun from the saying: afta yufti iftaan, and its meaning in language is: answering a question, whether related to legal rulings or not, as in the Almighty's words narrating from the king of Egypt: "And the chiefs said: Give us a fatwa concerning my vision, if you can interpret visions" [Yusuf: 43] and narrating from the companion of Yusuf, peace be upon him: "Yusuf, O truthful one, give us a fatwa concerning seven fat cows which seven lean ones devour, and seven green ears of grain and others dry" [Yusuf: 46] and as in the Almighty's words narrating from the queen of Sheba: "She said: O chiefs, give me a fatwa concerning my affair; I never decide an affair until you witness" [an-Naml: 32]. In both places the word was used for answering a question not related to legal rulings. Then the word was specialized for answering a religious question, and in this meaning the Noble Quran used it where He said: "And they ask you for a fatwa concerning women; say: Allah gives you a fatwa concerning them" [an-Nisa: 127] and where He said: "They ask you for a fatwa; say: Allah gives you a fatwa concerning al-Kalalah" [an-Nisa: 176]. In this meaning the Noble Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, used it in more than one of his noble hadiths, as is reported in his saying, peace be upon him: "The most daring of you in giving fatwa is the most daring of you towards the Fire." So the meaning of the word in today's terminology is: "The answer concerning a religious matter." We chose the word "religious" instead of "legal" because the mufti does not answer only practical legal rulings, but perhaps answers matters of religious belief, and the meaning of hadiths, and the method of their chains, and so on from matters related to religion and its sciences. Then, the word fatwa and ifta' is used in the speech of the people in three meanings that we can divide into three categories: legislative fatwa, jurisprudential fatwa, and particular fatwa. Legislative fatwa: As for legislative fatwa, it is what issued from the Lawgiver, either by recited revelation in the Noble Quran or by non-recited revelation in the Sunnah of the Noble Prophet, peace be upon him, in answer to a question, or to explain an incident that occurred in the era of the Noble Prophet, peace be upon him, and thus became general law. That is like the aforementioned saying of the Almighty: "And they ask you for a fatwa concerning women; say: Allah gives you a fatwa concerning them" [an-Nisa: 127] and His saying: "They ask you for a fatwa; say: Allah gives you a fatwa concerning al-Kalalah" [an-Nisa: 176] and His saying: "They ask you about the new moons; say: They are appointed times for the people and for the Hajj" [al-Baqarah: 189]
Source pages p. 7

Commentary
This passage is a foundational definition and classification of fatwa. The author begins by clarifying the pronunciation and plural forms of the word 'fatwa', settling on 'fatwa' with fatha as the most correct. Linguistically, fatwa simply means answering any question, regardless of subject. The author proves this with three Quranic verses where the word is used for non-legal consultations: the king of Egypt's dream, the prisoner's request to Yusuf, and the queen of Sheba's council. However, in the Shariah and common usage, fatwa has become specialized to mean answering a religious question, not limited to practical legal rulings but including beliefs, hadith interpretation, and other religious sciences. The author then introduces a threefold classification of fatwa: legislative (from the Lawgiver), jurisprudential (from scholars), and particular (specific cases). The legislative fatwa is defined as divine revelation—either Quran or Sunnah—that answered a question or addressed an incident and became general law. Examples include the verses on women and kalalah. This classification is important because it distinguishes between the infallible fatwa of the Prophet and the fallible fatwa of a mufti.

Key Terms
الفتوى (al-fatwa): The answer concerning a religious matter, whether legal, doctrinal, or related to hadith sciences.
الفتوى التشريعية (al-fatwa al-tashri'iyya): A fatwa issued by the Lawgiver (Allah or His Prophet) that becomes general legislation.
الفتوى الفقهية (al-fatwa al-fiqhiyya): A fatwa issued by a qualified mufti deriving rulings from the Shariah sources.
الفتوى الجزئية (al-fatwa al-juz'iyya): A fatwa concerning a specific incident or individual case, not general.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary reason the author uses the word 'religious' (diniyya) instead of 'legal' (shar'iyya) in defining fatwa?
A) Because the mufti also answers questions about beliefs and hadith sciences.
B) Because the Quran never uses 'legal' for fatwa.
C) Because linguistic fatwa was not legal in origin.
D) Because the Prophet avoided the term 'legal'.

Key Takeaway
Fatwa is broadly defined as answering a religious question, with legislative fatwa from revelation being the highest authority, while mufti's fatwa is fallible and non-binding.

Distinguishing Fatwa from Qada: Scope and Nature
Distinguishing fatwa from qada by four criteria.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state four key differences between fatwa and qada, and apply them to distinguish advisory opinions from binding judgments.

Core Idea
Fatwa advises on all rulings; qada enforces only binding ones.

This lesson unpacks the passage's clear demarcation between fatwa (legal opinion) and qada (judicial verdict). Understanding these distinctions is essential for a mufti to operate within his proper role as an advisor, not a judge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two functions
Recognize that both fatwa and qada involve legal rulings but serve different purposes: fatwa guides, qada settles and enforces.
The mufti and the qadi have distinct responsibilities.
2
Analyze the fact-verification distinction
The mufti does not verify the truth of the questioner's facts; the judge does (by evidence). The mufti says 'the ruling is such' without guaranteeing it matches reality.
This is why fatwa is not binding.
3
Analyze the scope of rulings
Fatwa covers all categories: obligation, prohibition, recommendation, dislike, permission, validity/nullity. Qada only covers enforceable matters, not mere recommendations or minor dislikes.
Recommendations and minor dislikes cannot be enforced by a judge.
4
Analyze the scope of subject matter
Fatwa includes beliefs and acts of worship; qada only deals with these incidentally (e.g., when they relate to disputes).
Fatwa is comprehensive, qada is limited.
5
Synthesize the overall distinction
Combine the four points: fatwa is advisory, non-binding, broad in scope; qada is binding, enforced, and narrower.
The mufti must never exceed his advisory role.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أصول الإفتاء
الفتوى وخطورتها
وظيفته أن يُحقِّق صحته فى نفس الأمر بطلب البينة وغيرها. ولذلك يقول المفتى: "الحكم فى الصورة المسئول عنها كذا." ولا يلزم منه أن تكونَ الصورة المسئول عنها موافقة للواقع في نفس الأمر.
الثالث: الفتوى تجرى فيما يترتب عليه الوجوب أو الحرمة أو الإباحة أو النُّدب أو الكراهة، أو الصحة أو البطلان أما القضاء، فلا يجرى فيما يترتب عليه الندب أو الكراهة التنزيهيّة، لأنّ الندب والكراهة حث على الفعل أو الترك من غير إلزام، والقضاء إجبار والزام.
الرابع: أن الفتوى لا تقتصر على الأحكام الفقهية، بل تتعلق بالعقائد والعبادات أيضاً، والقضاء لا يتعلّق بالعقائد والعبادات إلا عن طريق التبعية.
تهيب السلف للفتيا
قال الإمام النووي رحمه الله تعالى في مقدمة شرح المهذب.
إعلم أن الإفتاء عظيم الخَطَرِ، قدير الموقع كثير الفضل، لأن المفتي وارث الأنبياء صلوات الله عليهم وسلامه، وقائم بفرض الكفاية، ولكنّه مَعْرَضَ للخطر، ولهذا قالوا: المُفتى موقع عن الله سبحانه وتعالى.
فيجب على المفتى أن يشعُرَ بخُطورَةِ منصب الإفتاء، وأنه ليس إبداء للآراء الشخصيّة، أو تحكيماً للعقل المجرّد أو تفعيلاً للعواطف النفسيّة، وإنما هو تبيين لما شرع الله سبحانه وتعالى لعباده من شرائع وأحكام لحياتهم الفرديّة والاجتماعية التى تضمن لهم السعادة الأبدية في الدنيا والآخرة. وكفى لخطورة هذا المنصب ومهابته أنه نيابة عن الله عزوجل ورسوله صلى الله عليه وسلم في بيان تلك الأحكام، وتوقيع عن رب السَّماوات والأرض ورب العالمين، كما سمّاه الإمام النووى وابنُ القيم رحمهما الله تعالى، وقال ابن القيم رحمه الله تعالى: "وَإِذَا كَانَ مَنْصِبُ التَّوْقِيعِ عَنْ الْمُلُوكِ بالمحل الذي لا يُنْكَرُ فَضْلُهُ ، وَلَا يُجْهَلُ قَدْرُهُ ، وَهُوَ مِنْ أَعْلَى المَرَاتِبِ السَّنِيَّاتِ ، فَكَيْفَ بِمَنْصِب التوقيع عَنْ رَبِّ الْأَرْضِ وَالسَّمَوَاتِ؟ فَحَقِيق بِمَنْ أُقِيمَ فِي هَذَا المَنْصِب أَنْ يَعْدَّ لَهُ عِدَّتَهُ، وَأَنْ يَتَأَهَبَ لَهُ أُهْبَتَهُ،"
Principles of Ifta: Fatwa and its gravity. Its function is to ascertain correctness in reality by requesting evidence and other means. Therefore the mufti says: "The ruling in the inquired case is such." It does not require that the inquired case correspond to reality. Third: Fatwa applies to whatever entails obligation, prohibition, permission, recommendation, or dislike, or validity/invalidity. As for qada, it does not apply to what entails recommendation or minor dislike, because recommendation and dislike are encouragement to act or refrain without compulsion, while qada is compulsion and obligation. Fourth: Fatwa is not limited to fiqh rulings, but also relates to beliefs and acts of worship, while qada does not relate to beliefs and acts of worship except incidentally. Caution of the Salaf regarding fatwa: Imam Nawawi (may Allah have mercy on him) said in the introduction to Sharh al-Muhadhdhab: "Know that issuing fatwa is of great danger, lofty in rank, abundant in virtue, because the mufti is the heir of the prophets, and fulfilling a communal obligation, but it is exposed to danger, and for this they said: The mufti is a signatory on behalf of Allah Almighty." So the mufti must feel the gravity of the position of ifta, and that it is not an expression of personal opinions, nor a validation of mere reason nor an activation of emotional sentiments, but rather an explanation of what Allah Almighty has legislated for His servants of laws and rulings for their individual and social lives that guarantee them eternal happiness in this world and the hereafter. Sufficient for the gravity and awe of this position is that it is deputyship from Allah Almighty and His Messenger in explaining those rulings, and a signing on behalf of the Lord of the heavens and earth and Lord of the worlds, as Imam Nawawi and Ibn al-Qayyim (may Allah have mercy on them) called it. And Ibn al-Qayyim said: "When the position of signing on behalf of kings is at a place whose virtue is not denied and whose rank is not unknown, and it is among the highest dignified stations, then how about the position of signing on behalf of the Lord of the earth and heavens? It behooves one who is placed in this position to prepare his provisions and make ready his equipment."
Source pages p. 9

Commentary
This passage is a lesson in the etiquette of the mufti (mufti_adab) from the book Usul al-Ifta' by Muhammad Taqi Usmani. The author first distinguishes fatwa from judicial judgment (qada) by four points: (1) The mufti's role is advisory—he gives an opinion based on the facts presented without verifying them, while a judge must ascertain the truth. (2) The mufti does not guarantee that his fatwa corresponds to reality; the judge's verdict is binding. (3) Fatwa covers all categories of rulings (obligatory, forbidden, recommended, etc.), while qada is limited to enforceable matters, not mere recommendations. (4) Fatwa includes beliefs and acts of worship, whereas qada only deals with these incidentally. Then the author emphasizes the gravity of fatwa, quoting Imam Nawawi that the mufti is a signatory on behalf of Allah and an heir of the prophets, and Ibn al-Qayyim's comparison of signing for kings versus signing for the Lord of the heavens. The concluding lesson is that the mufti must realize he is not expressing personal opinion but explaining Allah's law, and must prepare himself accordingly.

Key Terms
الفتوى (al-fatwā): A legal opinion given by a mufti in response to a question, covering all categories of rulings including beliefs and acts of worship, but not binding like a judge's verdict.
القضاء (al-qaḍā’): Judicial judgment that is binding and enforced, based on verification of facts, and limited to matters that can be enforced, not including mere recommendations or beliefs except incidentally.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is a correct difference between fatwa and qada?
A) Fatwa applies to enforceable matters only; qada to all rulings.
B) Fatwa covers beliefs and worship; qada does so only incidentally.
C) The mufti must verify facts; the judge does not.
D) Qada can include recommendatory rulings; fatwa cannot.

Key Takeaway
Fatwa is an advisory opinion that covers all rulings and does not require factual verification, while qada is a binding judgment limited to enforceable matters.

Adab al-Mufti — Ethics of the Mufti
intermediate
8 min
The Gravity and Responsibility of Issuing Fatwa
Emphasizing the grave responsibility and proper mindset of the mufti.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the mufti's role is a grave responsibility and how the metaphor of 'signatory on behalf of Allah' shapes the mufti's mindset.

Core Idea
The mufti signs for Allah, not himself; his task is to explain divine law, not give personal opinions.

This lesson focuses on the profound gravity of the position of ifta. Drawing from warnings of the Salaf, the passage reminds the mufti that he is a deputy of Allah and an heir of the prophets, and must prepare accordingly.

Guided Path
1
Comprehend the title 'signatory on behalf of Allah'
Recognize that the mufti is not speaking his own words but conveying Allah's ruling. This is a weighty responsibility.
Imam Nawawi and Ibn Qayyim used this phrase.
2
Contrast personal opinion with divine explanation
The mufti must not present personal views, mere reason, or emotions. His fatwa must be a faithful explanation of the Shariah.
The mufti is a mubayyin (explainer).
3
Reflect on the comparison with kings
Signing for kings is highly honored; signing for the Lord of the heavens is infinitely greater. This elevates the mufti's rank but also increases the danger.
Ibn Qayyim's analogy.
4
Understand the required preparation
The mufti must prepare himself thoroughly—knowledge, piety, and caution—since he is acting on behalf of Allah.
The passage says: 'prepare his provisions and make ready his equipment.'
5
Apply this mindset to modern ifta
Contemporary muftis must avoid casual fatwas, especially on social media, and always feel the weight of representing Allah's law.
This protects the mufti from arrogance and error.

أصول الإفتاء
الفتوى وخطورتها
وظيفته أن يُحقِّق صحته فى نفس الأمر بطلب البينة وغيرها. ولذلك يقول المفتى: "الحكم فى الصورة المسئول عنها كذا." ولا يلزم منه أن تكونَ الصورة المسئول عنها موافقة للواقع في نفس الأمر.
الثالث: الفتوى تجرى فيما يترتب عليه الوجوب أو الحرمة أو الإباحة أو النُّدب أو الكراهة، أو الصحة أو البطلان أما القضاء، فلا يجرى فيما يترتب عليه الندب أو الكراهة التنزيهيّة، لأنّ الندب والكراهة حث على الفعل أو الترك من غير إلزام، والقضاء إجبار والزام.
الرابع: أن الفتوى لا تقتصر على الأحكام الفقهية، بل تتعلق بالعقائد والعبادات أيضاً، والقضاء لا يتعلّق بالعقائد والعبادات إلا عن طريق التبعية.
تهيب السلف للفتيا

المفتى (al-muftī): One who issues fatwa; he is a signatory on behalf of Allah, an heir of the prophets, and must be aware of the gravity of his position.

According to the passage, what must the mufti feel about the position of ifta?

Key Takeaway

Adab al-Mufti — Ethics of the Mufti
intermediate
8 min
The Mufti: A Signatory for Allah – The Gravity of Issuing Fatwa
Stating the gravity and danger of the office of mufti

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the mufti's role is described as 'tawqi' 'an Allah' and identify the hadith and Salaf practices that demonstrate the caution required in issuing fatwa.

Core Idea
The mufti signs on behalf of Allah – the most solemn responsibility in Islam.

The author opens with a powerful statement: issuing fatwa is of great danger and great virtue. This lesson unpacks why the mufti is called a 'signatory for Allah' and why the early scholars (Salaf) were so cautious. The passage sets the foundation for the entire book: the mufti must be deeply conscious of his responsibility.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the central metaphor
Understand the phrase 'al-mufti muwaqqi' 'an Allah' (the mufti is a signatory on behalf of Allah). Consider what this implies about authority, accountability, and the weight of every fatwa.
This metaphor is from Ibn al-Qayyim, highlighting that the mufti represents Allah in conveying rulings.
2
Examine the Quranic evidence
Identify the two verses cited (4:127 and 4:176) where Allah Himself issues fatwas. Reflect on why this elevates the office and reminds the mufti of his solemn duty.
Allah's direct involvement shows the importance of ifta; the mufti follows in that role.
3
Analyze the hadith warning
Read the hadith: 'The most daring among you regarding fatwa is the most daring regarding the Fire.' Explain its meaning and how it instills caution.
This hadith is a severe warning against reckless fatwa-giving.
4
Study the Salaf example
Examine the report of Ibn 'Umar, who frequently said 'La adri' (I do not know) and his statement about people wanting to make scholars a 'bridge to Hell'. Derive the practical lesson for a mufti.
Ibn 'Umar's caution exemplifies the Salaf's fear of speaking without knowledge.
5
Synthesize the overall message
Combine the metaphor, Quran, hadith, and Salaf practice to articulate why fatwa is not personal opinion but a sacred trust. Conclude what qualities a mufti must cultivate.
The mufti must prepare thoroughly, speak truth, and be conscious of standing before Allah.

Source Text

أصول الإفتاء
۱۳
الفتوى وخطورتها
"إعلم أن الإفتاء عظيم الخَطَرِ، قدير الموقع كثير الفضل، لأن المفتي وارث الأنبياء صلوات الله عليهم وسلامه، وقائم بفرض الكفاية، ولكنّه مَعْرَضَ
للخطر، ولهذا قالوا: المُفتى موقع عن الله سبحانه وتعالى."
فيجب على المفتى أن يشعُرَ بخُطورَةِ منصب الإفتاء، وأنه ليس إبداء للآراء الشخصيّة، أو تحكيماً للعقل المجرّد أو تفعيلاً للعواطف النفسيّة، وإنما هو تبيين لما شرع الله سبحانه وتعالى لعباده من شرائع وأحكام لحياتهم الفرديّة والاجتماعية التى تضمن لهم السعادة الأبدية في الدنيا والآخرة. وكفى لخطورة هذا المنصب ومهابته أنه نيابة عن الله عزوجل ورسوله صلى الله عليه وسلم في بيان تلك الأحكام، وتوقيع عن رب
السَّماوات والأرض ورب العالمين، كما سمّاه الإمام النووى وابنُ القيم
(1)
رحمهما الله تعالى، وقال ابن القيم رحمه الله تعالى: "وَإِذَا كَانَ مَنْصِبُ التَّوْقِيعِ عَنْ الْمُلُوكِ بالمحل الذي لا يُنْكَرُ فَضْلُهُ ، وَلَا يُجْهَلُ قَدْرُهُ ، وَهُوَ مِنْ أَعْلَى المَرَاتِبِ السَّنِيَّاتِ ، فَكَيْفَ بِمَنْصِب التوقيع عَنْ رَبِّ الْأَرْضِ وَالسَّمَوَاتِ؟ فَحَقِيق بِمَنْ أُقِيمَ فِي هَذَا المَنْصِب أَنْ يَعْدَّ لَهُ عِدَّتَهُ، وَأَنْ يَتَأَهَبَ لَهُ أُهْبَتَهُ،
(۱) الإمام ابن القيم: محمد بن أبي بكر الدمشقي، أبو عبد الله، شمس الدين ابن قيم الجوزية، ولد رحمه الله بدمشق سنة ٦٩١ هـ ، كان والده قيما للمدرسة الجوزية، فقيل في النسبة إليه "ابن قيم "الجوزية كان أحد كبار العلماء. تتلمذ لشيخ الإسلام ابن تيمية حتى كان لا يخرج عن شيء من أقواله، بل ينتصر له في جميع ما يصدر عنه. وهو الذي هذّب كتبه ونشر علمه، وسُجن معه في قلعة دمشق. وأُطلق بعد وفاة شيخه ابن تيميّة. وكان حَسَن الخلق محبوباً عند الناس، أغري بحب الكتب، فجمع منها عدداً عظيماً. وألّف تصانيف كثيرة منها: "إعلام الموقعين" و "الطرق الحكمية في السياسة الشرعية" و "زاد المعاد" في السيرة النبوية على صاحبها ألف ألف تحية. توفي رحمه الله سنة بدمشق. ملخص من الدرر الكامنة :۳ : ٤۰۰ إلى ٤٠٣ والأعلام ٦: (٥٦)

أصول الإفتاء
١٤
الفتوى وخطورتها
جمہ
وأَنْ يَعْلَمَ قَدْرَ الْمَقَامِ الَّذِي أَقِيمَ فِيهِ ، وَلَا يَكُونُ فِي صَدْرِهِ حَرَجٌ مِنْ قَوْلِ الْحَقِّ وَالصَّدْعِ بِهِ : فَإِنَّ اللَّهَ نَاصِرُهُ وَهَادِيهِ ، وَكَيْف و هُوَ الْمَنْصِبُ الَّذِي تَوَفَّاهُ بِنَفْسِهِ رَبُّ الْأَرْبَابِ فَقَالَ تَعَالَى: ﴿وَيَسْتَفْتُونَكَ فِي النِّسَاءِ قُلِ اللَّهُ يُفْتِيكُمْ فِيهِنَّ وَمَا يُتْلَى عَلَيْكُمْ فِي الكتب [النساء: ۱۲۷] وَكَفَى بِمَا تَوَلَّاهُ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى بِنَفْسِهِ شَرَفًا وَجَلَالَةٌ ، إِذْ يَقُولُ فِي كِتَابِهِ : يَسْتَفْتُونَكَ قُلِ اللَّهُ يُفْتِيكُمْ فِي الْكَلَلَة [النساء: ١٧٦]، وَلِيَعْلَمَ الْمُفْتِي عَمَّنْ يَنُوبُ فِي فَتْوَاهُ ، وَلِيُوقِنَ أَنَّهُ مَسْئُولٌ غَدًا وَمَوْقُوفٌ بَيْنَ يَدي اللهِ. كما يكفى لبيان خطورته ما روى عن النبي الكريم صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قالَ: "أَجْرَؤُكُمْ عَلَى الْفُتْيَا أَجْرَؤُكُمْ عَلَى النَّارِ. وهناك آثار كثيرة تدلّ على تهيب السلف للفتيا، وتحرزهم من ذلك مهما (۳) أمكن. نذكر منها مايلي: أخرج ابن عبد البر رحمه الله تعالى بسنده إلى عقبة بن مسلم قال: "صحبت ابن عُمر أربعة وثلاثين شهراً فكثيراً ما كان يُسئل فيقول: لا أدرى، ثم يلتفت إلى فيقول: أتدرى مايُريد هؤلاء؟ يُريدون أن يجعلوا ظهورنا جسراً لهم إلى جهنّم .
(۱) إعلام الموقعين عن رب العالمين ج ١ ص ١١ . (۲) تقدم تخريجه في أول حاشية لهذا الكتاب

(٤) جامع بيان العلم وفضله، ص ٣١٦ رقم ۸۹۹
Principles of Issuing Fatwa
13
Fatwa and Its Gravity
"Know that issuing fatwa is of great danger, immense in its position, abundant in virtue, because the mufti is the heir of the prophets, peace and blessings of Allah be upon them, and he is fulfilling a communal obligation, but he is exposed to danger. For this reason they said: The mufti is a signatory on behalf of Allah, the Exalted and Glorious."
So the mufti must feel the gravity of the office of ifta, and that it is not an expression of personal opinions, nor a validation of abstract reason, nor an activation of emotional sentiments, but rather it is an explanation of what Allah, the Exalted and Glorious, has legislated for His servants of laws and rulings for their individual and social lives that guarantee them eternal happiness in this world and the Hereafter. Sufficient for the gravity and awe of this office is that it is representation of Allah, the Mighty and Majestic, and His Messenger, peace be upon him, in explaining those rulings, and a signatory on behalf of the Lord of the heavens and the earth and the Lord of the worlds, as Imam al-Nawawi and Ibn al-Qayyim (1) , may Allah have mercy on them, called it. And Ibn al-Qayyim, may Allah have mercy on him, said: "If the office of signing on behalf of kings is in a position whose virtue is not denied and whose rank is not unknown, and it is one of the highest lofty ranks, then how about the office of signing on behalf of the Lord of the earth and the heavens? It is fitting for one who is placed in this office to prepare his equipment and to make ready his preparedness...
...and that he know the measure of the station in which he is placed, and that there be no constraint in his chest from speaking the truth and proclaiming it - for Allah is his supporter and guide. And how could it be otherwise when it is the office that the Lord of lords Himself undertook? He said, the Exalted: 'And they ask you for a ruling concerning women. Say: Allah gives you a ruling concerning them and what is recited to you in the Book.' [Quran 4:127] And sufficient for its honor and majesty is that Allah, the Exalted, Himself undertook it, as He says in His Book: 'They ask you for a ruling, say: Allah gives you a ruling concerning al-kalalah.' [Quran 4:176] And so that the mufti knows on whose behalf he acts in his fatwa, and so that he is certain that he will be questioned tomorrow and will stand before Allah. Also sufficient to explain its gravity is what is narrated from the noble Prophet, peace be upon him, that he said: 'The most daring among you regarding fatwa is the most daring among you regarding the Fire.' And there are many reports indicating the caution of the Salaf regarding fatwa and their carefulness as much as possible. We mention among them the following: Ibn Abd al-Barr, may Allah have mercy on him, narrated with his chain to 'Uqbah ibn Muslim who said: 'I accompanied Ibn 'Umar for thirty-four months, and he was often asked a question and he would say: I do not know. Then he would turn to me and say: Do you know what these people want? They want to make our backs a bridge for them to Hell.'
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This passage opens the subject of the gravity of issuing fatwa (الفتوى وخطورتها). The author, Mufti Muhammad Taqi Usmani, begins by stating a well-known maxim among scholars: 'Issuing fatwa is of great danger, immense in its position, abundant in virtue, because the mufti is the heir of the prophets and is fulfilling a communal obligation (فرض كفاية), but he is exposed to danger.' The mufti is described as a 'signatory on behalf of Allah' (موقع عن الله). This carries immense responsibility. The author then explains that fatwa is not a matter of personal opinion, abstract reason, or emotional impulse; it is the explanation of Allah's revealed laws for human life. The office of mufti is a representation (نيابة) of Allah and His Messenger. He quotes Ibn al-Qayyim's famous analogy: if signing on behalf of kings is a high honor, how much more so signing on behalf of the Lord of the heavens? The mufti must prepare himself thoroughly and speak the truth without hesitation. The Quranic verses (4:127 and 4:176) show that Allah Himself issued fatwas, which elevates the office. The hadith 'The most daring among you regarding fatwa is the most daring regarding the Fire' warns against reckless fatwa-giving. The author then cites the practice of the Salaf, specifically the companion Ibn 'Umar, who would frequently say 'I do not know' to avoid the danger of speaking without knowledge. This sets the tone for the entire book: the mufti must be deeply conscious of his responsibility.

Key Terms
الإفتاء (al-iftaa): The act of issuing a fatwa, i.e., giving a legal ruling on a question of Islamic law.
المفتي (al-mufti): The one who issues fatwas; the jurist qualified to give legal rulings.
توقيع عن الله (tawqi' 'an Allah): Signing on behalf of Allah; a metaphor for the mufti's role as a deputy in conveying Allah's rulings.
فرض الكفاية (fard al-kifayah): A communal obligation; if some Muslims perform it, the rest are absolved.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the hadith 'The most daring among you regarding fatwa is the most daring regarding the Fire' imply?
A) Issuing fatwa is a sin that leads to Hell.
B) Only those who give fatwa will enter Hell.
C) Reckless fatwa-giving incurs divine punishment; caution is required.
D) Fatwa is not an important matter.

Key Takeaway
The mufti is a signatory for Allah; issuing fatwa is a grave responsibility that demands thorough preparation, truthfulness, and caution, as exemplified by the Salaf.

Adab al-Mufti — Ethics of the Mufti
intermediate
8 min
The Gravity of Fatwa: Divine Lineage and Salaf Caution
Exhortation on the gravity of fatwa with Quran, hadith, and Salaf examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Quranic and hadith evidence for the gravity of fatwa and explain why the Salaf were extremely cautious in issuing fatwa.

Core Idea
Fatwa is Allah's own office; the mufti speaks on His behalf and will be held accountable.

This passage from Usul al-Ifta by Mufti Muhammad Taqi Usmani sets the foundational adab for a mufti: profound awareness of responsibility. The author cites Quranic verses where Allah Himself answers inquiries, a hadith warning that the bold fatwa-giver is bold to the Fire, and numerous reports of the Companions and early scholars who shunned fatwa unless necessary. This lesson instills the essential mindset of caution and piety.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the divine origin of fatwa
Allah says in the Quran: 'They ask you for a ruling concerning women. Say: Allah gives you a ruling...' (4:127) and similarly for kalala (4:176). The mufti acts as a deputy of Allah, a role of immense honor and responsibility.
The mufti must internalize that he is not speaking from his own authority but as a representative of the Divine Law.
2
Understand the prophetic warning
The Prophet ﷺ said: 'The most daring of you in giving fatwa is the most daring of you to the Fire.' This highlights the grave spiritual danger of issuing fatwa without due knowledge and caution.
This hadith should make every mufti fear issuing hasty or incorrect rulings.
3
Learn from the Salaf's caution
Ibn Umar often said 'I don't know.' The Companions of Badr wished others would spare them the burden. Imam al-Shafi'i and Sufyan ibn 'Uyayna praised silence over fatwa. Bishr al-Harith said: 'Whoever loves to be asked is not fit to be asked.'
Their caution did not stem from ignorance but from deep knowledge of the consequences.
4
Internalize the mufti's accountability
The mufti will be questioned on the Day of Judgment about every fatwa he issued. Allah says: 'He utters no word except that there is with him a watcher ready.' (50:18)
This accountability should produce fear and humility, not pride.

Usul al-Ifta 14: The Fatwa and Its Gravity. And that he knows the status of the position in which he is placed, and there is no constraint in his heart from speaking the truth and proclaiming it, for Allah is his supporter and guide. How could it be otherwise, when it is the office which the Lord of lords Himself undertook, for He said: 'They ask you for a ruling concerning women. Say: Allah gives you a ruling concerning them and what is recited to you in the Book' (al-Nisa 4:127). Sufficient is that Allah Himself undertook it as honor and majesty, for He says in His Book: 'They ask you for a ruling. Say: Allah gives you a ruling concerning al-kalala' (al-Nisa 4:176). And so that the mufti knows on whose behalf he issues fatwa, and is certain that he will be questioned tomorrow and stood before Allah. Sufficient to explain its gravity is what was narrated from the noble Prophet ﷺ that he said: 'The most daring of you in giving fatwa is the most daring of you to the Fire.' There are many reports indicating the caution of the Salaf regarding fatwa and their guarding against it as much as (3) possible. We mention from them the following: Ibn Abd al-Barr (may Allah have mercy on him) narrated with his chain to Uqba ibn Muslim who said: 'I accompanied Ibn Umar for thirty-four months, and often he would be asked and he would say: I do not know. Then he would turn to me and say: Do you know what these people want? They want to make our backs a bridge for them to Hell.' (1) I'lam al-Muwaqqi'in 'an Rabb al-'Alamin vol. 1 p. 11. (2) Its takhrij has preceded in the first footnote of this book. (3) Imam Ibn Abd al-Barr: He is Yusuf ibn Abdullah ibn Muhammad ibn Abd al-Barr ibn Asim al-Namari al-Qurtubi, the imam, hafiz of Andalusia and Bukhari of the Maghrib, the jurist, hadith critic, usuli, author of al-Tamhid, al-Istidhkar, and al-Isti'ab fi Ma'rifat al-Ashab. He was born on Friday of Rabi' al-Akhir 368 AH. He died on the night of Friday, the end of Rabi' al-Akhir 463 AH at the age of ninety-five. Summarized from the introduction of the tahqiq of al-Istidhkar. (4) Jami' Bayan al-'Ilm wa Fadlihi, p. 316 no. 899. [PAGE_012] Usul al-Ifta: The Fatwa and Its Gravity. (1) Al-Khatib al-Baghdadi (may Allah have mercy on him) said in the chapter on forbidding haste in fatwa for fear of slipping: Allah said: 'We will write down their testimony and they will be questioned.' (al-Zukhruf 43:19). And He said: 'That He may ask the truthful about their truthfulness' (al-Ahzab 33:8). And He said: 'He utters no word except that there is with him a watcher ready.' (Qaf 50:18). And the Companions (may Allah be pleased with them) hardly gave fatwa except for what had actually occurred, trusting that Allah would grant success at the time of an incident for the answer. Each of them wished that his companion would suffice him the fatwa. (2)1 Then al-Khatib narrated with his chain from al-Bara' ibn 'Azib (may Allah be pleased with him) who said: 'I saw three hundred of the people of Badr; not one of them but loved that his companion would suffice him the fatwa.' And from Imam al-Shafi'i who said: 'I have not seen anyone whom Allah had gathered in him the tools of fatwa as He gathered in Ibn 'Uyayna, yet he was more silent about fatwa than him.' And from Sufyan ibn 'Uyayna who said: 'The most knowledgeable of people about fatwa is the most silent among them about it, and the most ignorant of people about fatwa is the most talkative among them about it.' And from Bishr ibn al-Harith who said: 'Whoever loves to be asked is not fit to be asked.' (1) Al-Khatib al-Baghdadi: He is Ahmad ibn Ali ibn Thabit ibn Ahmad ibn Mahdi Abu Bakr al-Khatib, the great hafiz. He was born in 392 AH. He and his father were khatibs in some areas of Iraq. He studied fiqh under Qadi Abu al-Tayyib al-Tabari, the Shaykh of the Shafi'is in Baghdad in his time. Al-Khatib was among the great hadith scholars, skilled and knowledgeable in the intricacies of hadith sciences. His works exceed sixty, including 'Tarikh Madinat al-Salam' known as 'Tarikh Baghdad' which spread in fame, and 'al-Faqih wa al-Mutafaqqih' and others. He died on the 7th of Dhu al-Hijjah 463 AH in Baghdad and was buried beside the arif Bishr al-Hafi. Summarized from Siyar A'lam al-Nubala 18:270ff and Tabaqat al-Shafi'iyya al-Kubra 4:29-39 and the introduction of the tahqiq of Tarikh Madinat al-Salam by Dr. Bashshar 'Awwad Ma'ruf. (2) Al-Faqih wa al-Mutafaqqih by al-Khatib (vol. 2 p. 349) from the Dar Ibn al-Jawzi edition. (3) Also narrated by al-Ajuri in Akhlaq al-'Ulama p. 104.
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage is a strong exhortation on the gravity and responsibility of issuing fatwa. It opens by reminding the mufti to recognize the lofty station he occupies, as Allah Himself has taken charge of issuing fatwa in the Quran (e.g., verses on women and kalala). The mufti must realize he acts as a deputy for Allah and will be held accountable. The hadith 'the most daring in fatwa is most daring to the Fire' underscores the danger. Then the author cites numerous examples from the Salaf showing their extreme caution: Ibn Umar often said 'I don't know,' and the Companions of Badr wished others would spare them the burden of fatwa. Scholars like Imam al-Shafi'i and Sufyan ibn 'Uyayna praised silence in fatwa. The overall message is that fatwa is not a light matter; it requires deep knowledge and fear of Allah. This lesson instills the proper adab and mindset for a mufti.

Key Terms
الفتوى (al-fatwa): The formal legal opinion issued by a qualified jurist (mufti) in response to a question.
المفتي (al-mufti): The person authorized to issue fatwa, possessing the requisite knowledge and piety.
تهيب السلف (tahayyub al-salaf): The caution and reluctance of the early generations (Salaf) in giving fatwa, due to its gravity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What did the Prophet ﷺ say about those who are most daring in giving fatwa?
A) They are the most knowledgeable of people.
B) They are the most daring to the Fire.
C) They will be rewarded greatly.
D) They are the successors of the prophets.

Key Takeaway
Fatwa is a grave responsibility; a mufti must be deeply cautious, fear Allah, and emulate the Salaf's reluctance.

Adab al-Mufti — Ethics of the Mufti
beginner
8 min
Warning Against Hastiness in Fatwa
Collection of warnings about fatwa's gravity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key attitudes of early scholars toward fatwa and apply their caution to modern iftaa practice.

Core Idea
Issuing fatwa is a grave responsibility; the early scholars feared it more than any other task.

This lesson presents a collection of warnings from the Quran, the Companions, and the early imams about the dangers of hastiness in issuing fatwa. It reveals that the most knowledgeable were the most cautious, and that a mufti must tremble at the thought of being questioned by Allah about his opinions.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the Quranic Basis for Accountability
Read the three Quranic verses cited. They establish that every word is recorded and that Allah will question the truthful. This frames fatwa as a matter of ultimate accountability.
The verses are from Surah al-Zukhruf, al-Ahzab, and Qaf.
2
Understand the Companions' Extreme Caution
Note that the Companions only gave fatwa on actual incidents (ma nazala) and each wished another would take the responsibility. Al-Bara' ibn 'Azib reports that even the Badr veterans felt this way.
This shows that even the highest level of piety and knowledge did not make them reckless.
3
Analyze Statements of Later Scholars
Imam al-Shafi'i and Sufyan ibn 'Uyayna emphasize that the most knowledgeable are the most silent, while the ignorant are the most talkative. Bishr al-Harith warns that desiring to be asked disqualifies one.
These statements link knowledge to humility, not to eagerness to speak.
4
Reflect on the Physical Fear of Early Imams
The narrations describe physical trembling, color change, and feeling like standing between Paradise and Hell when asked a question. Imam Abu Hanifa states that only fear of knowledge being lost compels him to give fatwa.
This fear is a sign of taqwa, not weakness.
5
Apply to Contemporary Iftaa Practice
Consider how a modern mufti should approach questions: with thorough research, verification of the mufta bihi position, and a deep sense of accountability. Avoid giving quick answers or desiring to be asked.
The same caution applies to written fatwas and online responses.

Principles of Issuing Fatwa
Fatwa and Its Gravity
(1)
Al-Khatib al-Baghdadi (may Allah have mercy on him) said in the chapter on forbidding rushing to fatwa for fear of slipping: Allah, Blessed and Exalted, said: "They will write down their testimony, and they will be questioned" [al-Zukhruf: 19]. And He said: "That He may ask the truthful about their truth" [al-Ahzab: 8]. And He said: "Not a word does he utter but there is a watcher by him ready [to record]" [Qaf: 18]. The Companions (may Allah be pleased with them) would hardly ever give a fatwa except concerning what had actually occurred, trusting that Allah would grant success when an incident arose for which a reply was needed. Each of them wished that his companion would spare him the fatwa.
(2)1
Then al-Khatib narrated with his chain from al-Bara' ibn 'Azib (may Allah be pleased with him) who said: "I saw three hundred of the people of Badr, and there was not one of them but loved that his companion would spare him the fatwa." And from Imam al-Shafi'i who said: "I have not seen anyone in whom Allah had gathered the tools of fatwa as He gathered in Ibn 'Uyayna, yet he was more silent about giving fatwa than him." And from Sufyan ibn 'Uyayna who said: "The most knowledgeable of people about fatwa is the most silent among them regarding it, and the most ignorant of people about fatwa is the most talkative among them regarding it."
And from Bishr ibn al-Harith who said: "Whoever loves to be asked is not fit to be asked."
(1) Al-Khatib al-Baghdadi... [biographical note omitted for brevity]
(2) al-Faqih wa al-Mutafaqqih by al-Khatib, vol. 2 p. 349
(3) Also narrated by al-Ajuri in Akhlaq al-'Ulama p. 104

Principles of Issuing Fatwa

Fatwa and Its Gravity
And from 'Ata' ibn al-Sa'ib who said: "I came across people such that when one of them was asked about something, he would speak while trembling." And from al-Ash'ath from Muhammad (ibn Sirin) who said: "When he was asked about something of fiqh regarding the lawful and unlawful, his colour would change and he would become different until he seemed not to be the same person." And from one of the students of Imam Malik (may Allah have mercy on him) who said: "By Allah, when Malik was asked about a question, he was as if standing between Paradise and Hellfire." And from Muhammad ibn al-Munkadir who said: "Indeed the scholar is between Allah and His creation, so let him see how he enters upon them." And from 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with them both) who said: "You ask us for fatwa as if we will not be asked about what we give you as fatwa." And from Imam Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) who said: "Whoever speaks about something of knowledge and assumes it while thinking that Allah will not ask him about how he gave fatwa in the religion of Allah, has made his soul and his religion easy for him." And from him (may Allah have mercy on him) who said: "Were it not for the fear of Allah that knowledge would be lost, I would never have given a fatwa to anyone — for him there is ease and upon me the burden." And from Muhammad ibn Wasi' who said: "The first to be summoned..."
[...]
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage is a collection of warnings about the grave responsibility of issuing fatwa (mufti_adab). It opens with Quranic verses reminding that every word is recorded and that Allah will question the truthful. The early Companions (Sahaba) were extremely cautious; they only gave fatwa when necessary and each preferred another to bear that responsibility. Al-Khatib al-Baghdadi then narrates statements from various scholars: al-Bara' ibn 'Azib reports that even the Badr veterans wished to avoid fatwa. Imam al-Shafi'i and Sufyan ibn 'Uyayna highlight that the most knowledgeable are the most silent, while the ignorant are the most talkative. Bishr al-Harith warns that desiring to be asked disqualifies one from being a mufti. Further narrations describe the physical fear exhibited by early scholars when asked about halal and haram — trembling, color change, as if standing between Paradise and Hell. Imam Abu Hanifa states that one who takes knowledge lightly and assumes he will not be questioned about his fatwa has made his religion easy for himself. He also confesses that only fear of knowledge being lost compels him to give fatwa, knowing the burden outweighs the ease for the questioner. Muhammad ibn Wasi' mentions that the first to be summoned (for judgment) will be those who gave fatwa without knowledge. This lesson instills profound caution and humility in the mufti, emphasizing that fatwa is a trust from Allah, not a platform for personal opinion.

Key Terms
الفتوى (al-fatwa): A non-binding legal opinion issued by a qualified scholar (mufti) in response to a question about Islamic law.
التسرع إلى الفتوى (al-tasarru' ila al-fatwa): Hastiness in issuing fatwa without due deliberation, fear of error, and knowledge of the consequences.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what was the attitude of the Companions toward giving fatwa?
A) They eagerly gave fatwa on every issue.
B) They hardly gave fatwa except when necessary, and each wished his companion would spare him the task.
C) They only gave fatwa if they were paid.
D) They considered fatwa a light matter.

Key Takeaway
Fatwa is a grave trust; the most knowledgeable are the most cautious, and a mufti must constantly fear accountability before Allah.

Adab al-Mufti — Ethics of the Mufti
intermediate
6 min
The Gravity and Fear of Fatwa in the Salaf
Compilation of narrations on the gravity of fatwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state two narrations that show the physical or emotional reactions of the salaf when asked about fatwa, and explain why these reactions reflect the mufti's accountability before Allah.

Core Idea
Fatwa is a momentous trust; the salaf trembled when asked about halal and haram.

This passage gathers powerful testimonies from the early generations that depict the profound fear and reverence they had towards issuing fatwa. As you read these narrations, you will see that the mufti's role is not one of casual opinion but of ultimate responsibility before Allah. The salaf's example serves as a corrective to any modern tendency to treat fatwa lightly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the narrations
Scan the passage and list each anecdote from a salaf scholar (e.g., Ata ibn al-Sa'ib, Ibn Sirin, Malik, etc.). Note the specific description of their reaction—physical trembling, change of color, or verbal expression of fear.
2
Extract the common attitude
What is the recurring theme across all these narrations? Each one emphasizes that the scholar felt immense weight and anxiety when asked about a legal matter. This is not due to lack of knowledge but due to the awareness of being questioned by Allah.
Contrast this with the attitude of someone who gives fatwa casually.
3
Connect to the mufti's responsibility
Reflect on how these reactions translate into actual adab (etiquette) for a mufti. The salaf's fear should be internalised: the mufti must verify his answer, rely on the madhhab's strongest positions, and constantly remember that he will be asked about his fatwa on the Day of Judgment.
Imam Abu Hanifa's statement is particularly instructive: 'If not for the fear that knowledge would be lost, I would not give fatwa.'

(۲) هو عمر بن حَلْدَة على وزن حمزة. ليراجع تاج العروس (٨ ٦٤ الزرقي التابعي القاضي، سمع من أبي هريرة رضي الله تعالى عنه الله تعالى عنه وولي قضاء المدينة في خلافة عبد الملك بن مروان. قال محمد بن عمر: "كان عمر بن خلدة ثقةً قليل الحديث وكان رجلا مهيبا صارما ورعا عفيفا ولم يرتزق على القضاء شيئا، فلما عُزل قيل له: يا أبا حفص كيف رأيت ما كنت فيه؟ قال: كان لنا إخوان فقطعناهم وكانت لنا أَرَيضةٌ نعيش منها فبعناها وأنفقنا ثمنها." (ملخص من الطبقات الكبرى لابن سعد، الطبقة الثانية من أهل المدينة من التابعين من الأنصار ٧ ٢٧٥، وليراجع أيضاً المعرفة والتاريخ للعلامة يعقوب الفسوي رحمه الله تعالى ١: ٥٥٦) (۳) ربيعة بن أبي عبد الرحمن فروخ الإمام الفقيه أبو عثمان التيمي المدني مولى آل المنكدر، قال الخطيب: "كان فقيهاً عالما حافظا للفقه والحديث " كما كان بصيرا بالرأي ولذلك يقال له: ربيعةُ الرّأي. وكان أستاذ الإمام مالك رحمهما الله تعالى. تُوُفِّي سنة ١٣٦ هـ. (ملخص من تذكرة الحفاظ ۱: ١٥٧ و ١٥٨) (٤) ابْنُ هُرْمُز رحمه الله تعالى: هو أبو بكر عبد الله بن يزيد بن هرمز الأصم، وقيل اسمه يزيد بن عبد بن هرمز فقيه المدينة من التابعين. وما روى الحديث إلا قليلاً. وكان من العباد الزهاد. قال الإمام مالك: جلست إلى ابن هرمز ثلاث عشرة سنة واستحلفني أن لا أذكر اسمه في الحديث." وقال إمام دار الهجرة: "كنت أحب أن أقتدي "به. وكان قليل الفتيا، شديد التحفظ، وكان بصيرا بالكلام، يردّ على أهل الأهواء كان من أعلم الناس بذلك. وقال الإمام مالك: "لم يكن أحد بالمدينة، له شرف، إلا إذا حزبه أمر رجع إلى ابن هرمز، وكان إذا قدم المدينة غنم الصدقة، ترك أكل اللحم لكونهم لا يأخذونها كما ينبغي. " تو " توفّي رحمه الله سنة ١٤٨ هـ. (ملخص من سير أعلام النبلاء ٦: ۳۷۹ و ۳۸۰)
Fatwa and its gravity. And from Ata ibn al-Sa'ib said: 'I encountered people that if one of them was asked about something, he would speak while trembling.' And from al-Ash'ath from Muhammad (ibn Sirin) said: 'When he was asked about something of fiqh concerning halal and haram, his color would change and he would become altered, until he appeared not the same as before.' And from one of the students of Imam Malik (may Allah have mercy on him) said: 'By Allah, when Malik was asked about a question, it was as if he was standing between Paradise and Hellfire.' And from Muhammad ibn al-Munkadir said: 'Indeed the scholar is between Allah and His creation, so let him see how he enters upon them.' And from Abdullah ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with them both) said: 'You ask us for fatwa as if we are not going to be asked about what we answer you with.' And from Imam Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) said: 'Whoever speaks about something of knowledge and takes it upon himself while thinking that Allah will not ask him about how he gave fatwa in the religion of Allah, then he has taken his soul and his religion lightly.' And from him (may Allah have mercy on him) said: 'If not for the fear of Allah that knowledge would be lost, I would not give fatwa to anyone; for him there is comfort and upon me the burden.' And from Muhammad ibn Wasi' said: 'The first to be called to account on the Day of Judgment are the jurists.' And from Sufyan ibn Uyayna (may Allah have mercy on him) said: 'Seventy sins of the ignorant are forgiven before one sin of the scholar is forgiven.' And from Ibn Khalda that he said to Rabi'a ibn Abi Abd al-Rahman: 'Indeed I see the people have surrounded you. So when a man asks you about a question, let not your concern be to extricate him, but let your concern be to extricate yourself.' And from Malik (may Allah have mercy on him) from Ibn Hurmuz: [then footnotes with sources and biographies follow]
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage is a collection of narrations (athar) from the early generations (salaf) illustrating the immense fear and caution they had regarding issuing fatwas. The author gathers these to instill in the mufti the gravity of his task. The narrations show trembling, changes in color, and the feeling of standing between Paradise and Hell. Imam Abu Hanifa's statement is particularly striking: he would not give fatwa at all if not for the fear of knowledge being lost, emphasizing that the comfort is for the seeker while the burden is on the scholar. The passage serves as a powerful reminder that fatwa is not a light matter but one of utmost responsibility before Allah.

Key Terms
فتوى (fatwa): A legal ruling issued by a qualified mufti in response to a question about Islamic law.
ورع (wara'): Scrupulousness and piety that leads one to avoid even doubtful matters, especially in giving fatwa.
فقهاء (fuqaha): Jurists who are experts in Islamic jurisprudence, especially those qualified to issue fatwa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) He gave fatwa to gain fame and reward.
B) He gave fatwa only because of the fear that knowledge would be lost.
C) He gave fatwa because he enjoyed being asked.
D) He gave fatwa to refute other scholars.

Key Takeaway
The salaf's fear of fatwa teaches that issuing a fatwa is a momentous act that requires deep humility and accountability before Allah.

Adab al-Mufti — Ethics of the Mufti
intermediate
8 min
The Gravity of Fatwa and Caution of Early Scholars
Relating historical accounts on the seriousness of giving fatwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key reasons why early Hanafi scholars were extremely cautious about issuing fatwas and apply the principle that a mufti should avoid seeking the role and should refer difficult questions.

Core Idea
A mufti who rushes to give fatwa risks his Hereafter; true caution reflects taqwa and humility.

This passage illustrates the profound fear and caution that the early Muslim scholars, including the Companions and successors, had regarding the office of giving fatwa. They avoided it whenever possible, referring questions to others, and those who sought it out were often warned of spiritual loss. In the Hanafi tradition, this establishes the adab (etiquette) of the mufti: humility, reluctance, and reliance on Allah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central warning
The passage opens with a stark image: the mufti who sells his religion for worldly gain. What is the warning? Highlight the exact phrase and its implication.
The phrase: 'the mufti has sold his religion for this worldly gain.'
2
Analyze the hadith on authority
Al-Khatib uses the hadith 'Do not seek authority' to argue against seeking the position of mufti. How does this analogy work? Consider the similarity between imara and fatwa.
Fatwa is a form of authority over people's religion and worldly matters.
3
Examine the Companions' practice
The anecdotes about 120 Ansar and Umayr ibn Sa'id show that even the most knowledgeable Companions avoided giving fatwa. What does this teach about the proper attitude?
They referred questions to others and wished to be free of the burden.
4
Understand the final admonition
Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn 'Abbas said that giving fatwa on every question is insanity. What does this mean for a mufti's competence and humility?
It emphasizes that a mufti must recognize his limits and not pretend to know everything.
5
Synthesize the adab principle
From these accounts, derive the Hanafi adab: a mufti should be reluctant, refer questions when unsure, and not seek the role. How does this align with the broader adab al-mufti literature?
This caution is a core part of the mufti's spiritual preparation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفتوى وخطورتها
بعد نقل هذا القول: "ففكرت فيمن باع آخرته بدنيا غيره، فوجدتُه المفتى يأتيه الرّجل قد حنث في امرأته ورقيقه فيقول له: "لا شيئ عليك، فيذهب الحانث فيتمتع بامرأته ورقيقه، وقد باع المفتى دينه بدنيا هذا." (١) وقال الخطيب بعد رواية بعض ماذكر من الآثار: "قل من حرص على الفتيا وسابق إليها وثابر عليها، إلا قل توفيقه واضطرب في أمره، وإن كان كارها لذلك، غير مؤثر له ما وَجَدَ عنه مندوحة، وأحال الأمر فيه على غيره، كانت المعونة له من الله تعالى أكثر. " واستدل على قوله بالحديث الصحيح: "لا تسئل الإمارة، فإنك إن أعطيتها عن مسئلة وكلت إليها، وإن أُعْطِيتَها عن غير مسئلةٍ أُعِنت عليها." (٢)
وذكر النووي رحمه الله تعالى عن عبد الرحمن بن أبي ليلى قال: أدركت عشرين ومائة من الأنصار ،الصحابة، يُسأل أحدهم عن المسئلة فيَرُدُّها هذا إلى هذا، حتى تُرفع إلى الأول. "" وفي رواية: "ما منهم من يُحدث بحديث إلا ودَّ أن أخاه كفاه إيَّاه، ولا يُستفتى عن شيء إلا ود أن أخاه كفاه الفتيا." (٣) وأخرج الخطيب رحمه الله تعالى عن عمير بن سعيد ، قال : (٤)
"سألت علقمة (١) مسألة، فقال : انت عَبيدة فسله ، فأتيتُ عَبِيْدة فقال : عن ائت علقمة ، فقلت : علقمة أرسلنى إليك ، فقال : انت مسروقاً فسله ، فأتيت مسروقاً فسألته، فقال : انت علقمة فسله ، فقلت : علقمة أرسلني إلى عبيدة ، وعبيدة أرسلني إليك ، قال : فأت عبد الرحمن بن أبي ليلى ، فأتيت عبد الرحمن بن أبي ليلى فسألته فكرهه ، ثم رجعت إلى علقمة فأخبرته ، قال : كان يقال: أجراً القوم على الفتيا أدناهم علماً"
وذكر النووي رحمه الله تعالى عن ابن مسعود وابن عباس رضي الله عنهم قالا: من أفتى عن كلّ ما يُسأل فهو مجنون (٤)
Fatwa and its danger. After quoting this statement: "I thought about who sells his Hereafter for the worldly gain of someone else, and I found it is the mufti: a man comes to him who has made his wife and slaves forbidden to him by oath (hanith), and he tells him: 'Nothing is upon you,' so the oath-breaker goes and enjoys his wife and slaves, and the mufti has sold his religion for this worldly gain." (1) Al-Khatib said after relating some of the reported traditions: "Few are those who are keen on fatwa and race to it and persist in it except that their success becomes little and their affair becomes disturbed. But if he dislikes that and does not prefer it as long as he finds an alternative, and refers the matter to others, then divine assistance from Allah is greater for him." And he supported his statement with the authentic hadith: "Do not seek authority, for if you are given it due to asking, you will be entrusted to it, but if you are given it without asking, you will be helped in it." (2)
Al-Nawawi mentioned from Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Layla who said: I encountered one hundred and twenty of the Ansar among the Companions; one of them would be asked a question and he would refer it to another, and so on until it went back to the first. In another narration: "Not one of them would narrate a hadith except that he wished his brother had sufficed him, and none would be asked for a fatwa except that he wished his brother had sufficed him with the fatwa." (3) Al-Khatib narrated from Umayr ibn Sa'id who said: (4)
"I asked 'Alqamah (1) a question, and he said: Go to 'Ubaydah and ask him. So I came to 'Ubaydah, and he said: Go to 'Alqamah. I said: 'Alqamah sent me to you. He said: Go to Masruq and ask him. So I came to Masruq and asked him, and he said: Go to 'Alqamah and ask him. I said: 'Alqamah sent me to 'Ubaydah, and 'Ubaydah sent me to you. He said: Then go to Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Layla. So I came to Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Layla and asked him, but he disliked it. Then I returned to 'Alqamah and informed him. He said: It used to be said: 'The most deserving of the people of fatwa is the one with the least knowledge.'"
And al-Nawawi mentioned from Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn 'Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them) that they said: "Whoever gives a fatwa about everything he is asked is insane." (4)
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage discusses the extreme caution of the early Muslim scholars regarding the issuance of fatwa. The author begins by quoting a powerful observation: the mufti who carelessly issues a ruling that allows a person to violate a valid oath is effectively selling his own religion for a worldly gain. This highlights the immense responsibility and danger of the role.

Al-Khatib al-Baghdadi then notes that those who are eager to give fatwa often suffer a lack of divine success and confusion in their affairs. In contrast, those who are reluctant and refer questions to others receive greater assistance from Allah. He supports this with the prophetic hadith about not seeking authority (imara), which applies by analogy to the position of mufti.

Next, al-Nawawi reports from Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Layla that among 120 Ansar companions, they would pass a question around, each referring it to another, not wanting to be the one to answer. This shows their collective sense of responsibility and fear of error.

Another anecdote illustrates this: Umayr ibn Sa'id asked 'Alqamah a question, but 'Alqamah directed him to 'Ubaydah, who directed him to Masruq, who directed him to Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Layla, who disliked it. Finally, 'Alqamah remarked that the most deserving of the people to give fatwa is the one with the least knowledge—a saying that emphasizes how the learned ones avoid it, whereas those with less knowledge may rush to it.

Finally, a stern warning from Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn 'Abbas: whoever gives a fatwa on every matter he is asked about is insane. This is hyperbole to stress that it is impossible to know everything; a mufti must recognize his limits.

In the Hanafi tradition, these accounts reinforce the principle that a mufti must possess deep knowledge (fiqh) and God-consciousness (taqwa), and should be hesitant to issue rulings without certainty. The mufti's adab includes humility, consultation, and recognizing that fatwa is a matter of din (religion).

Key Terms
الفتوى (al-fatwa): A non-binding legal opinion issued by a qualified jurist (mufti) explaining the ruling of Allah on a particular matter.
المفتى (al-mufti): The person who issues a fatwa; a qualified jurist who is competent in ijtihad within the madhhab.
الإمارة (al-imara): Position of authority or leadership; in the hadith, it refers to any position of power including that of a judge or mufti.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what did Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn 'Abbas say about someone who gives a fatwa on everything he is asked?
A) He is a knowledgeable scholar.
B) He is insane.
C) He is courageous.
D) He is a sinner.

Key Takeaway
Early scholars' extreme caution in issuing fatwas teaches that a mufti must have taqwa, humility, and avoid seeking the position; rushing into fatwa risks one's Hereafter.

Adab al-Mufti — Ethics of the Mufti

The Gravity of Fatwa: Lessons from Early Scholars
Warning against hasty fatwa from early scholars

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the principles of caution in fatwa as demonstrated by early scholars and apply them to evaluate a mufti's conduct.

Core Idea
A mufti must fear giving fatwa; the most daring are the least knowledgeable.

This passage presents a collection of reports from early great scholars who exhibited extreme hesitation in issuing fatwa. These reports serve as a powerful reminder of the heavy responsibility that comes with speaking on behalf of Allah's law. The lesson distills the key adab of the mufti: humility, fear, and deep knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the pattern of reluctance
Identify how Alqamah repeatedly deferred the questioner to other scholars, showing his unwillingness to answer directly. Notice the chain of referrals.
This reluctance is the opposite of the common assumption that a mufti must always answer.
2
Extract the core principle
From Alqamah's statement, note the principle: 'The most courageous of people in giving fatwa are the least knowledgeable among them.' This links audacity in fatwa to ignorance.
Contrast with the idea that confidence comes from knowledge—here, confidence without knowledge is dangerous.
3
Understand the severity from the Sahaba
Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn Abbas said that anyone who gives a fatwa on everything asked is insane. This highlights that a mufti must know when to say 'I don't know'.
The word 'mad' (majnun) shows the extreme view of answering without proper knowledge.
4
Appreciate the standard of Umar
The report that Umar would gather the people of Badr for weighty questions shows that even the greatest scholar consults others. No single person has all knowledge.
This sets a high bar: a mufti should not rely solely on his own opinion.
5
Internalize the mufti's duty
Imam al-Shafi'i's hesitation and Zubayd's fear of declaring halal/haram illustrate the ultimate lesson: a mufti must weigh silence vs. answer and fear misattributing to Allah.
The mufti acts as a spokesperson for Allah; thus, extreme caution is required.

Source Text

الفتوى وخطورتها
سألت علقمة مسألة، فقال: انت عبيدة فسله، فأتيت عبيدة فقال: انت علقمة فسله، فقلت: علقمة أرسلنى إليك، فقال: انت مسروقاً فسله، فأتيت مسروقاً فسألته، فقال: انت علقمة فسله، فقلت: علقمة أرسلني إلى عبيدة، وعبيدة أرسلني إليك، قال: فأت عبد الرحمن بن أبي ليلى، فأتيت عبد الرحمن بن أبي ليلى فسألته فكرهه، ثم رجعت إلى علقمة فأخبرته، قال: كان يقال: أجرأ القوم على الفتيا أدناهم علما. وذكر النووي عن ابن مسعود وابن عباس قالا: من أفتى عن كلّ ما يُسأل فهو مجنون. وعن الشعبي والحسن وأبي الحصين قالوا: إن أحدكم ليفتي في المسألة، ولو وردت على عمر بن الخطاب لجمع لها أهل بدر. وعن سفيان بن عيينة وسحنون: أجسر الناس على الفتيا أقلهم علما. وعن الشافعي أنه قد سئل عن مسألة فلم يجب، فقيل له، فقال: حتى أدري أن الفضل في السكوت أو الجواب! وقد عقد الإمام الدارمي باباً في مقدمة سننه وترجمه: باب من هاب الفتيا وكره التنطع والتبدع. وأخرج فيه عن زبيد، قال: ما سألت إبراهيم عن شيء قط إلا علمت أنه لو علم ما سألت عنه ما أجابني، وما استفتيت إبراهيم قط إلا حدثت نفسي أنه كاره. وكان زبيد يقول: إذا قال الرجل: هذا حلال وهذا حرام، قال الله له: أنت قلت هذا حلال وهذا حرام؟ وكان زبيد مؤذن مسجده، فكان يقول للصبيان: تعالوا صلوا أهب لكم جوزاً، فكانوا يصلون ثم يحيطون به، فقلت له في ذلك، فقال:
Fatwa and Its Gravity. I asked Alqamah a question, and he said: Go to Abidah and ask him. So I went to Abidah, and he said: Go to Alqamah. I said: Alqamah sent me to you. He said: Go to Masruq and ask him. So I went to Masruq and asked him, and he said: Go to Alqamah. I said: Alqamah sent me to Abidah, and Abidah sent me to you. He said: Then go to Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Layla. So I went to Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Layla and asked him, but he disliked it. Then I returned to Alqamah and informed him. He said: It used to be said: The most courageous of people in giving fatwa are the least knowledgeable among them. And al-Nawawi mentioned from Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn Abbas that they said: Whoever gives a fatwa on everything he is asked is insane. And from al-Sha'bi, al-Hasan, and Abu al-Husayn that they said: One of you gives a fatwa on a matter which, if it had been presented to Umar ibn al-Khattab, he would have gathered the people of Badr for it. And from Sufyan ibn Uyaynah and Sahnun: The most daring of people in giving fatwa are those with the least knowledge. And from al-Shafi'i that he was asked a question and did not answer, so it was said to him, and he said: Until I know whether the virtue is in remaining silent or answering. And al-Darimi devoted a chapter in his Sunan and titled it: Chapter on those who fear fatwa and dislike exaggeration and innovation. And he narrated from Zubayd, who said: I never asked Ibrahim about anything except that I knew that if he knew what I was asking about, he would not have answered me, and I never consulted Ibrahim except that I told myself that he disliked it. And Zubayd used to say: When a man says 'this is halal' and 'this is haram', Allah says to him: Did you say this is halal and this is haram? And Zubayd was the muezzin of his mosque, and he used to say to the boys: Come pray, I will give you walnuts. So they would pray and then gather around him. I said to him about that, and he said:
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage is a collection of reports demonstrating the extreme caution exercised by early scholars regarding the issuance of fatwa. It begins with a story of Alqamah, who repeatedly directed a questioner to other scholars, showing reluctance to answer directly. The principle quoted is that the most fearless in giving fatwa are the least knowledgeable. Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn Abbas warn that anyone who answers every question is insane. The next report indicates that some questions are so weighty that even Umar ibn al-Khattab would have consulted the senior Companions. Sufyan and Sahnun reiterate the same idea. Imam al-Shafi'i's hesitation shows that a mufti must consider whether silence is more virtuous. Finally, al-Darimi's chapter title and the story of Zubayd illustrate the fear of speaking without certainty. The key lesson is that a mufti must recognize the gravity of his position and avoid hasty answers.

Key Terms
الفتوى (al-fatwa): Giving a non-binding legal ruling on a matter of Islamic law

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what did Alqamah say characterizes the people most daring in giving fatwa?
A) They are the most knowledgeable.
B) They are the least knowledgeable.
C) They are the most pious.
D) They are the most experienced.

Key Takeaway
A mufti must exhibit extreme caution, preferring silence over hasty answers, and recognize that ignorance leads to audacity in giving fatwa.

Adab al-Mufti — Ethics of the Mufti
beginner
6 min
The Gravity of Fatwa and Caution of Early Scholars
Anecdotes from early scholars on the gravity of fatwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key adab (etiquette) of a mufti regarding caution and humility as exemplified by early scholars, and apply this attitude to hypothetical fatwa scenarios.

Core Idea
Fatwa is a grave responsibility; the most knowledgeable scholars were the most hesitant to speak without certainty.

This lesson transports you into the cautious world of the early Muslim scholars, who treated every fatwa as a matter of life and death for the Hereafter. Through a series of powerful anecdotes, you will witness how giants like al-Sha'bi, Sa'id ibn Jubayr, and al-Qasim ibn Muhammad trembled at the thought of issuing a legal opinion without complete certainty. The lesson will help you internalize the principle that true knowledge breeds humility, not arrogance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key narrations
Read each narration carefully and note what each scholar did or said that demonstrates caution. For example, al-Sha'bi often said 'I do not know,' al-Qasim preferred losing his tongue over speaking without knowledge.
2
Synthesize the common theme
After listing the actions, identify the overarching principle: that fatwa carries immense responsibility, so the mufti must be extremely careful and willing to admit ignorance.
3
Apply to contemporary fatwa practice
Consider how a modern mufti can embody this caution. For instance, when asked about a ruling, he should research thoroughly, consult experts, and if uncertain, say 'I do not know' rather than risk error.
