مناهج الفتوى في السلف
قاضى القُضاة أيّامَ هارون الرشيد. وانتشر منها إلى معظم البلاد الإسلامية، وخاصةً في بلاد ماوراء النهر وتركيا والهند والسند. وأصبح هذا المذهب قانوناً رسمياً فى الخلافة العثمانية وما تحتها من البلاد. وانتشر مذهب المالكية فى بلادِ المغرب من الأندلس والجزائر ومراكش وتونس وغيرها. وانتشر مذهب الشافعية فى مصر والشام وماليزيا واندونيسيا وغيرها، كما انتشر مذهب الحنابلة فى مناطق من جزيرة العرب وغيرها.
مسئلة التقليد والتمذهب
كان الناس يستفتون العلماء منذ قديم فى المسائل التي يحتاجون إليها، لأنّ العامة من النّاس لا يستطيعون أن يستنبطوا الأحكام الشرعية من مآخذها الأصيلة، فلابد لهم من الرجوع إلى من عنده معرفة بهذه الأحكام، وهو الذى أمر به الله سبحانه وتعالى فى قوله الكريم: ﴿فَسْتَلُوا أَهْلَ الذِّكْرِ إِن كُنتُمْ لَا تَعْلَمُونَ) [النحل : ٤٣] ومادام المفتى موثوقاً بعلمه وتقواه، فلم يكونوا يُطالبونه بالدليل على ما يقول، وهو معنى التقليد في الاصطلاح، إذ عرفوه بالعمل بقول الغير من غير معرفة دليله أو مطالبته بالدليل. ولكن لم يكونوا في خير القرون يُقيَّدون أنفسهم بالاستفتاء من عالم واحد، بحيث لا يجوزون الاستفتاء من عالم آخر، وإن كان الأفراد لهم مناسبة خاصة بعالم من أهل بلده، فكانت ثقته عليه أكثر من غيره ، فيرجع بفضل تلك المناسبة والثقة إلى ذلك العالم في جميع مسائله أوفى معظمها. ومن ذلك ما أخرجه البخارى رحمه الله تعالى عن عكرمة أن أهل المدينة سألوا ابن عباس رضى الله تعالى عنهما هل يجوز للمرأة إذا حاضت أن تَنْفِرَ إلى وطنها بعد طواف الزيارة وتترك طواف الوداع، فأجابهم ابن عبّاس بأنه يجوز لها أن تَنْفِرَ وتترك طواف
الوداع. فقالوا له: "لا نأخذ بقولك، وندع قول زيد." وفي رواية للإسماعيلي: لا أُبالي أفتيتنا أو لم تُفتنا، زيد بن ثابت يقول: لا تنفر. وفي رواية للطيالسي "لا نتابعك يا ابن عباس وأنت تُخالف زيدا. " " وذلك لما كان لهم من زيادة الثقة على زيد بن ثابت رضى الله عنه. ثمّ إنّ زيد بن ثابت رضى الله تعالى عنه رجع عن قوله لما عرف حديث صفيّة رضى الله تعالى عنها، كما أخرجه مسلم عن طاوس: "كُنْتُ مَعَ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ إِذْ قَالَ لَهُ زَيْدُ بْنُ ثَابِتٍ: تُفْتِي أنْ تَصْدِرَ الْحَائِضِ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَكُوْنَ آخِرُ عَهْدِهَا بِالْبَيْتِ ؟ فَقَالَ ابْنُ عَبَّاس: إِمَّا لا، فَسَلْ فُلانَةَ الأَنْصَاريَّة (والظاهر أنّها أمُّ سُليم كما في رواية البخاري) هَلْ أَمَرَهَا النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ؟ قَالَ: فَرَجَعَ زَيْدُ بْنُ ثَابِتِ إِلَى ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ يَضْحَكُ وَهُوَ يَقُولُ: مَا أَرَاكَ إِلا قَدْ صَدَقْتَ " ولما رجع زيد بن ثابت رضى الله تعالى عنه اقتنع أهل المدينة بأنها يجوز لها أن تَنْفِر.
ومن ذلك ما أخرجه الإمام أحمد بن حنبل رحمه الله تعالى عن أبي مسلم الخولاني رحمه الله تعالى قال: "أتيتُ مسجد أهل دمشق، فإذا حلقة فيها كهول من أصحاب النبي صلى الله عليه وسلّم، (وفي رواية كثير بن هشام: فإذا فيه نحو ثلاثين كهلاً من أصحاب النبى صلى الله عليه وسلّم) وإذا شاب فيهم أكحل العينين، براق الثنايا، كلّما اختلفوا في شيء رَدّوه إلى الفتى
Methodologies of Fatwa among the Salaf
He was the chief judge during the days of Harun al-Rashid. And from it [the Hanafi madhhab] spread to most Islamic lands, especially in Transoxiana, Turkey, India, and Sindh. This madhhab became official law in the Ottoman Caliphate and the lands under it. The Maliki madhhab spread in the Maghreb lands from Andalusia, Algeria, Morocco, Tunisia, and others. The Shafi'i madhhab spread in Egypt, Syria, Malaysia, Indonesia, and others, just as the Hanbali madhhab spread in regions of the Arabian Peninsula and others.
The Issue of Taqlid and Adopting a Madhhab
People have been seeking fatwas from scholars since ancient times regarding the issues they need, because the common people cannot derive Islamic rulings from their original sources. So they must refer to one who has knowledge of these rulings, and that is what Allah the Exalted commanded in His noble verse: "So ask the people of remembrance if you do not know." [al-Nahl: 43] As long as the mufti is trustworthy in knowledge and piety, they would not demand proof from him for what he says, and that is the meaning of taqlid in terminology, as they defined it: acting on the saying of another without knowing his evidence or demanding proof. But they were not, in the best of generations, bound to seek fatwa from only one scholar, such that they would not permit seeking fatwa from another scholar, even though individuals might have a special connection with a scholar from their town, and their trust in him was greater than in others. So due to that connection and trust, they would refer to that scholar in all or most of their issues. Among that is what al-Bukhari narrated from 'Ikrimah: that the people of Madinah asked Ibn 'Abbas whether it is permissible for a woman, when she menstruates, to depart to her homeland after Tawaf al-Ziyarah and leave Tawaf al-Wada'. So Ibn 'Abbas answered them that it is permissible for her to depart and leave Tawaf al-Wada'. They said to him: "We will not take your saying and leave the saying of Zayd." In the narration of al-Isma'ili: "I do not care whether you give us a fatwa or not; Zayd ibn Thabit says: Do not depart." In the narration of al-Tayalisi: "We will not follow you, O Ibn 'Abbas, while you contradict Zayd." That was because they had increased trust in Zayd ibn Thabit. Then Zayd ibn Thabit retracted his saying when he learned the hadith of Safiyyah, as Muslim narrated from Tawus: "I was with Ibn 'Abbas when Zayd ibn Thabit said to him: 'Do you give a fatwa that a menstruating woman may depart before her last connection with the House?' Ibn 'Abbas said: 'If not, ask so-and-so al-Ansariyyah (apparently Umm Sulaym as in Bukhari's narration) whether the Prophet ordered her to do so.' He said: 'So Zayd ibn Thabit returned to Ibn 'Abbas laughing and saying: 'I think you have spoken the truth.'" When Zayd ibn Thabit retracted, the people of Madinah became convinced that it is permissible for her to depart.
And among that is what Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal narrated from Abu Muslim al-Khawlani: I came to the mosque of the people of Damascus, and there was a circle of elderly companions of the Prophet (peace be upon him) – and in the narration of Kathir ibn Hisham: there were about thirty elderly companions of the Prophet (peace be upon him) – and there was a young man among them with kohl-lined eyes, bright teeth; whenever they differed on something, they referred it to the young man.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage is a historical and methodological introduction to the practice of fatwa among the early generations (Salaf). The author begins by briefly describing the geographical spread of the four Sunni madhhabs, highlighting the Hanafi madhhab's adoption as official law in the Ottoman Empire. He then addresses the issue of taqlid and madhhab affiliation.

The author clarifies that taqlid, in its technical sense, means acting upon the statement of a qualified scholar without demanding the evidence for that statement. This practice is rooted in the Quranic command to 'ask the people of remembrance' (Surah al-Nahl: 43). The Salaf, however, did not obligate themselves to follow a single scholar exclusively. They would preferentially seek fatwa from a scholar they trusted, but they did not prohibit consulting others. To illustrate this, the author presents two key narrations:

First, the story of the people of Madinah consulting Ibn Abbas and Zayd ibn Thabit about a menstruating woman leaving after Tawaf al-Ziyarah without performing Tawaf al-Wada'. The people rejected Ibn Abbas's fatwa because they had greater trust in Zayd ibn Thabit. Later, when Zayd himself retracted his opinion after learning the hadith of Safiyyah, the people accepted the permissibility. This demonstrates that their following of Zayd was based on trust, not blind adherence; once the evidence was clarified, they accepted the correct position.

Second, the story of Abu Muslim al-Khawlani observing a gathering of elderly Companions in Damascus who referred their disputes to a young man, indicating that knowledge and competence determined whom they followed, not age or seniority.

The passage underscores that the early practice of fatwa was flexible and evidence-based, not rigidly bound to a single madhhab. This serves as a foundational lesson for muftis and seekers of knowledge about the proper attitude toward taqlid and following scholars.

Key Terms
التقليد (al-taqlid): Acting upon the saying of another (a qualified scholar) without knowing the evidence or demanding proof.
الاستفتاء (al-istifta'): Seeking a fatwa from a mufti regarding a legal issue.
المذهب (al-madhhab): The legal school of thought, such as Hanafi, Maliki, Shafi'i, and Hanbali.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What was the primary reason the people of Madinah rejected Ibn Abbas's fatwa regarding the menstruating woman?
A) They did not trust Ibn Abbas's knowledge.
B) They had greater trust in Zayd ibn Thabit's opinion.
C) They knew the hadith of Safiyyah already.
D) They were required to follow a single scholar.

Key Takeaway
Taqlid in the early generations was a flexible practice based on trust and openness to evidence, not rigid adherence to a single scholar.

Adab al-Mufti — Ethics of the Mufti

Salaf Practice in Seeking Fatwa: Thiqah Before Tadwin
Historical narratives of fatwa-seeking among Salaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the role of thiqah in fatwa-seeking among the Salaf and contrast pre-codification practices with modern madhhab adherence.

Core Idea
The Salaf followed trusted scholars, not schools; they could seek multiple opinions without fear of self-interest because rulings were unknown beforehand.

In this lesson, we examine two historical incidents from the Salaf that illuminate the early practice of seeking fatwa. The stories of Ibn Abbas and Zaid ibn Thabit, and of Mu'adh ibn Jabal, reveal that the principle of thiqah (trust) guided people to follow a particular scholar. Unlike later times, fatwa-seekers did not limit themselves to one madhhab because madhhabs were not yet codified. This lesson explores the implications of this historical context for the development of usul al-iftaa.

Guided Path
1
Recall the Ibn Abbas/Zaid Incident
Summarize the story: Ibn Abbas gave a ruling that a menstruating woman could depart without Tawaf al-Wada'. The people of Medina rejected it because they trusted Zaid ibn Thabit more. Later Zaid retracted upon learning a hadith.
This shows that laypeople followed the scholar they trusted most, even if it meant ignoring another.
2
Identify the Mu'adh ibn Jabal Incident
In Damascus, senior companions referred differences to the young Mu'adh ibn Jabal, showing that knowledge and trust, not age, determined authority.
Mu'adh was trusted despite his youth.
3
Extract the Criterion of Thiqah
The people of Medina said they had 'increased trust' in Zaid. Thiqah (trust) was the basis for preferring a mufti.
Thiqah encompasses both knowledge and piety.
4
Understand the Retraction Mechanism
Zaid retracted when the truth became clear via a hadith, indicating that truth overrides personal preference.
This reinforces that the goal is the correct ruling, not defending one's position.
5
Contrast Pre- and Post-Codification
Before tadwin, people sought fatwa from multiple scholars without fear of cherry-picking because they could not predict the answer. After tadwin, one could choose among known madhhab positions.
This historical context explains why later scholars emphasized following one madhhab.

(٤) مسند أحمد ٣٦:٣٩٩ رقم ٢٢٠٨٠ أصول الإفتاء مناهج الفتوى في السلف فتى شاب، قال: قلت لجليس لى مَن هذا؟ قال: هذا معاذ بن جبل!" وفي رواية أخرى: "إذا اختلفوا في شيئ أسندوه إليه وصَدَرُوا عن رأيه. (۱) ونظائر ذلك كثيرة. والحاصل أن كثيراً من العامة كانوا يرجعون إلى من يثقون به، ويُرجحون فتاواه على فتاوى غيره. وكان هناك من لا يقتصر على الاستفتاء من واحد لأن المذاهب لم تكن مدونة فى ذلك العصر، فماكانوا يرون محظوراً في أن يَسْتَفتُوا كل من تيسر لهم، وإن كان غير من يرجعون إليه عادة. ولم يكن هناك خوف من أن يَنْتَقِى الإنسان من المذاهب المختلفة ما وافق أهواءه، لأنه كان من العسير أن يعرف المستفتى قول من يستفتيه قبل أن يسأله، وذلك لعدم تدوين المذاهب.

They said to him: 'We do not take your saying and leave the saying of Zaid.' Then Zaid ibn Thabit, may Allah be pleased with him, retracted his statement when he learned the hadith of Safiyya, may Allah be pleased with her, as Muslim narrated from Tawus: 'I was with Ibn Abbas when Zaid ibn Thabit said to him: You give a fatwa that a menstruating woman should depart before her last visit to the House? Ibn Abbas said: If not, then ask such-and-such Ansari woman (apparently Umm Sulaym as in Bukhari's narration) whether the Prophet, peace be upon him, commanded her? He said: So Zaid ibn Thabit returned to Ibn Abbas laughing and saying: I think you have only spoken the truth.' And when Zaid ibn Thabit retracted, the people of Medina were convinced that it is permissible for her to depart. And among that is what Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal narrated from Abu Muslim al-Khawlani who said: 'I came to the mosque of the people of Damascus, and there was a circle of elders among the companions of the Prophet, peace be upon him, (and in a narration of Kathir ibn Hisham: there were about thirty elders of the companions) and among them was a young man with black-rimmed eyes and bright teeth; whenever they differed on something, they referred it to the young man.' I said to my companion: 'Who is this?' He said: 'This is Mu'adh ibn Jabal!' And in another narration: 'When they differed on something, they attributed it to him and followed his opinion.' And similar examples are many. The summary is that many of the common people used to turn to those they trusted and preferred their fatwas over others. And there were those who did not limit themselves to seeking fatwa from one person because the madhhabs were not codified in that era, so they did not see any prohibition in seeking fatwa from whoever was available, even if he was not the one they usually turned to. And there was no fear that a person would select from different madhhabs what agreed with his desires, because it was difficult for the seeker of fatwa to know the opinion of the one he was consulting before asking him, due to the lack of codification of madhhabs.

Commentary
This passage presents historical evidence from the Salaf regarding the practice of seeking fatwa. The author, Muhammad Taqi Usmani, narrates two key incidents. First, the story of Ibn Abbas and Zaid ibn Thabit concerning a menstruating woman leaving Mina before performing Tawaf al-Wada'. The people of Medina initially rejected Ibn Abbas’s fatwa because they had greater trust in Zaid ibn Thabit. However, when Zaid himself retracted upon learning a hadith, they accepted the ruling. This illustrates that the Salaf followed the scholar they trusted most, even if it meant rejecting another. Second, the story of Mu'adh ibn Jabal shows that even among senior companions, differences were referred to him despite his youth, indicating that trust and knowledge were the criteria. The author concludes that before the codification of madhhabs, people freely sought fatwa from multiple scholars without fear of cherry-picking rulings to suit their desires, because it was hard to predict a mufti's response. This historical context sets the stage for the later development of madhhab adherence.

Key Terms
الاستفتاء (al-istifta'): Seeking a fatwa or legal opinion from a mufti.
الثقة (al-thiqah): Trust in a scholar's knowledge and piety, leading to preference for his fatwa.
تدوين المذاهب (tadwin al-madhahib): The codification and systematic recording of the rulings of the four Sunni madhhabs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because they had greater trust in Zaid ibn Thabit
C) Because Ibn Abbas was too young
D) Because the hadith was weak

Key Takeaway
Before madhhabs were codified, fatwa-seeking was based on personal trust in a scholar, not adherence to a school.

The Prohibition of Talfiq and Necessity of Madhhab Adherence
Explaining the need for structured madhhab adherence and prohibition of arbitrary selection of rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify what constitutes talfiq, explain why it is prohibited in Hanafi fatwa methodology, and distinguish between legitimate tamadhhab and arbitrary intiqa'.

Core Idea
Talfiq disrupts the internal coherence of each madhhab and is prohibited because it leads to following desires, not evidence.

This passage from Usul al-Ifta' explains why a mufti and mustafti must adhere to a single madhhab. Through quotes from early authorities, you will understand the dangers of picking rulings arbitrarily and the benefits of systematic adherence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central rule
Read the passage and determine the primary ruling being discussed: the prohibition of talfiq and the necessity of tamadhhab.
The text opens by explaining that each madhhab is an interconnected system.
2
Understand the rationale
Analyze why talfiq is prohibited: because rulings within a madhhab are linked, and arbitrary selection disrupts the system and leads to chaos (fawdawiyyah).
The text says: 'فلو أخذ منه حكم وتُرك حكم آخر يرتبط به لاختل ذلك النظام'.
3
Examine the authoritative quotes
Review the statements from Ma'mar, Ibn Taymiyya, al-Nawawi, and Ibn Khaldun. Identify how each supports the prohibition.
Each scholar emphasizes that talfiq opens the door to following desires and undermines Sharia.
4
Apply the distinction
Distinguish between tamadhhab (committing to one madhhab with trust in its imam) and intiqa' (selecting based on desire). Note that tamadhhab brings order, while intiqa' leads to chaos.
Tamadhhab is not blind fanaticism but a practical necessity for the layperson.
5
Recognize the thamarah
Consider the practical consequence: without this rule, fatwa would be inconsistent and people would follow whims, dissolving the obligation of Sharia (inhilal rabiqat al-taklif).
Al-Nawawi explicitly mentions this danger.

أصول الإفتاء
مناهج الفتوى فى السلف

وبالتالي، فإن كل واحدٍ من هذه المذاهب له نظام خاص يعمل في إطاره، بحيث إن كثيراً من مسائله مرتبط بعضها ببعض. فلو أخذ منه حكم وتُرك حكم آخر يرتبط به لاختل ذلك النظام، وحدثت حالة من التلفيق لا يقول بصحتها أحد، ومن العسير للعامى أن يعرف هذه الدقائق، فلو فتح باب الانتقاء للعامة، لأدّى ذلك إلى فَوْضَويّةٍ فى أحكام الشريعة الغراء. ومن هنا دعت الحاجة إلى التمذهب بمذهب معيّن لا لأن صاحب مذهب معين يعتقد إمامه مطاعاً بنفسه، والعياذ بالله العظيم، بل لأنه يثق بعلمه بالشريعة وأدلتها أكثر من غيره، أو لأنّ معرفة مذهبه أيسر له بالنسبة إلى غيره من أصحاب المذاهب. وبهذا التمذهب انتظمت أوضاع الناس في الامتثال بالشريعة، دون اتباع الأهواء والعشوائية في ذلك، لأن الانتقاء من أقوال الفقهاء بالتشهى لا على أساس الدليل، ممّا ذمّه العلماء قديماً وحديثاً. قال الإمام مَعْمَر بن راشد رحمه الله تعالى: "لوأن رجلاً أخذ بقول أهل المدينة في استماع الغناء، وإتيانِ النّساء في أدبارهن، وبقول أهل مكة في المتعة والصرف، وبقول أهل الكوفة فى المسكر، كان شر عباد الله. (۱) وقال الحافظ ابن تيمية رحمه الله تعالى: "ونظير هذا أن يعتقد الرّجلُ ثبوت شُفعة الجوار إذا كان طالباً لها، وعدم ثبوتها إذا كان مشترياً، فإن هذا لا يجوز بالإجماع، وكذا من بنى على صحة ولاية الفاسق في حال نكاحه وبنى على فساد ولايته في حال طلاقه، لم يجز ذلك بإجماع المسلمين. ولو قال المستفتى المعين: أنا لم أكن أعرف ذلك، وأنا مِنَ اليوم التزم ذلك، لم يكن من ذلك، لأن ذلك يفتح باب التلاعب بالدين، وفتح الذريعة إلى أن يكون التحليل والتحريم بحسب الأهواء. (۱)
وقال الإمام النووي رحمه الله تعالى: "ووجهه أنه لو جاز اتباع أي مذهب شاء، لأفضى إلى أن يلتقط رُخص المذاهب متبعاً هواه، ويتخيّر بين التحليل والتحريم والوجوب والجواز، وذلك يؤدى إلى انحلال ربقة التكليف بخلاف العصر الأوّل، فإنّه لم تكن المذاهب الوافية بأحكام الحوادث مهذبةً وعُرفت. فعلى هذا يلزمه ان يجتهد في اختيار مذهب يُقلّده على التّعيين. وقال ابن خلدون رحمه الله تعالى: "ووقف التقليد في الأمصار عند هؤلاء الأربعة، ودرس المقلدون لمن سواهم. وسدّ النّاس باب الخلاف وطرقه لما كثر تشعب الاصطلاحات فى العلوم، ولمّا عاق عن الوصول إلى رتبة الاجتهاد، ولمّا خُشي من إسناد ذلك إلى غير أهله، ومن لا يُوثَق برأيه ولا بدینه فصرّحوا بالعجز والإعواز، وردّوا الناس إلى تقليد هؤلاء كل من اختص به من المقلدين. وحظروا أن يُتداول تقليدهم لما فيه من التلاعب. ولم يبق إلا نقل مذاهبهم. وعمل كلّ مقلد بمذهب من قلده منهم بعد تصحيح الأصول واتصال سندِها بالرواية. لا محصول اليوم للفقه غير هذا. ومدعى الاجتهاد لهذا العهد مردودٌ منكوص على عقبه مهجور تقليده. وقد صار أهل الإسلام اليوم على تقليد هؤلاء الأئمة الأربعة. (۳)
وقال الشيخ ولى الله الدهلوی رحمه الله تعالى: "إعلم أن النّاس كانوا في
Principles of Issuing Fatwas: Methodologies of Fatwa among the Early Muslims

Thus, each of these schools has its own system within which it operates, such that many of its issues are interconnected. If a ruling is taken from it and another ruling related to it is left, that system would be disrupted, resulting in a state of talfiq (patchwork) that no one deems valid. It is difficult for the layperson to know these subtleties. If the door of selection were opened for the common people, it would lead to chaos in the rulings of the noble Sharia. Hence arose the need to adhere to a specific madhhab — not because the follower of a particular madhhab believes his imam to be infallible in himself, God forbid, but because he trusts his knowledge of the Sharia and its evidences more than others, or because knowing his madhhab is easier for him than others. Through this adherence, people’s affairs in complying with the Sharia became orderly, without following whims and randomness, because selecting from jurists’ opinions based on desire rather than evidence is something scholars have condemned, past and present. Imam Ma'mar ibn Rashid (may Allah have mercy on him) said: “If a man were to take the opinion of the people of Madina regarding listening to singing and coming to women in their posteriors, and the opinion of the people of Makkah regarding mut'ah and currency exchange, and the opinion of the people of Kufa regarding intoxicants, he would be the worst of Allah’s servants.” (1) And Hafiz Ibn Taymiyyah (may Allah have mercy on him) said: “Analogous to this is a man who believes in the preemption of a neighbor when he is the claimant, but denies it when he is the buyer; this is impermissible by consensus. Similarly, if someone bases the validity of a sinful person’s guardianship during his marriage but invalidates it during his divorce, that is not permissible by consensus of Muslims. And if a particular seeker of a fatwa says, ‘I did not know that, and from today I abide by it,’ that would not be acceptable, because it opens the door to tampering with religion and opens the means for making things permissible or forbidden according to desires.” (1)

Imam al-Nawawi (may Allah have mercy on him) said: “The reason is that if it were permissible to follow any madhhab one wished, it would lead to picking the concessions of madhhabs following one’s desire, and choosing between permissibility and prohibition, obligation and permissibility, and that would lead to the dissolution of the bond of obligation, unlike the first era, for the comprehensive madhhabs covering the rulings of new incidents were not refined and known. So on this basis, it is necessary for him to strive to choose a madhhab to follow definitively.” And Ibn Khaldun (may Allah have mercy on him) said: “Taqlid (imitation) in the regions stopped at these four [imams], and those who imitated others ceased to study. People closed the door of differences and its ways because the terminologies in the sciences became highly branched, and because reaching the rank of ijtihad was hindered, and because they feared entrusting that to other than its people, and to one whose opinion and religion could not be trusted. So they declared incapability and unavailability, and directed people to imitate these [four], each follower to his specific imam. They forbade the circulation of their taqlid because it involves tampering. Nothing remains except transmitting their madhhabs. And every muqallid acts according to the madhhab of the one he imitates after verifying the principles and the continuity of their chain of transmission. Today, there is no benefit in fiqh other than this. And the one who claims ijtihad in this era is repudiated, turned back on his heels, and his taqlid is abandoned. The Muslims today have come to imitate these four imams.” (3)

And Shaykh Wali Allah al-Dihlawi (may Allah have mercy on him) said: “Know that people were in…

Commentary
This passage from Usul al-Ifta' establishes a fundamental rule of fatwa methodology: the prohibition of talfiq (arbitrary combining of rulings from different madhhabs) and the necessity of adhering to a specific madhhab. The text opens by explaining why each madhhab forms a coherent system—its rulings are interconnected. Taking only some and leaving related others disrupts this system, leading to invalid patchwork. The layperson cannot grasp these nuances, so if unrestricted selection were allowed, it would cause chaos. Thus, adherence to a single madhhab became necessary, not out of blind reverence for an imam but because the follower trusts the imam's knowledge or finds his method accessible. This system brings order and prevents following desires. The text then provides authoritative quotes: Ma'mar ibn Rashid condemns picking rulings across regions based on convenience. Ibn Taymiyya cites the example of inconsistent application of preemption and guardianship as impermissible; even if one claims ignorance and promises to mend his ways, it is unacceptable because it permits manipulation of religion. Al-Nawawi argues that allowing free choice among madhhabs leads to picking concessions according to whims, dissolving the obligation to obey Sharia, unlike the early era when comprehensive madhhabs were not yet refined. Therefore, one must commit to a specific madhhab. Ibn Khaldun affirms that taqlid has been confined to the four imams; the door of ijtihad is closed due to complexity and lack of qualified scholars. Only transmitting and following these madhhabs remains. The passage ends with the beginning of Wali Allah al-Dihlawi's statement, which likely continues on the next page. The rule is clear: a mufti and a mustafti must operate within a consistent madhhab framework; talfiq is prohibited as it undermines the integrity of Sharia.

Key Terms
التلفيق (al-talfiq): The act of combining rulings from different madhhabs arbitrarily, causing inconsistency and disruption within the legal system.
التمذهب (al-tamadhhab): Committing to follow a specific madhhab in all matters of fiqh, accepting its methodology and rulings.
الانتقاء (al-intiqa'): Selecting rulings from different scholars without a systematic basis, based on personal desire rather than evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is talfiq (arbitrarily combining rulings from different madhhabs) prohibited?
A) Because it is difficult for the layperson to know the different rulings
B) Because it leads to following one's desires and causes disorder in the application of Sharia
C) Because the scholars of the early centuries did not allow it
D) Because it is only permissible for those who have attained ijtihad

Key Takeaway
Talfiq is prohibited because it breaks the internal coherence of each madhhab and enables following desires; therefore, adherence to a single madhhab (tamadhhab) is necessary for orderly compliance with Sharia.

Adab al-Mufti — Ethics of the Mufti
intermediate
8 min
Adab When a Scholar's Opinion Contradicts a Hadith
Explaining Salaf methodology when a scholar's opinion contradicts hadith, and the etiquette of ikhtilaf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Salaf's methodology when encountering a contradiction between a scholar's opinion and a hadith, and articulate the proper adab (etiquette) towards scholars and muqallids in such situations.

Core Idea
Respect for scholars is mandatory even when their opinions contradict hadith; their error is excusable and every madhhab contains possibility of truth.

This passage from Muhammad Taqi Usmani's 'Usool al-Ifta wa Adabuhu' addresses a critical aspect of mufti adab: how to handle the discovery that a respected scholar's ruling contradicts a clear hadith. The author illustrates with examples from the Salaf and then draws principles for the muqallid and the one who abandons taqlid. The key lesson is that mutual respect and avoidance of insult are obligatory, even in disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key hadith examples
Read the two hadith stories: the first about the condemnation of those who prioritize scholars' rulings over Allah's book, and the second about Ibn Umar immediately accepting the hadith of the turtle. Note how the Salaf acted when evidence contradicted their opinion.
These examples establish the principle that a scholar must abandon his own view when a stronger proof is presented.
2
Extract the principle of immediate abandonment
From the examples, deduce that the Salaf would immediately abandon their opinion when informed of a contradictory hadith. There was no stubborn adherence to personal views.
This is the ideal: istidlal (derivation) must yield to nass (text).
3
Understand the caveat of respect
Despite the duty to follow the hadith, the passage emphasizes that it is forbidden to disrespect the scholar who held the opposing view. The author lists several valid excuses: the hadith may not have reached him, or it reached with a weak chain, or he interpreted it differently. Therefore, the scholar is excused.
Even the greatest companions like Umar (ra) missed some hadiths due to worldly occupations; this did not diminish their knowledge.
4
Apply the maxim of mutual possibility of truth
The author quotes the principle: 'Our madhhab is probably correct but may contain error; another madhhab is probably erroneous but may contain truth.' This removes the doubt about why one should follow only one madhhab if all might be right. It also forbids declaring others misguided or sinful.
This principle is foundational for maintaining unity and respect in ikhtilaf.
5
Recognize forbidden behaviors in disagreement
Identify the actions prohibited by the passage: backbiting, slander, jealousy, hatred, insulting (calling bid'ati or Wahhabi), and cursing. All these are absolutely haram, especially when they arise from ikhtilaf in fiqh.
The mufti and the student must avoid these at all costs, even if they believe the other is mistaken.

مناهج الفتوى في السلف

حدیث واقوال علماء میں آتی ہے، چنانچہ حدیث ہے۔۔۔ حضرت عدی بن حاتم سے روایت ہے کہ میں حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے حضور میں حاضر ہوا اور آپ کو یہ آیت پڑھتے سنا جسکا ترجمہ یہ ہے کہ ((اہل کتاب نے اپنے علماء اور درویشوں کو رب بنا رکھا تھا خدا کو چھوڑ کر اور ارشاد فرمایا کہ " وہ لوگ انکی عبادت نہ کرتے تھے ، لیکن وہ جس چیز کو حلال کہدیتے، وہ اسکو حلال سمجھنے لگتے ، اور جس چیز کو حرام کہہ دیتے، اسکو حرام سمجھنے لگتے" روایت کیا اسکو ترمذی نے۔ مطلب یہی ہے کہ اُن کے اقوال کو جو یقیناً انکے نزدیک بھی کتاب اللہ کے خلاف ہوتے ، مگر انکو کتاب اللہ پر ترجیح دیتے۔ سو اسکو آیت اور حدیث میں مذموم فرمایا گیا، اور تمام اکابر محقیقین کا یہی معمول رہا کہ جب انکو معلوم ہو گیا کہ یہ قول ہمارا یا کسی کا خلاف حکم خدا اور سول کے ہے فورا ترک کر دیا۔ چنانچہ حدیث میں ہے۔۔ نمیلہ انصاری سے روایت ہے کہ کسی نے ابن عمر سے کچھوے کے کھانے کو پوچھا، انہوں نے یہ آیت قل لا اجد الخ پڑھ دی (جس سے استنباط کرنا حکم حلت کا تھا) ایک معمر آدمی انکے پاس بیٹھے تھے، انہوں نے کہا کہ میں نے ابو ہریرہ سے سنا ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وآلہ وسلم کے سامنے کچھوے کا ذکر آیا، تو آپ نے یہ فرمایا کہ " منجملہ خبائث کے وہ بھی خبیث ہے"۔ ابن عمرؓ نے فرمایا کہ " اگر یہ بات رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وآلہ وسلم نے فرمائی ہے تو حکم یوں ہی ہے جس طرح حضور نے فرمایا۔" روایت کیا اسکو ابو داود نے۔ اور علماء حنفیہ بھی ہمیشہ اس عمل کے پابند رہے ۔ چناچہ جواب شبہ چہار دہم میں ان حضرات کا امام صاحب کے بعض اقوال کو ترک کر دینا مذکور ہو چکا ہے، جن سے منصف آدمی کے نزدیک ان حضرات پر تعصب و تقلید جامد کی اُس تہمت کا غلط ہونا متیقن ہو جاویگا جس کا منشا اکثر پر بلا درایت نظر کرنا ہے۔ اور مقصد سوم میں ایسی نظر کا غیر معتمد علیہ ہو نا ثابت کر دیا گیا ہے۔ لیکن اس مسئلے میں ترک تقلید کے ساتھ بھی کسی مجتہد کی شان میں گستاخی اربد زبانی کرنا، یا دل سے بد گمانی کرنا کہ انہوں نے اس حدیث کی مخالفت کی ہے ، جائز نہیں، کیونکہ ممکن ہے کہ انکو یہ حدیث نہ پہنچی ہو، یا بسندِ ضعیف پہنچی ہو ، یا اسکو کسی قرینہ شرعیہ سے ماڈل [؟] سمجھا ہو، اس لئے وہ معذور ہیں، اور حدیث نہ پہنچنے سے ان کے کمال علمی میں طعن کرنا بھی بد زبانی میں داخل ہے، کیونکہ بعض حدیثیں اکابر صحابہ کو جنکا کمال علمی مسلم ہے، کسی وقت تک نہ پہنچی تھیں، مگر انکے کمال علمی میں اسکو موجب نقص نہیں کہا گیا، چنانچہ حدیث میں ۔۔۔ عبید بن عمیر سے حضرت ابو موسیٰ کے حضرت عمر کے پاس آنے کی اجازت مانگنے کے قصّے میں روایت ہے کہ حضرت عمر نے فرمایا کہ " رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وآلہ وسلم کا یہ ارشاد مجھے مخفی رہ گیا، مجھے بازاروں میں جاکر سودا سلف کرنے نے مشغول کر دیا۔ " روایت کیا اسکو بخاری نے ۔۔۔اسی طرح مجتہد کے اُس مقلد کو جس کو اب تک اس شخص مذکور کی طرح اس مسئلے میں شرح صدر نہیں ہوا، اور اسکا اب تک یہی حسن ظن ہے کہ مجتہد کا قول خلاف حدیث نہیں ہے، اور اس گمان سے اب تک اس مسئلے میں تقلید کر رہا ہے ، اور حدیث کو رد نہیں کرتا ، لیکن وجہ موافقت کو مفضل سمجھتا بھی نہیں، تو ایسے مقلد کو بھی بوجہ اس کے کہ وہ بھی دلیل شرعی سے متمسک ہے، اور اتباع شرع ہی کا قصد کر رہا ہے ، بُرا کہنا جائز نہیں۔ اسی طرح اُس مقلد کو اجازت نہیں کہ ایسے شخص کو بُرا کہے کہ جس نے بعذرِ مذکور اس مسئلے میں تقلید ترک کردی ہے، کیونکہ اُن کا یہ اختلاف ایسا ہے جو سلف سے چلا آیا ہے، جس کے باب میں علماء نے فرمایا ہے کہ اپنا مذہب ظلنا صواب محتمل خطا، اور دوسرا مذہب ظناً خطا محتمل صواب ہے، جس سے یہ شبہ بھی دفع ہو جاتا ہے کہ جب سب حق ہیں ، تو ایک ہی پر عمل کیوں کیا جاوے؟ پس جب دوسرے میں بھی احتمال صواب ہے ، تو اس میں کسی کی تضلیل یا تفسیق یا بدعتی وہابی کا لقب دینا ، اور حسد و بغض و عناد و نزاع و غیبت و ست و سه ، وطعن ولعن کا شیوہ اختیار کرنا جو قطعاً حرام ہیں، کس طرح جائز ہوگا ؟
Methodology of fatwa among the Salaf. It is mentioned in hadith and sayings of scholars. The hadith from Adi ibn Hatim: I came to the Prophet (SAW) and heard him recite the verse: 'They took their rabbis and monks as lords besides Allah.' He said: 'They did not worship them, but they would declare something lawful and they would consider it lawful, and declare something unlawful and they would consider it unlawful.' Tirmidhi reported it. The meaning is that they gave priority to their sayings over the Book of Allah even when they knew it was contrary. So this was condemned in the verse and hadith. All great scholars would immediately abandon their own saying when they knew it contradicted the command of Allah and His Messenger. Another hadith: Numaylah al-Ansari reported that someone asked Ibn Umar about eating turtle. He recited the verse 'Say: I do not find...' (implying permissibility). An elderly man sitting with him said: I heard Abu Hurayrah say that the Prophet (SAW) mentioned turtle and said: 'It is from the impure things, so it is impure.' Ibn Umar said: 'If the Prophet (SAW) said so, then the ruling is as he said.' Abu Dawud reported it. Hanafi scholars always followed this practice. In the answer to the fourteenth doubt, it was mentioned that they abandoned some of Imam Abu Hanifah's sayings, proving that the accusation of rigid taqlid is false. But even with abandonment of taqlid, it is not permissible to disrespect a mujtahid or think ill of him that he opposed the hadith, because it is possible he did not receive the hadith, or received it with a weak chain, or interpreted it with a valid legal pretext. Hence he is excused. Insulting his knowledge due to not receiving the hadith is also insolence, because some hadiths did not reach great companions despite their established knowledge, but this was not considered a deficiency in their knowledge. Bukhari reported the hadith of Ubayd ibn Umayr about Abu Musa seeking permission from Umar, and Umar said: 'This saying of the Prophet (SAW) was hidden from me; my involvement in market transactions distracted me.' Similarly, a muqallid who has not yet been enlightened in this matter and believes that the mujtahid's saying is not contrary to the hadith, and continues to follow him, while not knowing the justification, should not be spoken ill of, because he too is adhering to a shariah evidence and intends to follow the shariah. Likewise, the muqallid is not permitted to speak ill of the one who abandoned taqlid due to the mentioned reason, because this difference has come from the Salaf. Scholars said: 'Our madhhab is probably correct but may contain error; another madhhab is probably erroneous but may contain truth.' This removes the doubt: if all are true, why follow only one? Since the other also has the possibility of truth, how can it be permissible to declare someone misguided or sinful, call them a bid'ati or Wahhabi, and adopt jealousy, hatred, enmity, dispute, backbiting, slander, insult, and cursing, which are absolutely forbidden?
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage discusses the methodology of fatwa among the Salaf, focusing on the proper attitude when a scholar's personal opinion contradicts a clear hadith. The author uses two hadith examples: first, the condemnation of those who prioritize scholars' rulings over Allah's book; second, the story of Ibn Umar immediately accepting the hadith of the turtle over his own interpretation. This shows that the Salaf would abandon their own views when presented with stronger evidence. Importantly, the author then emphasizes that even when one recognizes a contradiction, it is forbidden to disrespect the scholar who held the opposing view, because there may be valid reasons (hadith not reached him, weak chain, or different interpretation). He extends this to the muqallid who continues to follow the scholar out of good faith, and the one who abandons taqlid for the hadith; neither should be insulted. The underlying principle is that every madhhab has a possibility of truth and error, so mutual respect is obligatory. This passage serves as a guideline for muftis and laypeople on maintaining adab in ikhtilaf.

Key Terms
تقلید (taqlid): Following a qualified scholar's opinion without full knowledge of the evidence.
مقلد (muqallid): A person who practices taqlid of a particular madhhab.
مجتہد (mujtahid): A scholar qualified to derive rulings directly from the sources.
عدی بن حاتم (Adi ibn Hatim): A companion of the Prophet (SAW), narrator of the hadith about taking rabbis as lords.
خبائث (khaba'ith): Impure things; the hadith describes the turtle as being from the impure things.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary reason why it is forbidden to disrespect a mujtahid whose opinion contradicts a hadith?
A) The mujtahid is infallible.
B) The mujtahid may have a valid excuse, such as not receiving the hadith or having a different interpretation.
C) The hadith itself is not authentic.
D) The mujtahid's opinion is always correct despite the hadith.

Key Takeaway
Even when a scholar's opinion contradicts a clear hadith, following the hadith does not justify disrespect; every mujtahid is excused and each madhhab contains possibility of truth.

Choosing the Weaker Opinion to Avoid Fitna
Explains preferring weaker permissible opinion to avoid fitna

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle that a mufti may adopt a permissible weaker opinion to prevent discord, using prophetic and companion examples.

Core Idea
Avoiding fitna can override the preference for the stronger evidence when a weaker opinion remains permissible.

This lesson explores a key adab for muftis: when two valid opinions exist, prioritizing social harmony over the preponderant view. The Prophet's decision regarding the Ka'ba and Ibn Mas'ud's completion of prayers illustrate this principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two examples
Locate the two anecdotes in the passage: the Prophet's comment about rebuilding the Ka'ba and Ibn Mas'ud's action of praying four rak'at while traveling.
Each example shows a choice between a stronger and a weaker but permissible opinion.
2
State the preponderant and weaker opinions
For the Ka'ba: the preponderant (rajih) was to rebuild on Ibrahim's foundations; the weaker (marjuh) was to leave it as is. For Ibn Mas'ud: his preponderant view was qasr (shortening), but he prayed four (weaker).
Both weaker opinions were deemed permissible (ja'iz) by the actors.
3
Explain the reason for choosing the weaker
The Prophet feared fitna (disbelief) and confusion among new Muslims. Ibn Mas'ud avoided disagreement (khilaf) which he considered evil (sharr).
The motive was preventing social discord, not personal convenience.
4
Derive the general principle
If a weaker opinion is permissible, choosing it to avoid fitna is better than following the preponderant opinion. This is a guideline for muftis.
The principle is conditional: the weaker opinion must be valid (ja'iz), not prohibited.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مناهج الفتوى في السلف

فَقَالَ: "لَوْلا حِدثَانُ قَوْمِكِ بِالْكُفْرِ لَفَعَلْتُ " أخرجه الستة إلا أباداود. (۱) فبالرغم من أن بناء الكعبة على قواعد إبراهيم عليه السلام كان راجحاً، فإنّ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلّم اختار الجانب المرجوح خشية الفتنة والتشويش، لأن هذا الجانب المرجوح كان جائزاً شرعاً، وإن كان مرجوحاً... وكذلك عن ابن مسعود رضى الله تعالى عنه أنه صلى أربعاً، يعنى في السفر) فقيل له: عبت على عثمان، ثمّ صليت أربعاً؟ فقال: "الخلاف شر " أخرجه أبوداود).

فبالرغم من أن الراجح عند ابن مسعود رضى الله تعالى عنه كان هو القصر فى السفر، فإنّه أتم الصلوة تجنباً عن الخلاف والشر، والظاهر أنه كان يرى جواز ذلك أيضاً. فتأيّد بذلك ماذكرنا أنه إن كان الجانب المرجوح جائزاً، فاختياره أولى تجبُّباً عن الفتنة والتشويش.

(۱) صحيح البخاري، كتاب الحج، باب فضل مكة وبنيانها حديث ١٥٨٣ و صحیح مسلم کتاب الحج، باب نقض الكعبة وبنائها حديث ٣٢٤٢ وسنن الترمذي، كتاب الحج، باب ما جاء في كسر الكعبة حديث ۸۷۵ ولفظه لولا أن قومك حديث عهد بالجاهلية، لهدمت الكعبة وجعلت لها بابين." وسنن النسائي، كتاب مناسك الحج، باب(١٢٥) بناء الكعبة، حديث ۲۹۰۳، والموطأ للإمام مالك، كتاب الحج، باب ما جاء في بناء الكعبة، حديث ١٠٥٤.
(۲) سنن أبي داود، كتاب المناسك، باب الصلوة بمنى، حديث ١٩٦٠.
Methodologies of issuing fatwas among the Salaf: He (the Prophet) said: 'Were it not that your people are recent in disbelief, I would have done it.' Reported by the six except Abu Dawud. (1) Despite the fact that building the Ka'ba on the foundations of Ibrahim (peace be upon him) was more preponderant (rajih), the Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings be upon him) chose the weaker side (marjuh) for fear of tribulation and confusion, because this weaker side was legally permissible, even though it was weaker. Similarly, from Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) that he prayed four (i.e., while traveling). It was said to him: 'You criticized 'Uthman, yet you prayed four?' He said: 'Disagreement is evil.' Reported by Abu Dawud. So despite the fact that the preponderant view according to Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) was to shorten (qasr) during travel, he completed the prayer to avoid disagreement and evil, and it appears that he also considered that permissible. Thus this supports what we mentioned: if the weaker side is permissible, choosing it is better to avoid tribulation and confusion.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage presents a key principle of fatwa methodology: when two valid opinions exist, the mufti may choose the weaker but permissible opinion if it prevents fitna (discord) and tashweesh (confusion). The author supports this with two hadith examples. First, the Prophet (PBUH) did not rebuild the Ka'ba on the foundations of Ibrahim despite it being the preponderant (rajih) option, because the Quraysh were new to Islam and might be disturbed. Instead, he left the structure as it was, which was permissible (ja'iz). Second, Ibn Mas'ud, who held that shortening prayers during travel is stronger, prayed complete (4 rak'at) to avoid disagreement. Both examples illustrate that avoiding fitna can override the preference for the stronger opinion, as long as the weaker opinion is still legally valid. This is a practical guideline for muftis: prioritize unity and stability over strict adherence to the preponderant view when circumstances warrant.

Key Terms
الجانب المرجوح (al-janib al-marjuh): The weaker or less preponderant legal opinion that remains valid and permissible.
الفتنة (al-fitna): Discord, tribulation, or social unrest that could result from a ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did the Prophet (PBUH) not rebuild the Ka'ba on the foundations of Ibrahim, despite that being the preponderant option?
A) Because it was forbidden to change the Ka'ba.
B) Because the weaker opinion was easier to implement.
C) To avoid fitna since the Quraysh were new to Islam.
D) Because he did not have the authority.

Key Takeaway
A mufti should prioritize avoiding fitna by choosing a permissible weaker opinion over a stronger one when circumstances demand.

The Limits of Taqlid: When Clear Text Overrides Opinion
Establishes that taqlid is invalid when it contradicts a clear Quranic or Hadith text.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the boundary of permissible taqlid and apply the rule that clear textual evidence overrides qiyas-based opinions in a mufti's practice.

Core Idea
Taqlid is impermissible when it leads to abandoning an obligation or committing a prohibition against a clear, authentic hadith.

This lesson explores a foundational principle in mufti adab: the absolute priority of clear revelation over scholarly opinion derived from analogy. You will learn not only the rule itself but also how the Salaf and the Hanafi imams themselves exemplified this commitment. The lesson also addresses a common accusation against the Hanafi school and provides the necessary caution when setting aside a mujtahid's view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Trigger Condition
Read the opening sentence: the weaker side (opinion) must necessitate abandoning a wajib or committing a haram, and its only evidence is qiyas, while the preponderant side has a sahih, explicit hadith. This sets the condition for invalidating taqlid.
2
Extract the Dalil and Its Application
Locate the hadith of 'Adi ibn Hatim and the story of Ibn 'Umar. Understand how each illustrates the condemnation of blind following and the immediate submission to a hadith.
The Prophet interpreted 'taking rabbis as lords' as obeying them in making lawful/unlawful against God's law.
3
Analyze the Hanafi Defense
Note the author's rebuttal to the accusation of rigid taqlid: Hanafi scholars themselves abandoned the Imam's view in numerous cases. This demonstrates that the school is not blindly rigid.
This is a crucial point for understanding the internal flexibility of the Hanafi madhhab.
4
Apply the Caution on Adab
Read the final sentence: despite leaving the taqlid, one must not speak ill of or think badly of the mujtahid. Recognize that ijtihad requires deep knowledge and that a scholar may have reasons for his opinion.
This is a key adab for muftis and students.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما إن كان الجانب المرجوح لا يحتمل الجواز، بل يستوجب ترك واجب أو ارتکاب محظور، وليس له دليل سوى القياس، ويوجد حديث صحيح صريح في الجانب الراجح، فيجب العمل بالحديث من غير تردد ولا يجوز التقليد في هذه الحالة أصلاً، لأنّ أصل الدين هو القرآن الكريم والسنة، وليس المقصود من التقليد إلا العمل بهما بسهولة وسلامة. فلما انْتَفَت الموافقة بينهما، وجب العمل بالقرآن والسنة والجمود على التقليد في مثل هذه الحالة التقليدُ الّذى وَرَدَ ذَمُّه فى القرآن والسنّة وفى كلام العلماء. فروى عن عدى بن حاتم رضی الله تعالى عنه قَالَ: أَتَيْتُ النَّبيَّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَسَمِعْتُهُ يَقْرَأُ ﴿اتَّخَذُوا أَحْبَارَهُمْ وَرُهْبَتَهُمْ أَرْبَابًا مِّن دُونِ اللَّهِ﴾ [التوبة : ۳۱] قَالَ: إِنَّهُمْ لَمْ يَكُونُوا يَعْبُدُوتَهُمْ، وَلَكِنَّهُمْ كَانُوْا إِذَا أَحَلُوْا شَيْئاً اسْتَحَلُوْهُ، وَإِذَا حَرَّمُوا عَلَيْهِمْ شَيْئاً، حَرَّمُوهُ. أخرجه الترمذى )) ولم يزل عمل السلف والمحققين أنهم كلّما ظهر لهم أن قولهم أو قول غيرهم مخالف لأمر من الله تعالى أو من رسوله صلى الله عليه وسلّم، أقْلَعُوا عنه من ساعته. كماروى عن نُمَيْلة الأنصاري رضى الله عنه قال: سئل ابن عمر رضی الله تعالى عنهما عن أكل القنفذ، فتلا ﴿قُل لا أجِدُ فِي مَا أُوحِيَ إِلَى مُحَرَّمًا عَلَى طَاعِمٍ يَطْعَمُهُ﴾ [الأنعام : ١٤٥] الآية، فقال شيخ عنده: سمعت أبا هريرة يقول: ذُكِرَ القُنْفُذُ عند رسولِ الله صلى الله عليه وسلّم، فَقَالَ: خَبِيْنَةٌ مِنَ الْخَبَائِثِ، فَقَالَ ابنُ عُمَرَ: إِنْ كَانَ قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم - هَذَا فَهُوَ كَمَا قَالَ ما لم ندر. أخرجه أبو داود. (۲) ولم يزل العلماء الحنفية أيضاً ملتزمين بهذا الأصل، فإنّهم تركوا أقوال إمامهم في عدة مسائل، ويتبيّن بذلك لكل منصف أن ما اتهمهم به بعض الناس من التعصب والتقليد الجامد خطاً قطعاً، منشأه النظر في الروايات بغير دراية... ولكن لا يجوز مع ترك التقليد في تلك المسئلة الوقوع في شأن المجتهد بإطالة اللسان في جنابه أو إساءة الظن في القلب بأنه ترك الحديث الصحيح،

(۱) جامع الترمذي، كتاب التفسير، حديث ٣٠٩٥ (۲) سنن أبي داود، كتاب الأطعمة حديث ۳۷۹۹
As for the case where the weaker side does not permit permissibility, but rather necessitates abandoning an obligation or committing a prohibited act, and has no evidence except analogy (qiyas), while there is an authentic and explicit hadith on the preponderant side, then acting upon the hadith is obligatory without hesitation, and taqlid is absolutely not permissible in this situation, because the foundation of the religion is the Noble Quran and the Sunnah, and the purpose of taqlid is only to act upon them with ease and safety. So when congruence between them is absent, it becomes obligatory to act upon the Quran and Sunnah, and rigidity in taqlid in such a case is the taqlid that has been condemned in the Quran, the Sunnah, and the statements of scholars. It is narrated from 'Adi ibn Hatim (may Allah be pleased with him) who said: I came to the Prophet (peace be upon him) and heard him recite 'They took their rabbis and monks as lords besides Allah' (Quran 9:31). He said: 'They did not worship them, but when they permitted something, they took it as permissible, and when they forbade something to them, they took it as forbidden.' Reported by Tirmidhi. And the practice of the Salaf and the scholars of verification (muhaqqiqin) has always been that whenever it became clear to them that their own statement or the statement of others contradicted an order of Allah or His Messenger, they desisted from it immediately. Similarly, it is narrated from Numayla al-Ansari (may Allah be pleased with him) that Ibn 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with them) was asked about eating hedgehog, and he recited 'Say: I do not find in what has been revealed to me anything forbidden to eat...' (Quran 6:145). Then an old man with him said: I heard Abu Huraira say: The hedgehog was mentioned before the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), and he said: 'It is an impure thing from among the impure things.' So Ibn 'Umar said: 'If the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said this, then it is as he said as long as we do not know otherwise.' Reported by Abu Dawud. (2) And the Hanafi scholars have also always adhered to this principle, for they abandoned the statements of their Imam in several issues, and this makes clear to any fair-minded person that the accusation of bigotry and rigid taqlid leveled against them by some people is absolutely wrong, arising from looking at transmissions without insight. However, it is not permissible, when abandoning taqlid in that issue, to disparage the mujtahid by extending the tongue against him or thinking ill of him in the heart that he abandoned an authentic hadith.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage clarifies the boundary of permissible taqlid. When a weaker opinion relies only on qiyas (analogy) and contradicts a clear, authentic hadith, taqlid of that opinion is forbidden. The author then condemns blind rigidity (jumud) in taqlid, citing the famous hadith of 'Adi ibn Hatim where the Prophet interprets verse 9:31 as obeying scholars in making lawful/unlawful against divine commands. The story of Ibn 'Umar and the hedgehog demonstrates the Salaf's practice: when confronted with a hadith, they immediately abandoned their own opinion. The author notes that Hanafi scholars themselves left the Imam's view in many cases, refuting the charge of rigid adherence. However, an important caution follows: one should not disrespect the mujtahid or assume he ignored hadith, as ijtihad requires nuanced understanding. This passage is a classic Hanafi statement on the limits of taqlid, balancing adherence to the school with submission to textual evidence.

Key Terms
التقليد (al-taqlid): Following the opinion of a mujtahid without requiring evidence; condemned when it contradicts clear text.
الجمود على التقليد (al-jumud 'ala al-taqlid): Rigid adherence to taqlid even when clear evidence contradicts it; this is condemned.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling when a weaker opinion is based only on qiyas and contradicts an authentic hadith?
A) It is permissible to follow the weaker opinion to avoid discord.
B) Taqlid of the weaker opinion is not allowed; the hadith must be followed.
C) The weaker opinion takes precedence because it is from a mujtahid.
D) Both opinions can be followed as equally valid.

Key Takeaway
Taqlid of a qiyas-based opinion is invalid when it contradicts a clear, authentic hadith; the text must be followed unconditionally, but with proper adab toward the mujtahid.

Following Evidence: The Obligation to Abandon Taqlid When a Text Contradicts
Explains principle of abandoning opinions for Quran and Sunnah, and the proper respect for scholars.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the obligation of following Quran and Sunnah over human opinions, and identify the condemned form of taqlid described in the passage.

Core Idea
When clear evidence from Quran or Sunnah contradicts a scholar's opinion, it is obligatory to follow the evidence, not the scholar.

This passage from Mufti Taqi Usmani's Usul al-Ifta' establishes a foundational principle for fatwa-giving: the Quran and Sunnah are the ultimate authorities. It distinguishes between legitimate taqlid and the blind, rigid following that is condemned. Through examples from the Companions and later scholars, the author shows that true adherence to a madhhab requires abandoning it when evidence demands.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central ruling
What is obligatory according to the passage? (Acting by Quran and Sunnah)
2
Distinguish between types of taqlid
Which taqlid is condemned? (The blind, rigid taqlid that follows without considering evidence)
3
Examine the first example
What did 'Adi ibn Hatim's hadith teach about taking scholars as lords?
The Prophet explained that obeying scholars in making lawful/unlawful can amount to taking them as lords.
4
Examine the second example
How did Ibn Umar act when he heard a hadith about hedgehog? What does this show about following evidence?
Ibn Umar immediately accepted the hadith, showing that even a Companion deferred to prophetic teaching.
5
Apply to Hanafi school
How did Hanafi scholars themselves abandon statements of Abu Hanifa? What does this refute?
They left their Imam's statements in several issues, refuting the accusation of rigid taqlid.

وجب العمل بالقرآن والسنة والجمود على التقليد في مثل هذه الحالة التقليدُ الّذى وَرَدَ ذَمُّه فى القرآن والسنّة وفى كلام العلماء. فروى عن عدى بن حاتم رضی الله تعالى عنه قَالَ: أَتَيْتُ النَّبيَّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَسَمِعْتُهُ يَقْرَأُ اتَّخَذُوا أَحْبَارَهُمْ وَرُهْبَتَهُمْ أَرْبَابًا مِّن دُونِ اللَّهِ ﴾ [التوبة : ۳۱] قَالَ: إِنَّهُمْ لَمْ يَكُونُوا يَعْبُدُوتَهُمْ، وَلَكِنَّهُمْ كَانُوْا إِذَا أَحَلُوْا شَيْئاً اسْتَحَلُوْهُ، وَإِذَا حَرَّمُوا عَلَيْهِمْ شَيْئاً، حَرَّمُوهُ. أخرجه الترمذى)) ولم يزل عمل السلف والمحققين أنهم كلّما ظهر لهم أن قولهم أو قول غيرهم مخالف لأمر من الله تعالى أو من رسوله صلى الله عليه وسلّم، أقْلَعُوا عنه من ساعته. كماروى عن نُمَيْلة الأنصاري رضى الله عنه قال: سئل ابن عمر رضی الله تعالى عنهما عن أكل القنفذ، فتلا قُل لا أجِدُ فِي مَا أُوحِيَ إِلَى مُحَرَّمًا عَلَى طَاعِمٍ يَطْعَمُهُ ﴾ [الأنعام : ١٤٥] الآية، فقال شيخ عنده: سمعت أبا هريرة يقول: ذُكِرَ القُنْفُذُ عند رسولِ الله صلى الله عليه وسلّم، فَقَالَ: خَبِيْنَةٌ مِنَ الْخَبَائِثِ، فَقَالَ ابنُ عُمَرَ: إِنْ كَانَ قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم - هَذَا فَهُوَ كَمَا قَالَ ما لم ندر. أخرجه أبو داود. (۲) ولم يزل العلماء الحنفية أيضاً ملتزمين بهذا الأصل، فإنّهم تركوا أقوال إمامهم في عدة مسائل، ويتبيّن بذلك لكل منصف أن ما اتهمهم به بعض الناس من التعصب والتقليد الجامد خطاً قطعاً، منشأه النظر في الروايات بغير دراية... ولكن لا يجوز مع ترك التقليد في تلك المسئلة الوقوع في شأن المجتهد بإطالة اللسان في جنابه أو إساءة الظن في القلب بأنه ترك الحديث الصحيح،

لأنه من الممكن أن يكون ذلك الحديث لم يبلغه، أو بلغه بسند ضعيف، أو يكون ذلك الحديث مؤولاً عنده بقرينة شرعيّة، فإنّه معذور. وإن الطعن في كمال علمهم بعدم اطلاعهم على ذلك الحديث من جملة إطالة اللسان في جنابهم، فإنه قد ثبت أن بعض الأحاديث لم تبلغ بعض أكابر الصحابة الذين لا شبهة في كمال علمهم ، ولم يُعتبر ذلك نقصاً في كمالهم. فقد روى عن عبيد بن عمير رحمه الله تعالى في قصة استيذان أبي موسي رضي الله تعالي عنه قول عمر رضي الله تعالي عنه: "خَفيَ عَلَيَّ هَذَا مِنْ أَمْرِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلّم الهَانِي الصَّفَقُ بِالْأَسْوَاقِ " أخرجه البخاري". وكذلك إذا كان ، بعض المقلّدين لذلك المجتهد لم ينشرح صدره في تلك المسألة، وهو يحسب بحُسن الظَّنِّ بالمجتهد أنّ قولَه ليس مخالفاً للحديث ، فلا يزال يقلده في تلك المسألة بسبب هذا الظن، ولا يرد الحديث الصحيح، ولكن لا يفهم موافقة إمامه لذلك الحديث الصحيح تفصيلاً، فإنه لا يجوز ذم ذلك المقلّد، لأنه أيضاً متمسك بدليل شرعي، ولا يقصد إلا اتباع الشريعة، وكذلك لا يجوز لذلك المقلد أن يذمّ ذلك العالم الذي تَرَكَ التقليد في تلك المسألة بالعُذر المذكور، لأن اختلافهم هذا نظير الاختلاف الذي وقع بين السلف والذي قال فيه العلماء: "إنّ مذهبنا صواب ظنًا يحتمل الخطأ، ومذهب غيرنا خطاً ظنًا يحتمل الصواب " فلما كان الجانب الثاني محتملا للصواب أيضاً، فكيف يجوز بذلك تضليل أحدٍ أو تفسيقه أو رميه بالبدعة أو الوهابية
Methodologies of Fatwa Among the Early Generations

It is obligatory to act by the Quran and Sunnah. And rigid adherence to taqlid in such a situation is the taqlid that has been condemned in the Quran and Sunnah and in the statements of scholars. It is narrated from 'Adi ibn Hatim (may Allah be pleased with him) that he said: I came to the Prophet (peace be upon him) and heard him reciting: 'They have taken their rabbis and monks as lords besides Allah' [Quran 9:31]. He said: They did not worship them, but when they made something permissible they deemed it permissible, and when they forbade them something they forbade it. (Narrated by al-Tirmidhi). And the practice of the early generations and the verifying scholars continued that whenever it became clear to them that their own statement or that of someone else contradicted a command from Allah or His Messenger (peace be upon him), they would abandon it immediately. As narrated from Numaylah al-Ansari (may Allah be pleased with him) who said: Ibn 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with them both) was asked about eating hedgehog, so he recited 'Say: I do not find in what has been revealed to me anything forbidden for a consumer who consumes it' [Quran 6:145] until the end of the verse, and an old man present said: I heard Abu Hurayrah say: The hedgehog was mentioned in the presence of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), and he said: It is one of the evil things. So Ibn 'Umar said: If the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said that, then it is as he said, as far as we know. Narrated by Abu Dawud. And the Hanafi scholars also have remained committed to this principle, for they abandoned the statements of their Imam in several issues, and that makes clear to every fair-minded person that the accusation some people level against them of bigotry and rigid taqlid is definitely mistaken, its origin being looking at narrations without knowledge... But it is not permissible, when abandoning taqlid in that issue, to attack the mujtahid by extending the tongue against his dignity or to think ill of him in the heart by saying that he abandoned an authentic hadith.

Because it is possible that that hadith did not reach him, or reached him with a weak chain, or that hadith was interpreted by him with a legal contextual indicator, and he is excused. Attacking the completeness of their knowledge due to their lack of awareness of that hadith is part of extending the tongue against their dignity, for it is established that some hadiths did not reach some major Companions, about whom there is no doubt about the completeness of their knowledge, and that was not considered a deficiency in their perfection. It is narrated from 'Ubayd ibn 'Umayr (may Allah have mercy on him) in the story of the permission of Abu Musa (may Allah be pleased with him) that 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) said: 'This matter from the Prophet (peace be upon him) was hidden from me because the transactions in the market kept me busy.' Narrated by al-Bukhari. Similarly, if a follower of that mujtahid's school is not at ease in his heart regarding that issue, and he assumes based on good opinion of the mujtahid that his statement does not contradict the hadith, so he continues to follow him in that issue due to that assumption, and he does not reject the authentic hadith, but he does not understand in detail the conformity of his imam's statement to that authentic hadith, then it is not permissible to blame that follower, because he also holds on to a legal proof, and intends only to follow the Shariah. Similarly, that follower is not allowed to blame the scholar who abandoned taqlid in that issue for the mentioned excuse, because their difference is similar to the difference that occurred among the early generations, regarding which the scholars said: 'Our madhhab is correct with probability of error, and the madhhab of others is erroneous with probability of correctness.' Since the other side is also probable to be correct, how then can it be permissible to declare someone misguided or sinful or to accuse him of innovation or Wahhabism?
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage from Mufti Muhammad Taqi Usmani's 'Usul al-Ifta' discusses the correct methodology for giving fatwa and the proper etiquette towards scholars when abandoning taqlid. It begins by establishing that acting upon the Quran and Sunnah is obligatory, and the condemned taqlid is blind following that disregards clear texts. The practice of the salaf—the early generations of Muslims, including the Companions and the verifying scholars—was that whenever they discovered their own opinion or someone else's contradicted a clear command of Allah or His Messenger, they would immediately retract from it. An example is cited: when a hadith stating that hedgehog is impure reached Ibn Umar, who had initially relied on a general verse, he deferred to the hadith. The Hanafi scholars also adhered to this principle, abandoning the statements of Imam Abu Hanifa in several issues when contrary evidence appeared. This refutes the accusation of rigid taqlid leveled at them. However, the passage then draws a crucial distinction: abandoning taqlid in a specific issue does not permit disrespecting the mujtahid who held the differing opinion. The mujtahid may have been unaware of the hadith, considered its chain weak, or had a valid interpretation. Attacking his knowledge because he did not know a particular hadith is unjust, as even some major Companions were unaware of certain hadiths due to circumstances. Similarly, a lay follower who remains in taqlid due to a good assumption about his imam is excused, as long as he does not reject an established hadith. The passage concludes by applying a principle from the early scholars: each madhhab is considered correct in probability while allowing for error, so no one should be labeled misguided, sinful, innovative, or Wahhabi for following a valid method.

Key Terms
تقليد جامد (taqlīd jāmid): Blind, rigid adherence to a madhhab without considering evidence, which is condemned.
إطالة اللسان (iṭālat al-lisān): Disrespectful speech or slander against a scholar, particularly by accusing him of disregarding authentic hadith.
مذهبنا صواب يحتمل الخطأ (madhhabunā ṣawāb yaḥtamil al-khaṭa'): Our madhhab is correct but subject to error; others' madhhab is erroneous but subject to correctness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the correct attitude towards a mujtahid when we find his opinion contradicts an authentic hadith?
A) We must declare him misguided and reject all his teachings.
B) We should abandon his opinion in that issue but respect him, as he may have had a valid reason.
C) We must follow his opinion anyway to maintain unity.
D) We should only abandon his opinion if the majority of scholars agree.

Key Takeaway
It is obligatory to follow clear evidence from Quran and Sunnah over any human opinion, but doing so must be accompanied by respect for scholars.

Module 2 · Lesson 37

Adab al-Mufti — Ethics of the Mufti
intermediate
10 min
The Etiquette of Disagreeing with a Mujtahid: Respect and Good Assumption
Explains principle of abandoning opinions for Quran and Sunnah, and the proper respect for scholars.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why it is impermissible to disparage a mujtahid whose opinion is abandoned, and identify the valid excuses that excuse him.

Core Idea
When you abandon a scholar's opinion for a text, do not disrespect him; he may have been unaware, considered the chain weak, or had a valid interpretation.

The previous lesson established that we must follow evidence over opinions. But this does not give license to attack the scholar who held the contrary view. This lesson delves into the etiquette of disagreement, as taught by the passage: the mujtahid is excused, and even a lay follower who remains in taqlid due to a good assumption is not to be blamed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibition
What is not permissible when abandoning taqlid? (Attacking the mujtahid's dignity or thinking ill of him)
2
State the three excuses
What are the possibilities for why the mujtahid held a different view? (Hadith did not reach him, reached with weak chain, or he had a valid interpretation)
3
Support with example
How does the example of Umar not knowing a hadith support this? (Umar said it was hidden from him due to market preoccupation)
4
Analyze the lay follower's case
If a follower remains in taqlid due to good assumption, is he blameworthy? (No, because he holds on to a legal proof)
5
Apply the principle of mutual respect
How does the statement 'Our madhhab is correct with probability of error...' guide interaction between scholars and followers?
It fosters humility and prevents labeling others as misguided.

Source Text

مناهج الفتوى في السلف

وجب العمل بالقرآن والسنة والجمود على التقليد في مثل هذه الحالة التقليدُ الّذى وَرَدَ ذَمُّه فى القرآن والسنّة وفى كلام العلماء. فروى عن عدى بن حاتم رضی الله تعالى عنه قَالَ: أَتَيْتُ النَّبيَّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَسَمِعْتُهُ يَقْرَأُ اتَّخَذُوا أَحْبَارَهُمْ وَرُهْبَتَهُمْ أَرْبَابًا مِّن دُونِ اللَّهِ ﴾ [التوبة : ۳۱] قَالَ: إِنَّهُمْ لَمْ يَكُونُوا يَعْبُدُوتَهُمْ، وَلَكِنَّهُمْ كَانُوْا إِذَا أَحَلُوْا شَيْئاً اسْتَحَلُوْهُ، وَإِذَا حَرَّمُوا عَلَيْهِمْ شَيْئاً، حَرَّمُوهُ. أخرجه الترمذى)) ولم يزل عمل السلف والمحققين أنهم كلّما ظهر لهم أن قولهم أو قول غيرهم مخالف لأمر من الله تعالى أو من رسوله صلى الله عليه وسلّم، أقْلَعُوا عنه من ساعته. كماروى عن نُمَيْلة الأنصاري رضى الله عنه قال: سئل ابن عمر رضی الله تعالى عنهما عن أكل القنفذ، فتلا قُل لا أجِدُ فِي مَا أُوحِيَ إِلَى مُحَرَّمًا عَلَى طَاعِمٍ يَطْعَمُهُ ﴾ [الأنعام : ١٤٥] الآية، فقال شيخ عنده: سمعت أبا هريرة يقول: ذُكِرَ القُنْفُذُ عند رسولِ الله صلى الله عليه وسلّم، فَقَالَ: خَبِيْنَةٌ مِنَ الْخَبَائِثِ، فَقَالَ ابنُ عُمَرَ: إِنْ كَانَ قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم - هَذَا فَهُوَ كَمَا قَالَ ما لم ندر. أخرجه أبو داود. (۲) ولم يزل العلماء الحنفية أيضاً ملتزمين بهذا الأصل، فإنّهم تركوا أقوال إمامهم في عدة مسائل، ويتبيّن بذلك لكل منصف أن ما اتهمهم به بعض الناس من التعصب والتقليد الجامد خطاً قطعاً، منشأه النظر في الروايات بغير دراية... ولكن لا يجوز مع ترك التقليد في تلك المسئلة الوقوع في شأن المجتهد بإطالة اللسان في جنابه أو إساءة الظن في القلب بأنه ترك الحديث الصحيح،

لأنه من الممكن أن يكون ذلك الحديث لم يبلغه، أو بلغه بسند ضعيف، أو يكون ذلك الحديث مؤولاً عنده بقرينة شرعيّة، فإنّه معذور. وإن الطعن في كمال علمهم بعدم اطلاعهم على ذلك الحديث من جملة إطالة اللسان في جنابهم، فإنه قد ثبت أن بعض الأحاديث لم تبلغ بعض أكابر الصحابة الذين لا شبهة في كمال علمهم ، ولم يُعتبر ذلك نقصاً في كمالهم. فقد روى عن عبيد بن عمير رحمه الله تعالى في قصة استيذان أبي موسي رضي الله تعالي عنه قول عمر رضي الله تعالي عنه: "خَفيَ عَلَيَّ هَذَا مِنْ أَمْرِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلّم الهَانِي الصَّفَقُ بِالْأَسْوَاقِ " أخرجه البخاري". وكذلك إذا كان ، بعض المقلّدين لذلك المجتهد لم ينشرح صدره في تلك المسألة، وهو يحسب بحُسن الظَّنِّ بالمجتهد أنّ قولَه ليس مخالفاً للحديث ، فلا يزال يقلده في تلك المسألة بسبب هذا الظن، ولا يرد الحديث الصحيح، ولكن لا يفهم موافقة إمامه لذلك الحديث الصحيح تفصيلاً، فإنه لا يجوز ذم ذلك المقلّد، لأنه أيضاً متمسك بدليل شرعي، ولا يقصد إلا اتباع الشريعة، وكذلك لا يجوز لذلك المقلد أن يذمّ ذلك العالم الذي تَرَكَ التقليد في تلك المسألة بالعُذر المذكور، لأن اختلافهم هذا نظير الاختلاف الذي وقع بين السلف والذي قال فيه العلماء: "إنّ مذهبنا صواب ظنًا يحتمل الخطأ، ومذهب غيرنا خطاً ظنًا يحتمل الصواب " فلما كان الجانب الثاني محتملا للصواب أيضاً، فكيف يجوز بذلك تضليل أحدٍ أو تفسيقه أو رميه بالبدعة أو الوهابية
Methodologies of Fatwa Among the Early Generations

It is obligatory to act by the Quran and Sunnah. And rigid adherence to taqlid in such a situation is the taqlid that has been condemned in the Quran and Sunnah and in the statements of scholars. It is narrated from 'Adi ibn Hatim (may Allah be pleased with him) that he said: I came to the Prophet (peace be upon him) and heard him reciting: 'They have taken their rabbis and monks as lords besides Allah' [Quran 9:31]. He said: They did not worship them, but when they made something permissible they deemed it permissible, and when they forbade them something they forbade it. (Narrated by al-Tirmidhi). And the practice of the early generations and the verifying scholars continued that whenever it became clear to them that their own statement or that of someone else contradicted a command from Allah or His Messenger (peace be upon him), they would abandon it immediately. As narrated from Numaylah al-Ansari (may Allah be pleased with him) who said: Ibn 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with them both) was asked about eating hedgehog, so he recited 'Say: I do not find in what has been revealed to me anything forbidden for a consumer who consumes it' [Quran 6:145] until the end of the verse, and an old man present said: I heard Abu Hurayrah say: The hedgehog was mentioned in the presence of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), and he said: It is one of the evil things. So Ibn 'Umar said: If the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said that, then it is as he said, as far as we know. Narrated by Abu Dawud. And the Hanafi scholars also have remained committed to this principle, for they abandoned the statements of their Imam in several issues, and that makes clear to every fair-minded person that the accusation some people level against them of bigotry and rigid taqlid is definitely mistaken, its origin being looking at narrations without knowledge... But it is not permissible, when abandoning taqlid in that issue, to attack the mujtahid by extending the tongue against his dignity or to think ill of him in the heart by saying that he abandoned an authentic hadith.

Because it is possible that that hadith did not reach him, or reached him with a weak chain, or that hadith was interpreted by him with a legal contextual indicator, and he is excused. Attacking the completeness of their knowledge due to their lack of awareness of that hadith is part of extending the tongue against their dignity, for it is established that some hadiths did not reach some major Companions, about whom there is no doubt about the completeness of their knowledge, and that was not considered a deficiency in their perfection. It is narrated from 'Ubayd ibn 'Umayr (may Allah have mercy on him) in the story of the permission of Abu Musa (may Allah be pleased with him) that 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) said: 'This matter from the Prophet (peace be upon him) was hidden from me because the transactions in the market kept me busy.' Narrated by al-Bukhari. Similarly, if a follower of that mujtahid's school is not at ease in his heart regarding that issue, and he assumes based on good opinion of the mujtahid that his statement does not contradict the hadith, so he continues to follow him in that issue due to that assumption, and he does not reject the authentic hadith, but he does not understand in detail the conformity of his imam's statement to that authentic hadith, then it is not permissible to blame that follower, because he also holds on to a legal proof, and intends only to follow the Shariah. Since the other side is also probable to be correct, how then can it be permissible to declare someone misguided or sinful or to accuse him of innovation or Wahhabism?
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage from Mufti Muhammad Taqi Usmani's 'Usul al-Ifta' discusses the correct methodology for giving fatwa and the proper etiquette towards scholars when abandoning taqlid. It begins by establishing that acting upon the Quran and Sunnah is obligatory, and the condemned taqlid is blind following that disregards clear texts. The practice of the salaf—the early generations of Muslims, including the Companions and the verifying scholars—was that whenever they discovered their own opinion or someone else's contradicted a clear command of Allah or His Messenger, they would immediately retract from it. An example is cited: when a hadith stating that hedgehog is impure reached Ibn Umar, who had initially relied on a general verse, he deferred to the hadith. The Hanafi scholars also adhered to this principle, abandoning the statements of Imam Abu Hanifa in several issues when contrary evidence appeared. This refutes the accusation of rigid taqlid leveled at them. However, the passage then draws a crucial distinction: abandoning taqlid in a specific issue does not permit disrespecting the mujtahid who held the differing opinion. The mujtahid may have been unaware of the hadith, considered its chain weak, or had a valid interpretation. Attacking his knowledge because he did not know a particular hadith is unjust, as even some major Companions were unaware of certain hadiths due to circumstances. Similarly, a lay follower who remains in taqlid due to a good assumption about his imam is excused, as long as he does not reject an established hadith. The passage concludes by applying a principle from the early scholars: each madhhab is considered correct in probability while allowing for error, so no one should be labeled misguided, sinful, innovative, or Wahhabi for following a valid method.

Key Terms
تقليد جامد (taqlīd jāmid): Blind, rigid adherence to a madhhab without considering evidence, which is condemned.
إطالة اللسان (iṭālat al-lisān): Disrespectful speech or slander against a scholar, particularly by accusing him of disregarding authentic hadith.
مذهبنا صواب يحتمل الخطأ (madhhabunā ṣawāb yaḥtamil al-khaṭa'): Our madhhab is correct but subject to error; others' madhhab is erroneous but subject to correctness.

Adab al-Mufti — Ethics of the Mufti
