The Balanced Approach to Madhhab Differences and Taqlid
Mufti's adab: handling differences of opinion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qawida 'مذهبنا صواب ظنًا يحتمل الخطأ...' to determine when it is permissible to criticize or avoid a fellow Muslim over madhhab differences.

Core Idea
The famous qawida mandates mutual respect among madhhabs; only those who reject definitive texts or revile the Salaf are outside Ahl al-Sunnah.

The Salaf differed on many furuʿ issues, yet they maintained brotherhood. This lesson unpacks a key principle that governs the etiquette of disagreement: our madhhab is probably correct but could be wrong, and the other is probably wrong but could be correct. This insight protects us from extremism and teaches us to balance steadfastness with humility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize the given situation: a scholar or layperson differs from an authentic hadith. What possible excuses could he have? The passage lists three: the hadith did not reach him, it came with a weak chain, or he interpreted it differently.
2
Extract the Qawida
Capture the exact Arabic of the principle: مذهبنا صواب ظنًا يحتمل الخطأ، ومذهب غيرنا خطأ ظنًا يحتمل الصواب. Understand its meaning: it is a statement of epistemic humility.
This is the core of the lesson.
3
Apply the Qawida to Both Actors
Apply it to the lay follower who remains with his imam and to the scholar who leaves taqlid. Both are excused; neither should blame the other.
The qawida generates mutual respect.
4
Identify the Exceptions
Two types of people are exempted: those who reject definitive beliefs/rulings or revile the Salaf, and those who exaggerate in taqlid to reject Quran and hadith. These are to be avoided.
The qawida does not apply to fundamental deviations.
5
Define the Scope of Taqlid
Taqlid is only a means to follow Shariah for those unable to reconcile proofs. It is unnecessary in maʿlūm min al-dīn bi al-ḍarūrah (clear rulings like prayer, fasting, prohibition of wine).
This prevents absolute blind following.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مناهج الفتوى في السلف
لأنه من الممكن أن يكون ذلك الحديث لم يبلغه، أو بلغه بسند ضعيف، أو يكون ذلك الحديث مؤولاً عنده بقرينة شرعيّة، فإنّه معذور. وإن الطعن في كمال علمهم بعدم اطلاعهم على ذلك الحديث من جملة إطالة اللسان في جنابهم، فإنه قد ثبت أن بعض الأحاديث لم تبلغ بعض أكابر الصحابة الذين لا شبهة في كمال علمهم ، ولم يُعتبر ذلك نقصاً في كمالهم. فقد روى عن عبيد بن عمير رحمه الله تعالى في قصة استئذان أبي موسى رضي الله تعالى عنه قول عمر رضي الله تعالى عنه: "خفي علي هذا من أمر النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ألهاني الصفق بالأسواق " أخرجه البخاري". وكذلك إذا كان بعض المقلّدين لذلك المجتهد لم ينشرح صدره في تلك المسألة، وهو يحسب بحُسن الظَّنِّ بالمجتهد أنّ قولَه ليس مخالفاً للحديث ، فلا يزال يقلده في تلك المسألة بسبب هذا الظن، ولا يرد الحديث الصحيح، ولكن لا يفهم موافقة إمامه لذلك الحديث الصحيح تفصيلاً، فإنه لا يجوز ذم ذلك المقلّد، لأنه أيضاً متمسك بدليل شرعي، ولا يقصد إلا اتباع الشريعة، وكذلك لا يجوز لذلك المقلد أن يذمّ ذلك العالم الذي تَرَكَ التقليد في تلك المسألة بالعُذر المذكور، لأن اختلافهم هذا نظير الاختلاف الذي وقع بين السلف والذي قال فيه العلماء: "إنّ مذهبنا صواب ظنًا يحتمل الخطأ، ومذهب غيرنا خطأ ظنًا يحتمل الصواب " فلما كان الجانب الثاني محتملا للصواب أيضاً، فكيف يجوز بذلك تضليل أحدٍ أو تفسيقه أو رميه بالبدعة أو الوهابية، وإحداث الحسد والبغض والعناد والنزاع والغيبة والسب والشتم والطعن واللعن الذي هو حرام قطعاً. نعم! إن الرجل الذي يُخالف جمهور المسلمين في عقائدهم أو في المسائل المُجمع عليها، أو يُطيل لسانه في جناب السلف الصالحين، فإنّه خارج عن أهل السنة والجماعة، لأن أهل السنة والجماعة هم الذين يسلكون طريق الصحابة. وإنّ هذه الأمور مخالفة لعقائدهم، فكان هذا الرجل خارجاً عن أهل السنة وداخلاً في أهل البدع والأهواء. وكذلك الرجل الذي يغلو في تقليده بحيث يرد القرآن والحديث من أجله، فالواجب الاجتناب والاحتراز من هذين الرجلين مع الإعراض عن المجادلة المتعارفة، وهذا هو الحق الوسط. وأما ما عدا ذلك فغلط وشَطَط. اللهم أرنا الحق حقاً وارزقنا اتباعه وأرنا الباطل باطلاً وارزقنا اجتنابه.(١)
فتبيّن بهذا أن التمذهب بمذهب معين وتقليد مجتهد ليس إلا للوصول إلى ما ثبت من الأحكام الشرعية من الكتاب والسنة ممن لا يستطيع أن يوافق الأدلة المتعارضة. ولذلك صرّح العلماء بأن التقليد لا حاجة إليه في العقائد والأحكام المنصوصة قطعاً، مثل فرضيّة الصلوة والصوم والزكوة والحج، وحرمة الخمر والخنزير والربوا والكذب والخديعة والخيانة، من الأحكام التي لا مجال فيها للاجتهاد، ولا تحتمل فيه النصوص أكثر من معنى(٢)
وكذلك ليس معنى التمذهب أن لا يخالف علماء ذلك المذهب قول إمامهم
(١) الاقتصاد في التقليد والاجتهاد للشيخ أشرف على التهانوي رحمه الله تعالى
(٢) راجع الذخيرة للقرافي ١:١٤٨
Methodologies of Fatwa among the Salaf: Because it is possible that the hadith did not reach him, or reached him with a weak chain, or that he interpreted it based on a legal contextual indicator; so he is excused. And criticizing the completeness of their knowledge due to their unawareness of that hadith is part of extending the tongue against them, for it is established that some hadiths did not reach some senior Companions, whose completeness of knowledge is unquestioned, and that was not considered a deficiency in their completeness. For it is narrated from Ubayd ibn Umayr, may Allah have mercy on him, in the story of Abu Musa's seeking permission, the statement of Umar, may Allah be pleased with him: 'This was hidden from me from the matter of the Prophet ﷺ; the buying and selling in the markets distracted me.' (Bukhari). Similarly, if a follower of that mujtahid is not at ease in that issue, and he assumes, by good opinion of the mujtahid, that his statement is not contrary to the hadith, so he continues to follow him in that issue due to this assumption, and he does not reject the authentic hadith, but he does not understand in detail the conformity of his imam to that authentic hadith, then it is not permissible to blame that follower, because he too is holding to a legal proof, and intends only to follow the Shariah. Likewise, it is not permissible for that follower to blame that scholar who abandoned taqlid in that issue for the mentioned excuse, because their difference is similar to the difference that occurred among the Salaf, wherein the scholars said: 'Our madhhab is correct in supposition, with the probability of error; and the madhhab of another is wrong in supposition, with the probability of correctness.' Since the second side is also probable for correctness, how then is it permissible to declare someone misguided, or sinful, or to brand him with innovation or Wahhabism, and to create envy, hatred, enmity, dispute, backbiting, abuse, insult, accusation, and cursing, which is absolutely forbidden? Yes! The man who opposes the majority of Muslims in their beliefs or in matters agreed upon, or extends his tongue against the esteemed Salaf, then he is outside Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah, because Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah are those who tread the path of the Companions. These matters contradict their beliefs, so this man is outside Ahl al-Sunnah and among the people of innovation and desires. Likewise, the man who exaggerates in his taqlid to the point that he rejects the Quran and hadith for his imam's sake, then it is obligatory to avoid and be cautious of these two men, while refraining from typical argumentation. This is the balanced truth. And whatever is besides that is error and excess. O Allah, show us the truth as truth and grant us its following, and show us falsehood as falsehood and grant us its avoidance. (1) Thus it becomes clear that adopting a specific madhhab and taqlid of a mujtahid is only to reach the established legal rulings from the Quran and Sunnah for one who cannot reconcile conflicting proofs. Therefore, the scholars explicitly stated that taqlid is unnecessary in beliefs and rulings that are categorically established, such as the obligation of prayer, fasting, zakat, and hajj, and the prohibition of wine, pork, usury, lies, deception, and betrayal, from the rulings that have no room for ijtihad, and the texts bear no more than one meaning. (2) Also, the meaning of tamadhhab is not that the scholars of that madhhab cannot oppose their imam's statement. (1) Al-Iqtisad fi al-Taqlid wa al-Ijtihad by Sheikh Ashraf Ali al-Tahanawi, may Allah have mercy on him. (2) Refer to Al-Dhakhirah by al-Qarafi, 1:148.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage is from a work on Usul al-Iftaa and discusses the proper methodology of issuing fatwas among the Salaf. The author, Mufti Muhammad Taqi Uthmani, begins by excusing a scholar who does not act upon a hadith for valid reasons: it may not have reached him, it reached him through a weak chain, or he interpreted it in light of other legal evidence. Criticizing such scholars is unjust, as even senior companions like Umar ibn al-Khattab (ra) were unaware of certain hadiths due to being occupied with worldly matters. The author then extends this to lay followers who, due to good opinion of their imam, do not leave his madhhab even if they do not see the hadith. They are excused as well. The famous principle 'Our madhhab is correct with the possibility of error; the madhhab of another is wrong with the possibility of correctness' is invoked. This principle demands mutual respect and forbids declaring others misguided or sinful. However, the passage makes an exception for two types of people: those who oppose the majority in matters of belief or consensus, or who revile the Salaf; and those who blindly follow their madhhab to the extent of rejecting Quran and Hadith. These are to be avoided. The conclusion explains that taqlid is a means for laypeople to follow the Shariah; it is not needed in clear, definitive rulings like the obligations of prayer or prohibitions of alcohol. The passage provides a balanced, middle path for dealing with differences among Muslims.

Key Terms
التقليد (al-taqlid): Following a qualified mujtahid in his legal rulings without independent investigation of the evidence
التمذهب (al-tamadhhab): Adopting a specific madhhab (e.g., Hanafi) as one's school of thought and practice
السلف (al-salaf): The early righteous generations: Companions, Followers, and the early imams
الاجتهاد لا ينقض بالاجتهاد (al-ijtihad la yunqad bi al-ijtihad): A ruling based on ijtihad is not overturned by another ijtihad

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT permissible?
A) Criticizing a scholar who leaves taqlid for a hadith
B) A layperson adhering to his imam's opinion even if he does not know the hadith
C) Avoiding a person who rejects Quran and hadith for his imam's sake
D) Treating the madhhab of another as possibly correct

Key Takeaway
Respectful disagreement is required; only deviation in fundamentals necessitates avoidance.

The Middle Path in Taqlid and Madhhab Adherence
A call to avoid extremism in religious adherence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two forms of extremism in taqlid and state the Hanafi middle path.

Core Idea
The middle path avoids both opposing the Salaf and blindly following a madhhab against clear evidence.

This passage from Usool al-Iftaa addresses a critical issue for every mufti: how to navigate taqlid without falling into extremes. The author first condemns the social harms of partisan disputes, then pinpoints two dangerous groups: those who reject the Salaf and those whose fanatical taqlid leads them to disregard the Quran and Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two extremes
Read the passage and name the two types of people the author warns against. One opposes the majority and the Salaf; the other's taqlid is so extreme that he rejects clear revelation.
The first is outside Ahl al-Sunnah, the second is also to be avoided.
2
Understand Ahl al-Sunnah definition
The author defines Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah as those who follow the path of the Companions. Why is this definition important for the middle path?
It grounds the middle path in the Salaf's methodology.
3
Recognize the middle path prescription
State the author's recommended response: avoid both extremist men, turn away from heated argument, and seek the truth with good manners.
The author calls this 'the middle truth' (al-haqq al-wasat).
4
Connect to mufti conduct
How does this lesson apply to a mufti today? The mufti must avoid partisanship, respect scholarly authority without blind following, and prioritize the Quran and Sunnah.
This is a core adab for fatwa issuance.

وإحداث الحسد والبغض والعناد والنزاع والغيبة والسب والشتم والطعن واللعن الذي هو حرام قطعاً. نعم! إن الرجل الذي يُخالف جمهور المسلمين في عقائدهم أو في المسائل المُجمع عليها، أو يُطيل لسانه في جناب السلف الصالحين، فإنّه خارج عن أهل السنة والجماعة، لأن أهل السنة والجماعة هم الذين يسلكون طريق الصحابة. وإنّ هذه الأمور مخالفة لعقائدهم، فكان هذا الرجل خارجاً عن أهل السنة وداخلاً في أهل البدع والأهواء. وكذلك الرجل الذي يغلو في تقليده بحيث يرد القرآن والحديث من أجله، فالواجب الاجتناب والاحتراز من هذين الرجلين مع الإعراض عن المجادلة المتعارفة، وهذا هو الحق الوسط. وأما ما عدا ذلك فغلط وشَطَط. اللهم أرنا
الحق حقاً وارزقنا اتباعه وأرنا الباطل باطلاً وارزقنا اجتنابه. (۱)
فتبيّن بهذا أن التمذهب بمذهب معين وتقليد مجتهد ليس إلا للوصول إلى ماثبت من الأحكام الشرعية من الكتاب والسنة ممن لا يستطيع أن يوافق الأدلة المتعارضة. ولذلك صرّح العلماء بأن التقليد لاحاجة إليه في العقائد والأحكام المنصوصة قطعاً، مثل فرضيّة الصلوة والصوم والزكوة والحج، وحرمة الخمر والخنزير والربوا والكذب والخديعة والخيانة، من الأحكام التي لا مجال فيها للاجتهاد، ولا تحتمل فيه النصوص أكثر من معنى (٢). وكذلك ليس معنى التمذهب أن لا يخالف علماء ذلك المذهب قول إمامهم في شيئ من المسائل. ومنه ماروى عن الإمام الطحاوى، وهو حنفى المذهب، أنّه قال: "كان أبو عبيد ابن حَربَوَيْهِ (۳) يُذاكرنى بالمسائل. فأجبته يوماً في مسئلة، فقال لي: "ماهذا قول أبي حنيفة." فقلت له: "أيّها القاضي أو كلّما قاله أبو حنيفة أقول به؟" قال: "ماظننتك إلا مقلّداً." فقلت له: "وهل يُقلّد إلا عصبي؟" فقال لى: "أوغبى" فطارت هذه الكلمة بمصر، حتى صارت مثلاً " وما قصده الطحاوى رحمه الله تعالى هو أن التمذهب بمذهب معين لا ينافى أن لا يأخذ عالم مثل الطحاوى بقول غير قول إمامه في شيئ من المسائل، والأصار تعصباً. (۱) الاقتصاد في التقليد والاجتهاد للشيخ أشرف على التهانوي رحمه الله تعالى (۲) راجع الذخيرة للقرافي ١:١٤٨ (۳) هو أحمد محمد سلامة أبو جعفر الطحاوى بفتح الطاء والحاء، نسبة إلى طحية، قرية بصعيد مصر الأزدى. إمام جليل القدر، مشهور في الآفاق. انتهت إليه رئاسة الحنفية بمصر. كان يقرأ على خاله الإمام المزني الشافعي، فانتقل من مذهبه وتفقه على مذهب الإمام أبي حنيفة وذكر أبو يعلى الخليلى فى كتاب الإرشاد في ترجمة المزنى أن محمد بن أحمد الشروطي قال للطحاوي: لم خالفت مذهب خالك ، فقال لأنى كنت أرى خالى يديم النظر في كتب أبي حنيفة. أخذ الفقه عن أبي جعفر أحمد، ثم خرج إلى الشام فلقي بها أبا خازم عبد الحميد، قاضي القضاة بالشام، فأخذ عنه عن عيسى ابن أبان عن الإمام محمد رحمهم الله تعالى. كان إماما في الأحاديث والأخبار، وله تصانيف جليلة معتبرة منها معانى الآثار وقد يسمّى بشرح معاني الآثار، ومشكل الآثار، وأحكام القرآن والمختصر فى الفقه وشرح الجامع الصغير وشرح الجامع الكبير وغيرها. توفی رحمه الله تعالى سنة ٣٢١ هـ. (ملخص من الفوائد البهية ص ٣١ إلى (٣٤) (۲) القاضي أبو عبيد ابن حَرْبَوَيْه القاضي العلامة المحدّث الثبت قاضي القضاة، أبو عبيد، علي بن الحسين بن حرب بن عيسى البغدادي الشافعي ولي قضاء مصر، قال الإمام قال الإمام محيي الدين النووي: أصحاب الوجوه، تكرّر ذكره في " المهذب " و " الروضة ". توفي في صفر سنة ٣١٩ كان من، وصلّى عليه أبو سعيد الاصطخري، رحمهم الله تعالى أجمعين. (۳) ذكره الحافظ ابن حجر رحمه الله تعالى فى رفع الإصر عن قضاة مصر، في ذكر أبي عبيد على بن حسين بن حربویه ١:١٢٠
Methods of issuing fatwas among the Salaf: and the creation of envy, hatred, obstinacy, conflict, backbiting, cursing, insulting, slandering, and damning, which is absolutely forbidden. Yes! The man who opposes the majority of Muslims in their beliefs or in matters of consensus, or who extends his tongue against the noble Salaf, then he is outside Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah, because Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah are those who follow the path of the Companions. And these matters contradict their beliefs, so this man is outside Ahl al-Sunnah and inside the people of innovation and desires. Likewise, the man who goes to excess in his taqlid such that he rejects the Qur'an and Hadith for its sake, then it is obligatory to avoid and be cautious of both these men, while turning away from customary argumentation. This is the middle truth. As for anything besides that, it is error and extremism. O Allah, show us the truth as truth and grant us its followers, and show us falsehood as falsehood and grant us its avoidance. (1) So it becomes clear that adhering to a specific madhhab and following a mujtahid is only for reaching the established shari'ah rulings from the Book and Sunnah for one who cannot reconcile the conflicting evidences. Therefore the scholars have stated that taqlid is not needed in matters of creed and rulings that are textually definitive, such as the obligatory nature of prayer, fasting, zakat, and Hajj, and the prohibition of wine, pork, usury, lying, deception, and betrayal, among the rulings that have no room for ijtihad, and the texts do not allow more than one meaning (2). Also, the meaning of taqlid is not that the scholars of that madhhab never contradict the statement of their Imam in any matter. Among that is what is narrated from Imam al-Tahawi, who was Hanafi, that he said: 'Abu Ubayd ibn Harbawayh (3) would discuss issues with me. One day I answered him on a issue, and he said to me: 'This is not the statement of Abu Hanifah.' I said to him: 'O judge! Am I to say everything that Abu Hanifah said?' He said: 'I thought you were a muqallid.' I said to him: 'Does a muqallid follow except out of partisanship?' He said to me: 'Stupid!' And this word spread in Egypt until it became a proverb.' What al-Tahawi intended is that adherence to a specific madhhab does not prevent a scholar like al-Tahawi from not accepting the statement of his Imam in some issues, out of partisanship. (1) Al-Iqtisad fi al-Taqleed wa al-Ijtihad by al-Shaykh Ashraf Ali al-Tahanawi rahimahullah ta'ala. (2) See al-Dhakhirah by al-Qarafi 1:148. (3) He is Ahmad Muhammad Salamah Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi [biographical details].
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage from 'Usool al-Iftaa' by Mufti Muhammad Taqi Usmani discusses the proper methodology for issuing fatwas, emphasizing the middle path between two extremes: blind fanaticism and reckless rejection of scholarly authority. The author first warns against the social harms caused by partisan disputes, such as envy and hatred, which are clearly forbidden. Then he identifies two types of people who must be avoided: (1) those who oppose the beliefs of the Muslim majority or attack the Salaf, thereby leaving Ahl al-Sunnah, and (2) those who are so extreme in their taqlid that they reject clear Quranic and Hadith evidence. The correct approach is to avoid both extremes and instead engage in dialogue with good manners. The passage then clarifies the purpose of adopting a madhhab: it is a necessary tool for those who cannot directly derive rulings from the primary sources due to conflicting evidence. However, taqlid is not needed for definitive matters like the obligatory acts of worship or prohibitions of major sins, as these are clear in the texts. The anecdote about Imam al-Tahawi illustrates that even a staunch Hanafi may legitimately differ from Abu Hanifah in some questions; this does not negate his adherence to the madhhab unless done out of blind partisanship. Thus, true taqlid is a reasoned commitment to a methodological framework, not a rigid refusal to consider other valid opinions.

Key Terms
تقليد (taqlid): Following a mujtahid in his legal rulings without requiring the evidence, necessary for those who cannot perform ijtihad.
تمذهب (tamadhhub): Adherence to a specific madhhab (school of law) as a framework for deriving and applying rulings.
أهل السنة والجماعة (ahl al-sunnah wa al-jama'ah): The mainstream Sunni community that follows the path of the Companions in creed and practice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what should be done with the two types of extremist men?
A) Engage them in debate to convince them.
B) Avoid and be cautious of them, turning away from customary argumentation.
C) Declare them as disbelievers.
D) Follow them if they are from the same madhhab.

Key Takeaway
The middle path in taqlid is to follow a madhhab without rejecting clear evidence or opposing the Salaf.

Taqlid as a Tool: Purpose and Limits of Madhhab Adherence
Clarifying the role of taqlid and the scope of madhhab adherence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the purpose of taqlid and use Imam al-Tahawi's example to show that tamadhhub does not require agreement on every issue.

Core Idea
Taqlid is a necessity for non-mujtahids, but scholars may differ from their imam within the madhhab's methodology.

After establishing the middle path, the author delves into the philosophical underpinnings of taqlid and tamadhhub. He clarifies that taqlid is only needed for non-definitive matters and that even great Hanafi scholars like Imam al-Tahawi felt free to disagree with Abu Hanifah when evidence warranted.

Guided Path
1
Understand the purpose of taqlid
The author says taqlid and tamadhhub are only a means to reach the shari'ah rulings from the Book and Sunnah for those who cannot reconcile conflicting evidences. What does this imply about its necessity?
Taqlid is a tool, not an end in itself.
2
List definitive rulings not needing taqlid
Identify the examples given: fard of prayer, fasting, zakat, hajj; prohibition of wine, pork, usury, lying, etc. Why are these not subject to taqlid?
Because the texts are definitive and admit only one meaning.
3
Analyze the Tahawi anecdote
Read the story: Imam al-Tahawi was asked about a ruling, gave an answer not aligning with Abu Hanifah's known view, and when questioned, he asked if he must follow Abu Hanifah in everything. What does this prove?
It shows that a Hanafi scholar can differ from the imam without leaving the madhhab.
4
Derive the principle
What is the key takeaway? The author says al-Tahawi's point was that tamadhhub does not prevent a scholar from not taking his imam's view in some issues, as long as it's not out of partisanship.
The principle: adherence to a madhhab is methodological, not a rigid commitment to every view.
5
Distinguish legitimate difference from partisanship
How does the author differentiate between acceptable disagreement and blameworthy partisanship?
Disagreement based on evidence is fine; partisanship that rejects truth is condemned.

فتبيّن بهذا أن التمذهب بمذهب معين وتقليد مجتهد ليس إلا للوصول إلى ماثبت من الأحكام الشرعية من الكتاب والسنة ممن لا يستطيع أن يوافق الأدلة المتعارضة. ولذلك صرّح العلماء بأن التقليد لاحاجة إليه في العقائد والأحكام المنصوصة قطعاً، مثل فرضيّة الصلوة والصوم والزكوة والحج، وحرمة الخمر والخنزير والربوا والكذب والخديعة والخيانة، من الأحكام التي لا مجال فيها للاجتهاد، ولا تحتمل فيه النصوص أكثر من معنى (٢). وكذلك ليس معنى التمذهب أن لا يخالف علماء ذلك المذهب قول إمامهم في شيئ من المسائل. ومنه ماروى عن الإمام الطحاوى، وهو حنفى المذهب، أنّه قال: "كان أبو عبيد ابن حَربَوَيْهِ (۳) يُذاكرنى بالمسائل. فأجبته يوماً في مسئلة، فقال لي: "ماهذا قول أبي حنيفة." فقلت له: "أيّها القاضي أو كلّما قاله أبو حنيفة أقول به؟" قال: "ماظننتك إلا مقلّداً." فقلت له: "وهل يُقلّد إلا عصبي؟" فقال لى: "أوغبى" فطارت هذه الكلمة بمصر، حتى صارت مثلاً " وما قصده الطحاوى رحمه الله تعالى هو أن التمذهب بمذهب معين لا ينافى أن لا يأخذ عالم مثل الطحاوى بقول غير قول إمامه في شيئ من المسائل، والأصار تعصباً. (۱) الاقتصاد في التقليد والاجتهاد للشيخ أشرف على التهانوي رحمه الله تعالى (۲) راجع الذخيرة للقرافي ١:١٤٨ (۳) هو أحمد محمد سلامة أبو جعفر الطحاوى بفتح الطاء والحاء، نسبة إلى طحية، قرية بصعيد مصر الأزدى. إمام جليل القدر، مشهور في الآفاق. انتهت إليه رئاسة الحنفية بمصر. كان يقرأ على خاله الإمام المزني الشافعي، فانتقل من مذهبه وتفقه على مذهب الإمام أبي حنيفة وذكر أبو يعلى الخليلى فى كتاب الإرشاد في ترجمة المزنى أن محمد بن أحمد الشروطي قال للطحاوي: لم خالفت مذهب خالك ، فقال لأنى كنت أرى خالى يديم النظر في كتب أبي حنيفة. أخذ الفقه عن أبي جعفر أحمد، ثم خرج إلى الشام فلقي بها أبا خازم عبد الحميد، قاضي القضاة بالشام، فأخذ عنه عن عيسى ابن أبان عن الإمام محمد رحمهم الله تعالى. كان إماما في الأحاديث والأخبار، وله تصانيف جليلة معتبرة منها معانى الآثار وقد يسمّى بشرح معاني الآثار، ومشكل الآثار، وأحكام القرآن والمختصر فى الفقه وشرح الجامع الصغير وشرح الجامع الكبير وغيرها. توفی رحمه الله تعالى سنة ٣٢١ هـ. (ملخص من الفوائد البهية ص ٣١ إلى (٣٤) (۲) القاضي أبو عبيد ابن حَرْبَوَيْه القاضي العلامة المحدّث الثبت قاضي القضاة، أبو عبيد، علي بن الحسين بن حرب بن عيسى البغدادي الشافعي ولي قضاء مصر، قال الإمام قال الإمام محيي الدين النووي: أصحاب الوجوه، تكرّر ذكره في " المهذب " و " الروضة ". توفي في صفر سنة ٣١٩ كان من، وصلّى عليه أبو سعيد الاصطخري، رحمهم الله تعالى أجمعين. (۳) ذكره الحافظ ابن حجر رحمه الله تعالى فى رفع الإصر عن قضاة مصر، في ذكر أبي عبيد على بن حسين بن حربویه ١:١٢٠
Methods of issuing fatwas among the Salaf: and the creation of envy, hatred, obstinacy, conflict, backbiting, cursing, insulting, slandering, and damning, which is absolutely forbidden. Yes! The man who opposes the majority of Muslims in their beliefs or in matters of consensus, or who extends his tongue against the noble Salaf, then he is outside Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah, because Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah are those who follow the path of the Companions. And these matters contradict their beliefs, so this man is outside Ahl al-Sunnah and inside the people of innovation and desires. Likewise, the man who goes to excess in his taqlid such that he rejects the Qur'an and Hadith for its sake, then it is obligatory to avoid and be cautious of both these men, while turning away from customary argumentation. This is the middle truth. As for anything besides that, it is error and extremism. O Allah, show us the truth as truth and grant us its followers, and show us falsehood as falsehood and grant us its avoidance. (1) So it becomes clear that adhering to a specific madhhab and following a mujtahid is only for reaching the established shari'ah rulings from the Book and Sunnah for one who cannot reconcile the conflicting evidences. Therefore the scholars have stated that taqlid is not needed in matters of creed and rulings that are textually definitive, such as the obligatory nature of prayer, fasting, zakat, and Hajj, and the prohibition of wine, pork, usury, lying, deception, and betrayal, among the rulings that have no room for ijtihad, and the texts do not allow more than one meaning (2). Also, the meaning of taqlid is not that the scholars of that madhhab never contradict the statement of their Imam in any matter. Among that is what is narrated from Imam al-Tahawi, who was Hanafi, that he said: 'Abu Ubayd ibn Harbawayh (3) would discuss issues with me. One day I answered him on a issue, and he said to me: 'This is not the statement of Abu Hanifah.' I said to him: 'O judge! Am I to say everything that Abu Hanifah said?' He said: 'I thought you were a muqallid.' I said to him: 'Does a muqallid follow except out of partisanship?' He said to me: 'Stupid!' And this word spread in Egypt until it became a proverb.' What al-Tahawi intended is that adherence to a specific madhhab does not prevent a scholar like al-Tahawi from not accepting the statement of his Imam in some issues, out of partisanship. (1) Al-Iqtisad fi al-Taqleed wa al-Ijtihad by al-Shaykh Ashraf Ali al-Tahanawi rahimahullah ta'ala. (2) See al-Dhakhirah by al-Qarafi 1:148. (3) He is Ahmad Muhammad Salamah Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi [biographical details].
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage from 'Usool al-Iftaa' by Mufti Muhammad Taqi Usmani discusses the proper methodology for issuing fatwas, emphasizing the middle path between two extremes: blind fanaticism and reckless rejection of scholarly authority. The author first warns against the social harms caused by partisan disputes, such as envy and hatred, which are clearly forbidden. Then he identifies two types of people who must be avoided: (1) those who oppose the beliefs of the Muslim majority or attack the Salaf, thereby leaving Ahl al-Sunnah, and (2) those who are so extreme in their taqlid that they reject clear Quranic and Hadith evidence. The correct approach is to avoid both extremes and instead engage in dialogue with good manners. The passage then clarifies the purpose of adopting a madhhab: it is a necessary tool for those who cannot directly derive rulings from the primary sources due to conflicting evidence. However, taqlid is not needed for definitive matters like the obligatory acts of worship or prohibitions of major sins, as these are clear in the texts. The anecdote about Imam al-Tahawi illustrates that even a staunch Hanafi may legitimately differ from Abu Hanifah in some questions; this does not negate his adherence to the madhhab unless done out of blind partisanship. Thus, true taqlid is a reasoned commitment to a methodological framework, not a rigid refusal to consider other valid opinions.

Key Terms
تقليد (taqlid): Following a mujtahid in his legal rulings without requiring the evidence, necessary for those who cannot perform ijtihad.
تمذهب (tamadhhub): Adherence to a specific madhhab (school of law) as a framework for deriving and applying rulings.
أهل السنة والجماعة (ahl al-sunnah wa al-jama'ah): The mainstream Sunni community that follows the path of the Companions in creed and practice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What lesson did Imam al-Tahawi intend to teach through his exchange with the judge?
A) That taqlid is never required for anyone.
B) That adherence to a madhhab does not prevent a scholar from not taking his imam's view in some matters, as long as it is not partisanship.
C) That Abu Hanifah's rulings are always correct.
D) That the Shafi'i madhhab is superior.

Key Takeaway
Taqlid is a tool for the non-mujtahid, but within a madhhab, scholars may legitimately differ from the founder based on evidence.

Etiquette of Addressing Scholars: No 'Mawlana' Among Students in Presence of Teacher
A ruling on adab derived from Imam Muhammad's practice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi adab rule that students should not address each other as 'Mawlana' in the presence of their teacher, and justify it by citing the precedent of Imam Muhammad and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Avoid false equality in honorifics: the teacher's rank must be preserved.

In Hanafi adab, the way we address scholars reflects the hierarchy of knowledge and respect. This lesson examines a specific ruling derived from the practice of Imam Muhammad and Abu Yusuf, which forbids students from calling each other 'Mawlana' in the teacher's presence. The reasoning is to prevent any illusion of equality between the student and the teacher.

Guided Path
1
Identify the precedent from the Salaf
What did Imam Muhammad do regarding Abu Yusuf in al-Jami' al-Saghir? Why did he mention him by name rather than by his kunya?
The kunya is a title of respect.
2
Understand the reason: avoiding wahm al-taswiya
What illusion is being avoided? How would using the kunya create an impression of equality between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf?
Abu Hanifa is the teacher of Abu Yusuf.
3
Extract the adab ruling for students
What did the scholars of Bukhara derive from this precedent? How does the precedent of teachers apply to students?
They applied the same principle to students addressing each other.
4
Apply the ruling to the term 'Mawlana'
Why is 'Mawlana' specifically problematic in the presence of a teacher? What does using 'Mawlana' for a fellow student imply?
'Mawlana' means 'our master'.
5
Note the scope and exceptions
When is this ruling applicable? Is it an absolute prohibition on using 'Mawlana' among students?
The ruling is context-specific: only in the teacher's presence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي غاية البيان شرح الهداية لأمير كاتب الإتقاني في باب الأذان : ذكر محمد في الجامع الصغير أبا يوسف باسمه دون كنيته، حتى لا يكون وهم التّسوية في التعظيم بين الشيخين، لأنّ الكنية للتعظيم، وكان محمد مأموراً من جهة أبي يوسف بأن يذكره باسمه، حيث يذكرُ أبا حنيفة رحمهم تعالى. فَعَنْ هذا قال مشايخنا ببخارا : من الأدب أن لا يدعو بعض الطلبة بعضهم بلفظ "مولانا" عند أستاذهم احترازاً عن التسوية في التعظيم بين الأستاذ والتلميذ.
And in Ghayat al-Bayan, the commentary on al-Hidayah by Amir Katib al-Itqani, in the chapter on the adhan: Muhammad mentioned in al-Jami‘ al-Saghir Abu Yusuf by his name without his kunya, so that there would be no illusion of equality in honor between the two shaykhs, because the kunya is for honor. And Muhammad was instructed by Abu Yusuf to mention him by name when he mentions Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on them. For this reason, our scholars in Bukhara said: It is part of etiquette that some students not call each other with the word 'Mawlana' in the presence of their teacher, as a precaution against equality in honor between the teacher and the student.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on the etiquette (adab) of addressing teachers and students, derived from the practice of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani and Abu Yusuf. It explains that Imam Muhammad, when writing al-Jami‘ al-Saghir, mentioned Abu Yusuf by his name (Yaqub) rather than his kunya (Abu Yusuf) to avoid creating an impression of equality in stature between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Since the kunya is used as a title of respect, using it for Abu Yusuf alongside Abu Hanifa's name could suggest they are of equal rank. Abu Yusuf himself instructed Muhammad to do so. Based on this precedent, the scholars of Bukhara ruled that it is against adab for students to address each other as 'Mawlana' (our master) in the presence of their teacher, as this would imply equality between the teacher and the student. This ruling is a specific application of the broader principle of avoiding false equality in honorifics.

Key Terms
كنية (kunya): An honorific name beginning with 'Abu' or 'Umm', used as a sign of respect.
مولانا (mawlana): A term meaning 'our master', used as a respectful title for teachers and scholars.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) To avoid creating an illusion of equality in honor between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf
C) Because Abu Yusuf's kunya was unknown
D) To show disrespect to Abu Yusuf

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi adab ruling against students calling each other 'Mawlana' in the teacher's presence is derived from the precedent of Imam Muhammad's careful omission of Abu Yusuf's kunya to avoid equality in honor.

Fast Quran Recitation as a Karamah: A Biographical Lesson
Biographical anecdote with a lesson on karamah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi concept of karamah by referencing the biographical example of 'Imad al-Din's fast Quran recitation in Tarawih.

Core Idea
Speed in Quran recitation, when done with devotion, can be a divine gift (karamah).

This passage presents a biographical note about the father of a Hanafi scholar, 'Imad al-Din 'Ali ibn Ahmad, who used to recite the entire Quran in Tarawih within a remarkably short time. The author, citing al-Laknawi, defends this speed as a karamah (a supernatural favor granted to saints) and warns against denying such occurrences, as it contradicts the consensus of Ahl al-Sunnah. For a mufti, understanding that outward actions may be supported by spiritual states is essential to avoid hasty judgments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and his action
Who is being described? What did he do in terms of Quran recitation? The passage mentions 'Imad al-Din 'Ali ibn Ahmad and his extremely fast recitation during Tarawih.
He led Tarawih in three hours and forty minutes, covering the entire Quran.
2
Recognize the claim: this speed is a karamah
Al-Laknawi explicitly states that this speed is a karamah from among his karamat. What does karamah mean in the Hanafi tradition?
A karamah is a supernatural event granted to a saint (wali), distinct from a prophet's miracle (mu'jizah).
3
Understand the defense of karamat
Why does the author argue that denying such speed is wrong? The text says denying karamat is equivalent to denying supernatural events, which goes against the consensus of the majority (Ahl al-Sunnah).
This reinforces the Ahl al-Sunnah belief in the possibility of karamat.
4
Note the multiple sources cited
The author lists several biographical works (al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyyah, Taj al-Tarajim, al-A'lam, al-Jawahir al-Mudiyyah) to authenticate this account.
Such cross-referencing is common in Hanafi biographical literature to establish reliability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأعيان.
توفی رحمه الله سنة ٧٥٨ هـ. (فائدة) يذكر عن والده عماد الدين على بن أحمد) أنه كان يقرأ القرآن فى أقل مدة حتى صلّى التراويح به في ثلاث ساعات وثلثى ساعة بحضور من قال اللكنوى في الفوائد البهية (ص۱۱۷) في ترجمة والده رحمه الله تعالى: "وهذا القدر من السرعة كرامة من كراماته. وقد اتصف بها جمع كثير، ولا ينكره إلا من أنكر صدور الخوارق وهو لإجماع الجمهور خارق, ملخص من الفوائد البهية (ص ۱۰) وتاج التراجم (ص۸۹) والأعلام ( ج ۱ ص (٥١) والجواهر المضيئة (ج١ ص ٢١٣ و ٢١٤).
The notable figures. He died (may Allah have mercy on him) in the year 758 AH. (Benefit): It is mentioned about his father 'Imad al-Din 'Ali ibn Ahmad that he used to recite the Quran in the shortest time, so that he led Tarawih prayer with it in three hours and two-thirds of an hour, in the presence of whoever said. al-Laknawi in al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyyah (p. 117) in the biography of his father (may Allah have mercy on him) states: "This amount of speed is a karamah (miracle) among his karamat. Many people have been characterized by it, and none denies it except one who denies the occurrence of supernatural events, and it is a violation of the norm (kharq) by consensus of the majority." Summarized from al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyyah (p. 10), Taj al-Tarajim (p. 89), al-A'lam (vol. 1, p. 51), and al-Jawahir al-Mudiyyah (vol. 1, pp. 213-214).
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This is a biographical note (fā’idah) about the father of a scholar (likely of Ibn Abidin or al-Laknawi? Actually the text says 'his father', referring to the father of the person who died in 758 AH). The father, 'Imad al-Din 'Ali ibn Ahmad, was known for his extremely fast recitation of the Quran, such that he would complete the entire Tarawih prayer recitation in three hours and forty minutes (three hours and two-thirds of an hour). The author quotes al-Laknawi's verification that this speed was a miraculous gift (karamah) from Allah, and such speed has been witnessed in many righteous individuals. Denying the possibility of such karamat is tantamount to rejecting the occurrence of supernatural acts, which contradicts the consensus of the majority (Ahl al-Sunnah). This is a biographical illustration that even extraordinary speed in recitation can be a sign of divine favor.

Key Terms
كرامة (Karāmah): A supernatural event granted by Allah to a saint (wali) as a sign of honor, distinguished from a prophet's miracle (mu'jizah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is blameworthy and should not be imitated.
B) It is a karamah and a sign of divine favor.
C) It is only possible through lack of tajweed.
D) It is an innovation (bid'ah).

Key Takeaway
Extremely fast Quran recitation can be a karamah from Allah and should not be automatically rejected; a mufti must consider spiritual possibilities.

Correcting Ibn Abidin: The Arrangement of al-Muhit
Critical refinement of Ibn Abidin's historical claim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the correct attribution of the first systematically arranged fatwa collection in the Hanafi madhhab and critique the methodological error in Ibn Abidin's account.

Core Idea
Ibn Abidin's praise of Radi al-Din's arrangement actually applies to al-Muhit al-Burhani.

This lesson examines a critical refinement by Muhammad Taqi al-Uthmani regarding the history of Hanafi fatwa compilations. Ibn Abidin, in his commentary on Rasm al-Mufti, credited Radi al-Din al-Sarakhsi's al-Muhit with being the first to organize rulings into usul, nawadir, and fatawa. However, modern examination of manuscripts reveals that this description fits al-Muhit al-Burhani by Burhan al-Din ibn Maza, not al-Sarakhsi's work. Understanding this correction is crucial for properly tracing the development of Hanafi fatwa methodology and avoiding historical errors.

Guided Path
1
Identify Ibn Abidin's claim
Ibn Abidin states that Radi al-Din al-Sarakhsi's al-Muhit arranged rulings into usul, then nawadir, then fatawa.
This claim is found in his Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti.
2
Note the author's critique
Muhammad Taqi al-Uthmani suggests Ibn Abidin likely never personally saw either al-Muhit work.
He says 'it appears he did not see it himself, nor al-Muhit al-Burhani'.
3
Examine the evidence from al-Muhit al-Burhani
The introduction of al-Muhit al-Burhani explicitly states the author categorized the issues. The editor confirmed that a manuscript of Radi al-Din's al-Muhit was mixed and unarranged.
The editor, Shaykh Na'im Ashraf, examined a copy and found the issues mixed.
4
Determine the correct attribution
The credit for systematic arrangement goes to Burhan al-Din ibn Maza, not Radi al-Din al-Sarakhsi.
Al-Muhit al-Burhani is the organized work.
5
Extract the lesson for fatwa methodology
The distinction between categories (usul, nawadir, fatawa) is important for understanding authority levels in the madhhab.
This classification helps muftis weigh evidence properly.

طبقات الفقها
المذهب، فإنّها قد تكون استنباطاً جديداً من القرآن والسنّة على أصل الحنفيّة، وقد تكون تخريجاً أو قياساً على بعض المسائل التي نصوا عليها،
وقد تكون ترجيحاً لبعض الأقوال المروية عنهم على بعض. قال ابن عابدين رحمه الله تعالى: "وقد يتفق لهم أن يُخالفوا أصحاب المذهب لدلائل وأسباب ظهرت لهم. وأول كتاب جمع في فتواهم فيما بلغنا "كتاب النوازل " للفقيه أبى الليث السمرقندي، ثم جمع المشايخ بعده كتبا أخر، كمجموع النوازل والواقعات للناطفي ، والواقعات للصدر الشهيد. ثم ذكر المتأخرون هذه المسائل () مختلطة غير مميزة، كما في فتاوى قاضي خان والخلاصة وغيرهما، وميّز بعضهم كما فى كتاب المحيط لرضي الدين السَّرَحْسِيّ (٣) ، فإنّه ذكر أولاً مسائل الأصول، ثم النوادر ... ثمّ الفتاوى، ونِعْمَ ما فعل.

المحيط البرهاني ١:١٥٩
Layers of Jurists. The madhhab, for they may be a new deduction from the Quran and Sunnah upon the Hanafi principle, and may be a takhrij or qiyas upon some of the issues they explicitly stated, and may be a tarjih of some of the transmitted statements over others. Ibn Abidin (may Allah have mercy on him) said: "It sometimes happens that they contradict the founders of the madhhab due to proofs and reasons that appeared to them. The first book compiled on their fatwas, as far as we know, is 'Kitab al-Nawazil' by the jurist Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi. Then the later scholars compiled other books, such as 'Majmu' al-Nawazil wa al-Waqi'at' by al-Natifi, and 'al-Waqi'at' by al-Sadr al-Shahid. Then the later ones mentioned these issues mixed without distinction, as in Fatawa Qadi Khan and al-Khulasa and others. And some distinguished them, as in the book al-Muhit by Radi al-Din al-Sarakhsi, for he first mentioned the issues of the usul, then the nawadir..., then the fatawa. Excellent what he did." The weak slave (may Allah pardon him) said: This is what Ibn Abidin mentioned regarding the Muhit of Radi al-Din al-Sarakhsi, and it appears he did not see it himself, nor al-Muhit al-Burhani. The reality that became apparent after the printing of al-Muhit al-Burhani is that this description applies to it, not to the Muhit of Radi al-Din al-Sarakhsi. For Imam Burhan al-Din said in the introduction to his Muhit: "I collected the issues of al-Mabsut, al-Jami'ayn, al-Siyar, and al-Ziyadat, and appended to them the issues of al-Nawadir, al-Fatawa, and al-Waqi'at, and added to them benefits I gained from my master and father (may Allah envelop him in mercy) and the subtleties I preserved from my teachers. I detailed the book in detail and categorized the issues in categories." And the editor of the book, my nephew Shaykh Na'im Ashraf (may Allah preserve him), said that he saw a copy of al-Muhit al-Radawi and said: "I examined some parts of it and found the issues mixed and unarranged, contrary to what I heard and saw in the statement of some scholars that they mentioned that Radi al-Din al-Sarakhsi distinguished and arranged the issues, so he first mentioned the issues of..." [story about al-Sarakhsi's speech impediment follows]. Footnotes: (1) Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti p.25. (2) Al-Muhit al-Burhani 1:159.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage discusses the development of fatwa literature within the Hanafi madhhab. The author Ibn Abidin notes that later jurists sometimes derived new rulings from the Quran and Sunnah based on Hanafi principles, or used takhrij (derivation from existing rulings) and qiyas (analogy), or preferred one narrated opinion over others. He then traces the history of fatwa collections: the first was Kitab al-Nawazil by Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi, followed by works of al-Natifi and al-Sadr al-Shahid. Later compilations like Fatawa Qadi Khan and al-Khulasa mixed rulings from different categories (Zahir al-Riwayah, Nawadir, Fatawa) without distinction. A notable exception was al-Muhit by Radi al-Din al-Sarakhsi, who reportedly organized them: first the usul (core principles), then nawadir (rare narrations), then fatawa (later fatwas). Ibn Abidin praised this. However, the author (Muhammad Taqi al-Uthmani) offers a critical refinement: Ibn Abidin likely never saw the actual works. After printing al-Muhit al-Burhani (by Burhan al-Din ibn Maza), it becomes clear that the description of organized arrangement applies to that work, not to Radi al-Din's al-Muhit. The editor of al-Muhit al-Burhani examined a manuscript of Radi al-Din's al-Muhit and found the issues mixed and unarranged. Thus, the credit for systematic classification goes to Burhan al-Din, not Radi al-Din. The passage concludes with a biographical anecdote about Radi al-Din al-Sarakhsi, who had a speech impediment (lisp) that led to mockery and his dismissal from teaching in Aleppo. This story, from al-Jawahir al-Mudi'a, illustrates the human dimension of scholarship. The footnotes cite Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti and al-Muhit al-Burhani. This lesson emphasizes the importance of distinguishing between different categories of transmitted rulings (Zahir al-Riwayah, Nawadir, Fatawa) in fatwa compilations, a key concern in the methodology of iftaa.

Key Terms
النوازل (al-nawāzil): Fatwas on newly occurring events, often compiled as a genre of Hanafi legal literature.
ظاهر الرواية (ẓāhir al-riwāyah): The core transmitted rulings from Abu Hanifa and his students via reliable chains, forming the basis of the madhhab.
النوادر (al-nawādir): Rare or less authentic transmissions from Hanafi imams, outside the six books.
الفتاوى (al-fatāwā): Later jurists' fatwas based on ijtihad or tarjih within the madhhab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correction in this lesson, which work actually organized rulings into usul, nawadir, and fatawa?
A) Kitab al-Nawazil by Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi
B) Al-Muhit by Radi al-Din al-Sarakhsi
C) Al-Muhit al-Burhani by Burhan al-Din ibn Maza
D) Fatawa Qadi Khan

Key Takeaway
Historical claims about early fatwa collections must be verified against actual manuscripts; the systematic arrangement attributed to Radi al-Din al-Sarakhsi actually belongs to al-Muhit al-Burhani.

Adab al-Mufti — Ethics of the Mufti
intermediate
8 min
The Mufti's Need for Verification and Understanding of Fiqh Books
Explaining two essential qualifications for the mufti: verification of rulings and understanding fiqh book styles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two essential qualifications for a mufti—tanqih al-madhhab and understanding fiqh book styles—and apply them to detect and correct transmission errors in later compilations.

Core Idea
A mufti must verify rulings against early sources and understand the implicit style of fiqh texts.

In the discipline of ifta', the mufti's authority rests on accurate knowledge of the madhhab. However, later fiqh compilations sometimes contain errors that have been transmitted uncritically. This passage, from a summary of Rasm al-Mufti, outlines two critical skills: tanqih al-madhhab—verifying that a ruling is correctly attributed to the Imam—and understanding the distinctive style of fiqh literature, where absolute statements may hide implicit restrictions. Mastering these prevents the mufti from issuing fatwas based on mistaken transmissions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Essential Qualifications
Read the opening sentence: the mufti needs knowledge, intelligence, and a juristic faculty, followed by two specific 'matters' (الأمر الأول, الأمر الثاني). The first is tanqih al-madhhab (verification of the madhhab). The second is understanding the style of fiqh books.
The 'juristic faculty' (ملكة فقهية) is the overarching quality; the two items are practical requirements.
2
Examine the Examples of Transmission Errors
The passage gives three examples from Ibn Abidin: (1) hiring for Quran recitation vs. teaching, (2) repentance of a sabb, (3) mortgagee liability. For each, note the error and the correct ruling.
These illustrate how later books can perpetuate mistakes. The mufti must trace back to early sources.
3
Analyze the Madhhab Dispute on Repentance of a Sabb
The passage contrasts the early Hanafi position (acceptance) from Kitab al-Kharaj, Sharh al-Tahawi, and al-Nutaf with the later claim of non-acceptance from al-Bazzaziyya. Use the Madhhab Dispute Map to structure the analysis.
Ibn Taymiyyah's view was mistakenly attributed to the Hanafis; the error was propagated through Ibn al-Humam.
4
Understand the Second Matter: Style of Fiqh Books
Fiqh books often state absolute (mutlaq) rulings while intending restricted (muqayyad) meanings, relying on other passages or reader's knowledge. A mere reading can lead to misunderstanding.
This is a common pitfall: the mufti must read holistically and be aware of the author's method.
5
Apply Ibn Abidin's Methodology
Ibn Abidin is praised for consulting early sources (أصل الكتب المتقدمة) in his gloss. Recognize that his Hashiya is a model for verification.
The mufti should adopt a similar practice: verify against al-mutun al-mu'tabara and early shuruh.

أصول الإفتاء

تلخيص قواعد رسم المفتي

وإنّما يحتاج إلى علم وفِطْنةٍ ومَلَكةٍ فقهيّة لا يُمكن أن تستقيم الفتوى بدونها، وذلك لأمور:

الأمر الأول: لابد من تنقيح مذهب المجتهد، والتأكد من صحة نسبته إليه. فقد يوجد أغلاط فى النقل عنه ، وقد ذكر ابن عابدين رحمه الله تعالى عدة أمثلة لمثل هذه الأغلاط فقال: "وقد يتفق نقل قول في نحو عشرين كتاباً من كتب المتأخرين، ويكون القول خطاً أخطأ به أول واضع له، فيأتي من بعده وينقله عنه، وهكذا ينقل بعضهم عن بعض." وقد ذكر رحمه الله تعالى عدة أمثلة لذلك. فمنها : أنه وقع في السراج الوهاج والجوهرة شرح القدوري [أن] المفتى به صحة الاستئجار على تلاوة القرآن، ونقل ذلك كثير ممن جاءوا بعدهم، مع أنّ ذلك خطأ، فإنّ المفتى به هو صحة الاستئجار على تعليم القرآن، وليس على تلاوة القرآن، لأنّ فتوى الجواز مبنى على الضرورة في التعليم والإمامة والأذان، ولا يتعدى إلى مالا ضرورة فيه.

ومنها ما ذكر في البزازيّة من أن مذهب الحنفية عدم قبول توبة ساب الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم، وذلك على أساس ماذكره ابن تيمية رحمه الله تعالى فى الصارم المسلول، ونقل عنها ابن الهمام وغيره كذلك، ولكن المذهب المذكور في كتب المتقدمين من الحنفية مثل "كتاب الخراج" لأبي يوسف، وشرح الطحاوي، والنتف للسغدي هو قبول توبته،

(1) الإمام السغدي: هو علي بن الحسين ركن الإسلام أبو الحسن السُّغدي، نسبته إلى سغد بضم السين وسكون الغين ناحية من نواحى سمرقند، تلميذ شمس الأئمة السرخسي رحمه الله تعالى قال الإمام اللكنوي رحمه الله تعالى فى الفوائد البهيّة: "أخذ الفقه عن شمس الأئمة السرخسي وروى عنه شرح السير الكبير." وصاحب "النتف" في الفتاوى كان إماماً فاضلاً فقيهاً مناظراً. سكن بخارى وتصدّر للإفتاء وولي القضاء. انتهت إليه رئاسة الحنفية ورحل إليه فى النوازل والواقعات تكرر ذكره في فتاوى قاضيخان وسائر مشاهير الفتاوى تُوُفِّي رحمه الله سنة ٤٦١ هـ. ملخص من الفوائد البهية ص۱۲۱)

وأما عدم قبول توبته فذكره ابن تيمية رحمه الله مذهباً لغير الحنفية. ومنها ما وقع في الدرر وشرح المجمع لابن ملك، وتبعه في التنوير من أن المرتهن إن ادعى هلاك الرهن بلا برهان، فإنّه يضمنه، وإن برهن على ذلك، فلا يضمَنُ شيئاً، مع أن المذهب ضمانه بالأقل من قيمته ومن الدين، بلافرق بین ثبوتِ الهلاك ببرهان وبدونه ونبه عليه ابن عابدين رحمه الله تعالى في حاشيته على الدر المختار. وقد التزم ابن عابدين رحمه الله تعالى في هذه الحاشية بمراجعة أصل الكتب المتقدمة التى هى مأخذ المذهب، ولهذا كانت حاشيته من أحسن المآخذ المعتبرة للفقه الحنفي، فجزاه الله تعالى خيراً. الأمر الثاني: أن الكتب الفقهيّة لها أسلوب يخصها، فربما يذكر الفقهاء كلاماً مطلقاً، ويقصدون بذلك شيئاً مقيداً اعتماداً على ذكر تلك القيود في مواضع أخرى، أو على فهم القارئ العالم، فمجرد مطالعة كتاب الفقه ربما يؤدى

(1) ابن ملك: هو عبد اللطيف بن عبد العزيز بن أمين الدين بن فرشتا الكرماني، الشهير بابن ملك، نسبة إلى جدّه فرشتا من الفقهاء الحنفية المبرزين كان يسكن ويدرس في بلدة تيره، من مضافات ازمير من بلاد تركيا. وكان معلّماً للأمير محمد بن آيدين أيام السلطان مراد. له تصانيف كثيرة في فنون متنوعة من أشهرها "مبارق الأزهار فى شرح مشارق الأنوار" وهو كتاب جامع للأحاديث على ترتيب أنيق، وله شرح "المنار" للإمام النسفي فى أصول الفقه، وشرح "مجمع البحرين" للعلامة ابن الساعاتي في الفقه. وله أيضاً شرح على الوقاية، لكن سُرقت النسخة التي بيضها، فنقله ابنه محمد من المسودة وزاد عليه فوائد. وليراجع كشف الظنون والفوائد البهية لمزيد التفصيل. ونسب إليه الزركلي شرحاً لـ "تحفة الملوك"، لكن حقق الدكتور عبد المجيد الدرويش الذي اعتنى بتحقيق ودراسة هذا الشرح أنه لابنه محمد بن عبد اللطيف ونسبته إلى أبيه خطأ. هذا وقد وقع اختلاف فى تاريخ وفاته رحمه الله، وعوّل الزركلي على قول صاحب هدية العارفين الذي قال: "توفي سنة ۸۰۱ وأرخوا وفاته ببرهان الأتقياء." (ملخص من الفوائد البهية ص ۱۰۷ و ۱٠۸، وهدية العارفين ۱: ٦۱۷ والأعلام ٤: ٥٩، وكشف الظنون ۲: ۲۰۲۱، ومقدمة المحقق لشرح كتاب تحفة الملوك والبدر الطالع ١: ٢٦٠ و ٢٦١)

۱۰۷
Principles of Issuing Fatwa
Summary of the Rules of the Mufti's Methodology

He indeed needs knowledge, intelligence, and a juristic faculty without which fatwa cannot be upright, and that is for several reasons:

The first matter: It is necessary to refine the madhhab of the mujtahid and ensure the correctness of its attribution to him. For errors occur in transmission from him. Ibn Abidin (may Allah have mercy on him) mentioned several examples of such errors, saying: 'It may happen that a statement is transmitted in about twenty books of later scholars, but that statement is a mistake made by its first setter, then later ones transmit from him, and thus they transmit from one another.' He (may Allah have mercy on him) mentioned several examples of that. Among them: that it occurred in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj and al-Jawhara Sharh al-Quduri that the relied-upon fatwa is the validity of hiring for recitation of the Quran, and many who came after them transmitted that, but that is an error. Indeed, the relied-upon fatwa is the validity of hiring for teaching the Quran, not for recitation, because the fatwa of permissibility is based on necessity in teaching, leading prayers, and the call to prayer, and it does not extend to what has no necessity.

Among them is what was mentioned in al-Bazzaziyya that the Hanafi school does not accept the repentance of one who insults the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), based on what Ibn Taymiyyah (may Allah have mercy on him) mentioned in al-Sarim al-Maslul, and Ibn al-Humam and others transmitted from it likewise. But the madhhab mentioned in the books of the early Hanafis, such as Kitab al-Kharaj of Abu Yusuf, Sharh al-Tahawi, and al-Nutaf of al-Sughdi, is the acceptance of his repentance.

(1) Imam al-Sughdi: ... (biographical footnote)

As for not accepting his repentance, Ibn Taymiyyah mentioned it as the madhhab of non-Hanafis. And among them is what occurred in al-Durar and Sharh al-Majma' of Ibn Malik, followed in al-Tanwir, that if the mortgagee claims the destruction of the collateral without proof, he is liable for it, but if he proves it, he is not liable for anything, while the madhhab is his liability for the lesser of its value or the debt, with no difference between proving destruction with proof or without. Ibn Abidin (may Allah have mercy on him) pointed this out in his gloss on al-Durr al-Mukhtar. Ibn Abidin committed himself in this gloss to consulting the original early books that are the sources of the madhhab, and for this reason his gloss is among the best reliable sources for Hanafi fiqh. May Allah reward him well. The second matter: that fiqh books have a style particular to them. Perhaps the jurists mention an absolute statement, intending by it something restricted, relying on mentioning those restrictions in other places, or on the understanding of the knowledgeable reader. So mere study of a fiqh book may lead to...

(1) Ibn Malik: ... (biographical footnote)

107
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage is from the summary of rules for the mufti (Rasm al-Mufti). It opens by stating that a mufti requires knowledge, intelligence, and a juristic faculty. The author then lists two essential matters. The first matter is the necessity of verifying the madhhab of the mujtahid and ensuring correct attribution, because errors have been transmitted. The author quotes Ibn Abidin, who gave examples: (1) Many later books wrongly stated that hiring for Quran recitation is valid, but the correct Hanafi position is that it is only valid for teaching, due to necessity. (2) Some later works claimed the Hanafis do not accept the repentance of one who insults the Prophet, but early Hanafi authorities (Abu Yusuf, al-Tahawi, al-Sughdi) accept it; the opposite view was attributed to non-Hanafis by Ibn Taymiyyah. (3) An error regarding mortgagee liability: some books said that if the mortgagee proves destruction he is not liable, but the correct ruling is liability for the lesser of value or debt regardless of proof. Ibn Abidin is praised for verifying sources.

Then the second matter is introduced: fiqh books have a particular style; they sometimes state absolute rulings intending restricted meanings, relying on context or other passages. Merely reading a fiqh book may lead to misunderstanding without this awareness. The passage ends mid-sentence, but the point is clear: the mufti must also understand the implicit style of fiqh literature.

Key Terms
تنقيح مذهب المجتهد (tanqīḥ madhhab al-mujtahid): The process of verifying and refining the attributed rulings of a mujtahid/imam, distinguishing correct from erroneous transmissions.
رسم المفتي (rasm al-muftī): The set of rules and methodology that a mufti must follow when issuing fatwas.
الفتوى (al-fatwā): A non-binding legal opinion issued by a qualified jurist, based on the established rulings of the madhhab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Correcting an Error in the Madhhab: The Mortgagee's Liability
Correction of an error in the madhhab regarding mortgagee liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a common error in later Hanafi texts regarding the mortgagee's liability and apply the correct Hanafi ruling as confirmed by Ibn Abidin.

Core Idea
The mortgagee guarantees the lesser of the pledge's value and the debt, regardless of proof of destruction.

This lesson examines a real error found in some later Hanafi works (al-Durar, Sharh al-Majma', al-Tanwir) regarding the ruling when a pledged item is destroyed. The error claimed that if the mortgagee proves the destruction, he is not liable. Ibn Abidin corrected this by returning to the foundational sources of the madhhab. You will learn why this error occurred and how to identify the correct ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the erroneous ruling
Read the passage and note what al-Durar and Sharh al-Majma' claimed: that if the mortgagee proves the destruction, he is not liable. Compare with the correct madhhab position.
The error is a common pitfall: relying on later texts without verification.
2
State the correct Hanafi position
The authentic Hanafi madhhab, as found in early sources, holds that the mortgagee guarantees the lesser of the pledge's value and the debt, regardless of whether he proves destruction.
Ibn Abidin emphasizes 'la farq' (no difference) between proving or not.
3
Understand Ibn Abidin's methodology
Ibn Abidin corrected the error by reviewing the original books (al-kutub al-mutaqaddima) that are the sources of the madhhab. His Hashiyah is praised as one of the best reliable references.
This illustrates the importance of tracing rulings to their roots.
4
Note the practical difference (thamarah)
In the erroneous view, the mortgagee pays nothing if he proves destruction. In the correct view, he still pays the lesser of value or debt. This directly affects the mufti's fatwa.
The mufti must know the rajih (preponderant) opinion to avoid giving incorrect fatwa.

Source Text

تلخيص قواعد رسم المفتي

وأما عدم قبول توبته فذكره ابن تيمية رحمه الله مذهباً لغير الحنفية. ومنها ما وقع في الدرر وشرح المجمع لابن ملك ، وتبعه في التنوير من أن المرتهن إن ادعى هلاك الرهن بلا برهان، فإنّه يضمنه، وإن برهن على ذلك، فلا يضمَنُ شيئاً، مع أن المذهب ضمانه بالأقل من قيمته ومن الدين، بلافرق بین ثبوتِ الهلاك ببرهان وبدونه ونبه عليه ابن عابدين رحمه الله تعالى في حاشيته على الدر المختار. وقد التزم ابن عابدين رحمه الله تعالى في هذه الحاشية بمراجعة أصل الكتب المتقدمة التى هى مأخذ المذهب، ولهذا كانت حاشيته من أحسن المآخذ المعتبرة للفقه الحنفي، فجزاه الله تعالى خيراً.

(1) ابن ملك: هو عبد اللطيف بن عبد العزيز بن أمين الدين بن فرشتا الكرماني، الشهير بابن ملك، نسبة إلى جدّه فرشتا من الفقهاء الحنفية المبرزين كان يسكن ويدرس في بلدة تيره، من مضافات ازمير من بلاد تركيا. وكان معلّماً للأمير محمد بن آيدين أيام السلطان مراد. له تصانيف كثيرة في فنون متنوعة من أشهرها "مبارق الأزهار في شرح مشارق الأنوار" وهو كتاب جامع للأحاديث على ترتيب أنيق، وله شرح "المنار" للإمام النسفي في أصول الفقه، وشرح "مجمع البحرين" للعلامة ابن الساعاتي في الفقه. وله أيضاً شرح على الوقاية، لكن سُرقت النسخة التي بيضها، فنقله ابنه محمد من المسودة وزاد عليه فوائد. وليراجع كشف الظنون والفوائد البهية لمزيد التفصيل. ونسب إليه الزركلي شرحاً لـ "تحفة الملوك"، لكن حقق الدكتور عبد المجيد الدرويش الذي اعتنى بتحقيق ودراسة هذا الشرح، أنه لابنه محمد بن عبد اللطيف ونسبته إلى أبيه خطأ. هذا وقد وقع اختلاف فى تاريخ وفاته رحمه الله، وعوّل الزركلي على قول صاحب هدية العارفين الذي قال: "تُوفي سنة ۸۰۱ وأرخوا وفاته ببرهان الأتقياء." (ملخص من الفوائد البهية ص ٦ و ١٠٨، وهدية العارفين ١: ٦١٧ والأعلام ٤: ٥٩، وكشف الظنون ٢: ٢٠٢١، ومقدمة المحقق لشرح كتاب تحفة الملوك والبدر الطالع ١: ٢٦٠ و ٢٦١)

الأمر الثاني: أن الكتب الفقهيّة لها أسلوب يخصها، فربما يذكر الفقهاء كلاماً مطلقاً، ويقصدون بذلك شيئاً مقيداً اعتماداً على ذكر تلك القيود في مواضع أخرى، أو على فهم القارئ العالم، فمجرد مطالعة كتاب الفقه ربما يؤدى إلى خلاف المقصود وأمّا من قرأها لدى أساتذة مَهَرَةٍ، فإنّه يتنبّه على مثل ذلك، فلا يقع في خطأ، ولهذا لا يكفى معرفة اللغة العربيّة فقط، بل يجب التفقه على أستاذ ماهر.

الأمر الثالث: أنه ربما توجد روايات مختلفة عن المجتهد، ولابد من ترجيح بعضها على بعض، إما بقوة النقل وشهرته، وإما بترجيح أصحاب الترجيح على أساس قوة الدليل، كما سيأتى إن شاء الله تعالى. فلابد للمفتى وإن كان ناقلاً، أن من يتثبت في ماهو راجح. ونقل ابن عابدين رحمه الله تعالى عن خير الدين الرملي رحمه الله تعالى قال: "ولاشك أن معرفة راجح المختلف فيه من مرجوجه ومراتبه قوةً وضعفاً هو نهاية آمال المُسمرين في تحصيل العلم فالمفروض على المفتى والقاضي التثبت في الجواب وعدم المجازفة فيهما، خوفاً من الافتراء على الله تعالى "

والأمر الرابع أنه لا يكفى للمفتى، ولوكان ناقلاً، أن يعرف القول الصحيح الراجح المروي عن المجتهد، وإنما يحتاج بعد ذلك إلى تنزيل ذلك القول على الواقعة الجزئية التي سُئل عنها. ويجب لذلك الفهم الصحيح والملكة الفقهيّة، فإنّ مثل هذا المفتى وإن لم يكن مجتهداً في معرفة الأحكام الشرعيّة، ولكنّه لا محيص له من نوع من الاجتهاد، وهو الاجتهاد في تعيين

(1) العلامة خير الدين الرملي: هو خير الدين بن أحمد بن علي الأيوبي العليمي الفاروقي الرملي، ولد في أوائل رمضان برملة فلسطين فقيه حنفي، مفسر، محدث، لغوي، مشارك في أنواع من العلوم. رحل إلى مصر ودرس بالأزهر ثم عاد إلى بلده وأخذ في التعليم والإفتاء والتدريس. أخذ عنه العلماء الكبار والمفتون والمدرسون. من تصانيفه "الفتاوى الخيرية لنفع البرية" و "مظهر الحقائق الخفية من البحر الرائق" و "حاشية على الأشباه والنظائر." تُوفي رحمه الله في ٢٧ رمضان سنة ١٠٨١ هـ. (ملخص من الأعلام ٢: ٣٢٧ ومعجم المؤلفين ٤: ١٣٢)
Summary of the rules of Rasm al-Mufti

As for the non-acceptance of his repentance, Ibn Taymiyya mentioned it as a madhhab of other than the Hanafis. And among them is what occurred in al-Durar and Sharh al-Majma' by Ibn Malik, and followed by al-Tanwir, that if the mortgagee claims the destruction of the pledge without proof, then he guarantees it, and if he brings proof of that, then he does not guarantee anything, whereas the madhhab is that he guarantees the lesser of its value and the debt, with no difference between the destruction being proven by proof or without it. And Ibn Abidin pointed this out in his Hashiyah on al-Durr al-Mukhtar. And Ibn Abidin committed himself in this Hashiyah to reviewing the origin of the earlier books that are the source of the madhhab, and therefore his Hashiyah became one of the best reliable sources for Hanafi fiqh, so may Allah reward him well.

(1) Ibn Malik: He is 'Abd al-Latif ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz ibn Amin al-Din ibn Farishta al-Kirmani, known as Ibn Malik, from the prominent Hanafi jurists... [detailed biography].

The second matter: That fiqh books have a style particular to them; sometimes the jurists mention an absolute statement and intend by it something qualified, relying on mentioning those qualifications in other places, or on the understanding of the knowledgeable reader. So merely studying a fiqh book might lead to the contrary of what is intended. But whoever reads them under master teachers, then he becomes alert to such things, so he does not fall into error. Therefore, knowledge of the Arabic language alone is not sufficient; rather, one must acquire fiqh under a master teacher.

The third matter: That sometimes different narrations from the mujtahid exist, and one must prefer some over others, either by the strength of transmission and its fame, or by the preference of those who weigh on the basis of the strength of evidence, as will come insha'Allah. Therefore, it is necessary for the mufti, even if he is a transmitter, to be certain of what is preponderant. And Ibn Abidin narrated from Khayr al-Din al-Ramli that he said: 'There is no doubt that knowing the preponderant from the preponderated among that which is differed upon, and their levels in strength and weakness, is the ultimate hope of those who strive in acquiring knowledge. So it is obligatory upon the mufti and the judge to be certain in the answer and not to be reckless in them, for fear of slandering Allah.'

The fourth matter: That it is not sufficient for the mufti, even if he is a transmitter, to know the correct, preponderant statement narrated from the mujtahid; rather, after that he needs to apply that statement to the particular incident about which he was asked. And for that, correct understanding and fiqh aptitude are necessary. For such a mufti, even if he is not a mujtahid in knowing the legal rulings, he cannot avoid a type of ijtihad, and that is the ijtihad in determining...

(1) The scholar Khayr al-Din al-Ramli: He is Khayr al-Din ibn Ahmad ibn 'Ali al-Ayubi al-'Ulaymi al-Faruqi al-Ramli... [detailed biography].
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This passage from 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti summarizes four key rules for a mufti. First, the author corrects a common error found in later Hanafi works (al-Durar, Sharh al-Majma', al-Tanwir) regarding the liability of the mortgagee when a pledged item is destroyed. Some books incorrectly claimed that if the mortgagee proves the destruction, he is not liable; the correct madhhab, as established by the earlier sources and affirmed by Ibn Abidin, is that he guarantees the lesser of the pledge's value and the debt, regardless of proof. This shows the importance of verifying rulings against the original sources of the madhhab, not relying solely on later compilations. Ibn Abidin's Hashiyah is praised for its thoroughness in this regard. A biographical footnote provides details on Ibn Malik. Second, the mufti must study fiqh under a master teacher because books often state absolute rules that have implicit qualifications taught by a shaykh. Language proficiency alone is insufficient. Third, when different narrations exist from an imam, the mufti must know which is preponderant (rajih), either by transmission strength or scholarly preference. Khayr al-Din al-Ramli stresses that this knowledge is essential for muftis and judges to avoid slandering Allah. Fourth, even after knowing the correct ruling, the mufti needs Ijthad in applying it to specific cases—this requires sound understanding and fiqh aptitude. The passage concludes mid-sentence, noting that this type of ijtihad involves determining the correct application.

Key Terms
مرتهن (murtahin): The mortgagee or pledgee—the person who holds the collateral as security for a debt.
رهن (rahn): The pledge or collateral—an item given as security for a debt.
راجح (rājiḥ): The preponderant ruling among conflicting narrations, either due to stronger transmission chain or stronger evidence.
مرجوح (marjūḥ): The outweighed or weaker ruling among conflicting narrations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Ibn Abidin corrected the erroneous view in al-Durar by:
A) Issuing a fatwa that the mortgagee is never liable.
B) Referring to the original books of the madhhab.
C) Accepting the view of al-Tanwir.
D) Creating a new ruling based on istihsan.

Key Takeaway
The correct Hanafi position is that the mortgagee guarantees the lesser of the pledge's value and the debt, regardless of proof of destruction.
