The Mufti Must Have Training and Insight
Explaining the necessity of training and insight for a mufti

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a mufti requires basira (insight) and supervised training, and evaluate the danger of self-study without scholarly certification.

Core Idea
A mufti must have practical training and insight; mere book reading is insufficient for issuing fatwas.

This passage from a classical manual on ifta underscores that issuing fatwas is not a casual act. It requires a deep, practiced understanding of Shariah—what the scholars call basira—and formal authorization from qualified teachers. Without this, a person who only reads books is considered ignorant and unfit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six matters that make ifta challenging
The text enumerates six matters (though only two are detailed here: differences across persons/customs, and new emergent issues). Recognize that a mufti must constantly apply general principles to specific cases, which requires ijtihad.
The full list is implied; focus on the two elaborated in this excerpt.
2
Understand the concept of 'basira'
Basira is not mere knowledge but a penetrating insight gained through practice. The text emphasizes that it cannot be obtained simply by studying books; it requires experience and training under experts.
Contrast with rote memorization of fiqh rulings.
3
Examine Imam Malik's example
Imam Malik did not give fatwas until seventy scholars certified him. He rebuked Ibn al-Qasim for answering a question without authorization. This illustrates the high standard of qualification.
This applies across all madhhabs, not only Maliki.
4
Analyze Ibn Hajar al-Haytami's ruling
Ibn Hajar ruled that a self-taught person who reads books without a teacher cannot give fatwa and is considered a jahil (ignorant). Even someone who studied under scholars is not automatically qualified.
This ruling is quoted by Ibn Abidin, a key Hanafi authority.
5
Synthesize the requirements for a mufti
A mufti must possess basira, which comes from supervised practice and training, not just book knowledge. Scholarly certification and ongoing mentorship are essential.
This is a foundational principle in Hanafi and broader Sunni usul al-ifta.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تلخيص قواعد رسم المفتي
لم تتنزل الأحكام الشرعيّة على أفعال المكلفين إلا في الذهن؛ لأنها مُطلَقات وعمومات، وما يرجع إلى ذلك منزلات على أفعال مطلقات كذلك، والأفعال لا تقع في الوجود مطلقة، وإنما تقع معيّنة مشخصة، فلا يكون الحكم واقعاً عليها إلا بعد المعرفة بأنّ هذا المعين يشمله ذلك المطلق أو ذلك العام، وقد يكون ذلك سهلاً وقد لا يكون، وكله اجتهاد (۱)
والأمر الخامس: أنّ الفتوى قد تختلف باختلاف الأشخاص نظراً إلى خصوص أحوالهم، وباختلاف العُرفِ وأحوال الزمان حسب تحقيق المناط كما سيأتي إن شاء الله تعالى.
والأمر السادس: أن كثيراً من المسائل الجديدة تنشأ في كل عصر، وحدثت في عصرنا هذا بصفة خاصة، حيث تغيّرت مناهج الحياة إلى حد كبير عما كانت معهودةً فى عهد المجتهدين السابقين. فلا يوجد لمثل هذه المسائل ذكر صريح في كتبهم حتى يُنقل بعينه. وإنما يحتاج المفتى المعاصر في معرفة حكمها، إما إلى تنزيلها على العمومات الواردة في كلامهم، أو القياس والاستنباط من نظائرها وأشباهها. وإنّه عمل دقيق لابد له من بصيرة ثاقبة، وفهم المبادئ الشرعية فهماً صحيحاً.
ونظراً إلى هذه الأمور الستة، لابد للمفتى، وإن كان مقلدا، من أن تكون له بصيرة في جميع هذه الأمور. وإن مثل هذه البصيرة لا تحصل بمجرد مطالعة الكتب وحفظ جزئيات الفقه، وإنّما تحتاج إلى ملكة فقهيّة وتجربة لا تكاد تحصل إلا بممارسة الفتوى والتمرن عليها لدى أساتذة مهرة. ولذلك قالوا ليس كل من قرأ الكتب الفقهيّة أهلاً للإفتاء حتى يكون قد تدرب على الإفتاء بصفة مستقلة، وشهد له العلماء بأنه أهل للإفتاء.
وقد حكى عن الإمام مالك رحمه الله تعالى أنه قال: "ليس كل من أحب أن يجلس للحديث والفتيا، جلس حتى يُشاور فيه أهل الصلاح والفضل وأهل الجهة من المسجد، فإن رأوه لذلك أهلاً جلس، وما جلست حتى شهد لي سبعون شيخاً من أهل العلم أنّى موضع لذلك." وقال ابن وهب: وجاء رجل يسأل مالكاً عن مسألة، فبادر ابن القاسم فأفتاه، فأقبل عليه مالك كالمُغضَب وقال له: جَسَرْت على أن تُفتى يا عبد الرحمن، يكررها عليه، ما أفتيت حتى سألت هل أنا للفتيا موضع ؟ فلما سكن غضبه، قيل له: من سألت؟ قال: الزهري وربيعةَ الرّأي وعلى هذا الأساس قال ابن حجر الهَيْتَمِي ، كما نقل عنه ابن عابدين رحمهما الله تعالى: سئل رحمه الله تعالى فى شخص يقرأ ويطالع الكتب الفقهية بنفسه، ولم يكن له شيخ يقرر له المسائل الدينية والدنيوية، ثمّ إنّه يُسأل عن مسائل دينية ودنيوية، فيفتيهم ويعتمد على مطالعته في الكتب، ولم يتوقف فيما يُسأل عنه، هل يجوز له ذلك؟ وإذا قلتم بعدم الجواز، فماذا يستحقه من قبل الله تعالى ورسوله صلى الله عليه وسلّم؟ فأجاب، نفع الله تعالى به، بقوله: لا يجوز لهذا المذكور الإفتاء بوجه من الوجوه، لأنه عامي جاهل، لا يدرى ما يقول، بل الذي أخذ العلم عن المشايخ المعتبرين، لا يجوز له أن يُفتي من
Summary of the rules of Rasm al-Mufti: The legal rulings are not applied to the actions of the responsible individuals except in the mind, because they are absolutes and generals, and what pertains to that are similarly applied to absolute actions. But actions do not occur in existence as absolutes; rather they occur as specific and particularized. So the ruling is not applied to them except after knowing that this specific action is included in that absolute or that general. This may be easy or may not be, and all of it is ijtihad. (1)
The fifth matter: that the fatwa may differ according to differences of persons, considering their particular circumstances, and according to differences of custom and circumstances of time, based on investigation of the effective cause (tahqiq al-manat), as will come, Allah willing.
The sixth matter: that many new issues arise in every age, and have occurred in our time specifically, as life's methodologies have changed greatly from what was usual in the era of previous mujtahids. So there is no explicit mention of such issues in their books that could be directly transmitted. Rather, the contemporary mufti needs to know their ruling either by applying the general principles mentioned in their words, or by analogical deduction (qiyas) and inference from their parallels and similars. This is a delicate work that requires penetrating insight and a correct understanding of the shar'i principles.
Considering these six matters, it is necessary for the mufti, even if he is a muqallid, to have insight into all these matters. Such insight cannot be obtained merely by reading books and memorizing fiqh particulars; rather it requires a fiqh faculty and experience that can hardly be obtained except by practicing fatwa and training under expert teachers. Therefore they said: Not everyone who reads fiqh books is qualified for ifta until he has trained for ifta independently, and scholars have testified that he is qualified for ifta.
It is narrated from Imam Malik (may Allah have mercy on him) that he said: "Not everyone who wishes to sit for hadith and fatwa should sit until he consults the people of piety and virtue and the people of the mosque district. If they see him as qualified, he sits. And I did not sit until seventy scholars testified that I was fit for that." And Ibn Wahb said: A man came to Malik asking about a matter, and Ibn al-Qasim hurried and answered him. Malik turned to him in anger and said: "You dared to give fatwa, O Abd al-Rahman?" repeating it to him. "I did not give fatwa until I asked whether I was fit for fatwa." When his anger subsided, he was asked: "Whom did you ask?" He said: "Al-Zuhri and Rabi'a al-Ra'y." And on this basis, Ibn Hajar al-Haytami, as quoted by Ibn Abidin (may Allah have mercy on them), said: He was asked about a person who reads and studies fiqh books by himself, without having a teacher who explains religious and worldly matters to him, and then he is asked about religious and worldly matters, so he gives them fatwas relying on his reading in the books, and he does not pause when asked. Is this permissible for him? And if you say it is impermissible, what does he deserve from Allah and His Messenger? He answered: "It is not permissible for this mentioned person to give fatwa in any way, because he is a layman, ignorant, who does not know what he says. Rather, even one who has taken knowledge from reliable scholars is not allowed to give fatwa from
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage is an excerpt from the summary of rules of Rasm al-Mufti, discussing the essential qualifications of a mufti. It begins by explaining that legal rulings are general and absolute, while actions are specific, so a mufti must determine whether a particular action falls under a general rule. This requires ijtihad or effort. The fifth matter is that fatwas can differ based on individuals' circumstances and customs. The sixth matter is that new issues constantly arise, especially in modern times, and a mufti must apply general principles or analogical reasoning to them. Then the text emphasizes that mere book knowledge is insufficient; a mufti needs 'basira' (insight) and a developed fiqh faculty gained through supervised practice. To illustrate, it quotes Imam Malik, who did not sit for fatwa until seventy scholars certified him. He rebuked Ibn al-Qasim for giving a fatwa without proper authorization. Finally, Ibn Hajar al-Haytami rules that a self-taught person who reads books without a teacher cannot give fatwa, as he is ignorant and does not know what he is saying. This underscores the importance of traditional apprenticeship in Islamic scholarship.

Key Terms
البصيرة (al-basira): Penetrating insight and deep understanding of the Shariah gained through practice and training.
الممارسة (al-mumarasa): Practical training and repeated exercise in giving fatwa under expert supervision.
الإفتاء (al-ifta'): The act of issuing a legal ruling (fatwa) on a question.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what did Imam Malik do before he began giving fatwas?
A) He read all the books of fiqh available at his time.
B) He asked seventy scholars to testify that he was fit for fatwa.
C) He moved to a different city to study.
D) He only gave fatwas on matters he had seen the Prophet do.

Key Takeaway
A mufti must have practical training and insight; mere book reading without supervision and certification is insufficient for issuing fatwas.

Qualification Requirements for Issuing Fatwa
Defining qualifications and training for a mufti

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the necessary qualifications for a mufti and apply them to evaluate whether a person is permitted to issue fatwas.

Core Idea
Reading books alone never qualifies one for fatwa; only formal training and certification produce a competent mufti.

This lesson lays out the foundational rule that not every reader of fiqh books is entitled to issue fatwas. Drawing from the practice of Imam Malik and later authorities like Ibn Hajar al-Haytami and al-Khatib al-Baghdadi, the passage emphasizes the necessity of personal training under a qualified teacher and the development of a natural faculty (malaka nafsaniyya). Without these, a person remains an ignorant layman (ammi jahil) and his fatwas are prohibited. Understanding these criteria helps us distinguish between genuine scholars and those who assume the role without due qualification.

Guided Path
1
State the core principle
The passage opens by declaring that not everyone who reads fiqh books is qualified for fatwa. Identify the basic requirement beyond reading: independent training and scholarly testimony.
2
Examine Imam Malik's example
Why did Malik wait for seventy scholars to testify? What does this show about the social and scholarly validation process for a mufti?
Malik's caution demonstrates that even a scholar of his stature sought external confirmation.
3
Analyze Ibn Hajar al-Haytami's fatwa
The case of the self-taught person is explicitly addressed. Which two categories of people are contrasted, and what is the ruling for each?
The contrast is between the 'ammi jahil' and the expert with 'malaka nafsaniyya'.
4
Understand the concept of malaka nafsaniyya
How does this faculty develop? What distinguishes a real mufti from a book-reader?
Malaka is acquired through systematic study under teachers and sustained engagement with the discipline.
5
Explore the role of public authority
According to al-Khatib al-Baghdadi, what should the ruler do? What is the consequence for unqualified muftis?
The ruler has a duty to screen and prevent unqualified individuals from issuing fatwas.

تلخيص قواعد رسم المفتي
ليس كل من قرأ الكتب الفقهيّة أهلاً للإفتاء حتى يكون قد تدرب على الإفتاء بصفة مستقلة، وشهد له العلماء بأنه أهل للإفتاء.
وقد حكى عن الإمام مالك رحمه الله تعالى أنه قال: "ليس كل من أحب أن يجلس للحديث والفتيا جلس حتى يُشاور فيه أهل الصلاح والفضل وأهل الجهة من المسجد، فإن رأوه لذلك أهلاً جلس، وما جلست حتى شهد لي سبعون شيخاً من أهل العلم أنّى موضع لذلك."
وقال ابن وهب: وجاء رجل يسأل مالكاً عن مسألة، فبادر ابن القاسم فأفتاه، فأقبل عليه مالك كالمُغضَب وقال له: جَسَرْت على أن تُفتى يا عبد الرحمن، يكررها عليه، ما أفتيت حتى سألت هل أنا للفتيا موضع؟ فلما سكن غضبه، قيل له: من سألت؟ قال: الزهري وربيعةَ الرّأي وعلى هذا الأساس قال ابن حجر الهَيْتَمِي، كما نقل عنه ابن عابدين رحمهما الله تعالى:
سئل رحمه الله تعالى فى شخص يقرأ ويطالع الكتب الفقهية بنفسه، ولم يكن له شيخ يقرر له المسائل الدينية والدنيوية، ثمّ إنّه يُسأل عن مسائل دينية ودنيوية، فيفتيهم ويعتمد على مطالعته في الكتب، ولم يتوقف فيما يُسأل عنه، هل يجوز له ذلك؟ وإذا قلتم بعدم الجواز، فماذا يستحقه من قبل الله تعالى ورسوله صلى الله عليه وسلّم؟ فأجاب، نفع الله تعالى به، بقوله: لا يجوز لهذا المذكور الإفتاء بوجه من الوجوه، لأنه عامي جاهل، لا يدرى ما يقول، بل الذي أخذ العلم عن المشايخ المعتبرين، لا يجوز له أن يُفتي من كتاب ولا من كتابين بل قال النووي رحمه الله تعالى ولا من عشرة، فإنّ العشرة والعشرين قد يعتمدون كلهم على مقالةٍ ضعيفة في المذهب، فلا يجوز تقليدهم فيها، بخلاف الماهر الذى أخذ العلم عن أهله، وصارت له فيه ملكة نفسانية، فإنّه يميز بين الصحيح من غيره، ويعلم المسائل وما يتعلق بها على الوجه المعتمد به، فهذا هو الذي يُفتى النّاس، ويصلح أن يكون واسطة بينهم وبين الله تعالى. وأما غيره، فيلزمه إذا تسوّر هذا المنصب الشريف التعزيز البليغ، والزجر الشديد، الزاجر له ولأمثاله عن هذا الأمر القبيح الذي يؤدى إلى مفاسد لا تُحصى. والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم. وقال الخطيب البغدادي رحمه الله تعالى في الفقيه والمتفقه: "ينبغي لإمام المسلمين أن يتصفّح أحوال المفتين فمن كان يصلح للفتوى أقره عليها، ومن لم يكن من أهلها منعه منها... وأوعده بالعقوبة إن لم ينته عنها... والطريق للإمام إلى معرفة حال من يُريد نصبه للفتوى أن يسأل عنه أهل العلم في وقته، والمشهورين من فقهاء عصره" وقال مالك رحمه الله تعالى: "ولا ينبغى لرجل أن يرى نفسه أهلاً لشيئ حتّى يسئل من هو أعلم." ونقل ابن عابدين رحمه الله تعالى أنّه قال فى آخر منية المفتى: "لو أنّ الرّجل جميع كتب أصحابنا، لابد أن يتتلمذ للفتوى حتى يهتدى إليه، لأن كثيراً من المسائل يجاب عنه على عادات أهل الزمان فيما لا يخالف الشريعة."
Summary of the Rules of the Mufti's Decorum. Not everyone who reads fiqh books is qualified for issuing fatwas until he has trained in issuing fatwas independently, and scholars have testified that he is qualified for issuing fatwas. It has been narrated from Imam Malik (may Allah have mercy on him) that he said: 'Not everyone who wishes to sit for hadith and fatwa sits until he is consulted about by people of righteousness and virtue and the people of the locality from the mosque. If they see him as qualified for that, he sits. And I did not sit until seventy scholars testified that I am a place for that.' Ibn Wahb said: A man came to Malik asking about a matter, and Ibn al-Qasim rushed to give him a fatwa. Malik turned to him angrily and said: 'You dared to give fatwas, O Abd al-Rahman?' and repeated it to him. 'I did not give fatwas until I asked: Am I a place for fatwa?' When his anger subsided, he was asked: 'Whom did you ask?' He said: 'Al-Zuhri and Rabi‘a al-Ra‘y.' On this basis, Ibn Hajar al-Haytami, as quoted by Ibn Abidin (may Allah have mercy on them), said: He was asked about a person who reads and studies fiqh books by himself, and has no teacher to explain to him religious and worldly matters. Then he is asked about religious and worldly matters, so he gives them fatwas relying on his reading of the books, and does not hesitate in what he is asked. Is this permissible for him? And if you say it is not permissible, what does he deserve from Allah and His Messenger (peace be upon him)? He answered: It is not permissible for this mentioned person to give fatwas in any way, because he is an ignorant layman who does not know what he is saying. Rather, one who has taken knowledge from reliable teachers is not permitted to give fatwas from one book nor from two books. Rather, al-Nawawi (may Allah have mercy on him) said: nor from ten, for ten or twenty may all rely on a weak statement in the school, so it is not permissible to follow them in that. This is unlike the expert who has taken knowledge from its people and has developed a natural faculty (malaka nafsaniyya) in it, for he distinguishes the correct from others and knows the issues and what relates to them in the relied-upon manner. This is the one who gives fatwas to people and is fit to be an intermediary between them and Allah. As for others, if he assumes this noble position, he deserves severe punishment and harsh deterrence that will deter him and his likes from this ugly action that leads to countless corruptions. And Allah knows best. Al-Khatib al-Baghdadi (may Allah have mercy on him) said in al-Faqih wa al-Mutafaqqih: 'The ruler should examine the conditions of the muftis; whoever is fit for fatwa should be confirmed, and whoever is not among its people should be prevented... and he should threaten him with punishment if he does not desist... The way for the ruler to know the state of one he wants to appoint for fatwa is to ask about him from the scholars of his time and the well-known jurists of his era.' Malik (may Allah have mercy on him) said: 'A man should not consider himself qualified for something until he asks one who is more knowledgeable.' Ibn Abidin (may Allah have mercy on him) narrated that he said at the end of Minyat al-Mufti: 'Even if a man has all the books of our associates, he must still seek training for fatwa so that he is guided to it, because many issues are answered according to the customs of the people of the time in what does not contradict the Sharia.'
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings and principles regarding the qualifications necessary for a mufti. The author summarizes the rule that not everyone who reads fiqh books is competent to issue fatwas. The mufti must have undergone independent training and received certification (testimony) from recognized scholars. The text opens with an account from Imam Malik, who emphasized that he himself did not sit for fatwa until seventy scholars testified to his competence. When Ibn al-Qasim prematurely gave a fatwa, Malik rebuked him, asking if he had consulted those more knowledgeable. Ibn Hajar al-Haytami addresses a question about a self-taught person who reads books and issues fatwas. The ruling is clear: such a person is an ignorant layman (ammi jahil) and it is absolutely impermissible for him to give fatwas. Even studying from many books is insufficient, as al-Nawawi points out that multiple books may all rely on a weak opinion. The key qualification is that one must have taken knowledge from reliable teachers and developed a 'malaka nafsaniyya' (a spiritual/mental faculty) that enables him to distinguish correct from incorrect, and to know the relied-upon positions. Such a person is fit to be an intermediary between people and Allah. The passage then quotes al-Khatib al-Baghdadi, who says that the ruler (imam) should evaluate muftis and prevent unqualified ones. Finally, Ibn Abidin quotes that even mastery of all the books of the madhhab requires formal training with a teacher, because many issues are answered based on customs that do not contradict the Sharia. This passage does not present a dispute between madhhabs but rather a consensus across the Hanafi, Maliki, and Shafi‘i schools on the necessity of formal training and certification.

Key Terms
ملكة نفسانية (malaka nafsaniyya): A natural faculty or competence developed through proper training and study under scholars, enabling one to distinguish correct rulings from incorrect in the madhhab.
عامي جاهل (ammi jahil): A layperson who is ignorant of the detailed methodology of fiqh, lacking formal training and certification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the minimum requirement for a person to be qualified to issue fatwas?
A) Reading at least ten fiqh books
B) Having a teacher and developing a natural faculty (malaka) through training
C) Being appointed by the ruler regardless of training
D) Being able to answer any question without hesitation

Key Takeaway
A mufti must be trained, tested, and certified by recognized scholars; book knowledge alone is insufficient and can lead to serious religious corruption.

Qualification and Ijazah for the Mufti
Summary of rules for mufti qualification and authorization

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two essential qualifications for a mufti (expertise and authorization) and explain why formal ijazah is necessary in Hanafi fatwa practice.

Core Idea
Fatwa requires expertise and teacher authorization, not just book knowledge.

This passage distills the core requirements for a mufti in the Hanafi tradition. It warns against the danger of giving fatwa based on mere book learning or even reliance on many scholars if they follow weak positions. Instead, it elevates the qualified expert (mahir) who has developed a distinct faculty for discerning correct rulings and who has received formal authorization (ijazah) from his teachers. This lesson unpacks these conditions and their implications for contemporary fatwa practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary claim
Read the opening lines: the mufti must not rely on a small number of books or even consensus of many scholars if they follow weak positions. What is the key quality that overcomes this?
Look for the contrast between 'mere readers' and 'the expert (mahir)'.
2
Analyze the concept of 'mahir'
Define the term 'mahir' as used in the passage. It mentions a 'spiritual faculty' (malaka nafsaniyya) enabling distinction between authentic and weak rulings. What does this entail in practice?
Consider that this requires deep study under qualified teachers, not just reading.
3
Examine the role of ijazah
The passage concludes that a man should not set himself up for fatwa unless authorized by his shaykhs. Why is formal authorization (ijazah) necessary?
Ijazah is the acknowledgment that the student has attained the required expertise and is accountable to the tradition.
4
Consider the social dimension
Al-Khatib al-Baghdadi assigns the ruler the duty of screening muftis. Quoting Malik and Ibn Abidin, the passage emphasizes consulting the more learned and learning from customs. How do these external checks reinforce internal qualification?
The mufti does not operate in isolation; the community and authority have a role in ensuring integrity.

و فى ضوء أقوال السلف هذه لا ينبغى أن ينتصب الرجل للفتوى إلا إذا أجازه بذلك مشايخه و أساتذته.
Summary of the rules of the mufti's code. (1) Not from one book or two, but al-Nawawi said: not even from ten, for ten or twenty may all rely on a weak statement in the madhhab, so taqlid of them is not permissible. Unlike the expert who took knowledge from its people and acquired a spiritual faculty, for he distinguishes the correct from other, and knows the issues and what relates to them in the relied-upon manner. This is the one who gives fatwa to people and is fit to be an intermediary between them and Allah Almighty. As for others, if he dares to assume this noble office, he deserves severe rebuke and strong deterrence that prevents him and his likes from this ugly act that leads to countless harms. And Allah knows best. Al-Khatib al-Baghdadi said in al-Faqih wa al-Mutafaqqih: "The leader of the Muslims should examine the conditions of the muftis; whoever is fit for fatwa he confirms him, and whoever is not qualified he prevents him... and threatens him with punishment if he does not desist... The way for the leader to know the state of one he intends to appoint for fatwa is to ask the scholars of his time and the famous jurists of his era." And Malik said: "A man should not consider himself fit for anything until he asks someone more knowledgeable." And Ibn Abidin transmitted that he said at the end of Munyat al-Mufti: "Even if a man possesses all the books of our companions, he must still study for fatwa until he is guided, because many issues are answered according to the customs of the people of the time as long as they do not conflict with the Sharia." In light of these sayings of the predecessors, a man should not set himself up for fatwa unless he is authorized for that by his shaykhs and teachers.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage is a summary of rules for the mufti (Rasm al-Mufti). It opens by establishing that to give fatwa, one must be more than a mere reader of books; even consulting ten or twenty scholars is insufficient if they rely on weak positions. The key quality is being an expert (mahir) who has internalized knowledge and developed a faculty (malaka nafsaniyya) enabling him to distinguish authentic rulings. Such a person serves as an intermediary between people and Allah. Unqualified persons who assume this role deserve severe punishment. The passage then quotes al-Khatib al-Baghdadi on the duty of the Muslim ruler to screen muftis, and Malik on consulting the more learned. Ibn Abidin emphasizes that even owning all Hanafi books requires apprenticeship to understand customs that affect fatwa. The conclusion is that one must receive formal authorization (ijaza) from one's teachers. This lesson underscores that fatwa is a sacred responsibility, not a matter of personal ambition.

Key Terms
إجازة (ijāzah): Formal authorization from a teacher or shaykh to give fatwa, indicating the student has reached proficiency.
ماهر (māhir): Expert scholar who has internalized fiqh and can distinguish relied-upon rulings from weak ones.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the minimum prerequisite for a mufti to give fatwa?
A) Possessing all the books of the Hanafi school.
B) Having studied under many teachers.
C) Being an expert with a spiritual faculty and formal authorization.
D) Consulting ten scholars before giving an answer.

Key Takeaway
A mufti must be an expert (mahir) with a spiritual faculty to discern authentic rulings and must hold authorization (ijazah) from his teachers; mere book knowledge is insufficient.

Origin of Multiple Hanafi Opinions: Abu Hanifa's Teaching Method
Explains the origin of multiple Hanafi opinions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the origin of multiple opinions attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa and apply this understanding to distinguish between the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position and other views in fatwa practice.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa's teaching method of debating multiple possibilities is the source of many attributed opinions.

A student new to Hanafi fiqh might be puzzled by the many opinions ascribed to Imam Abu Hanifa. This lesson clarifies that these multiple opinions often arose from the Imam's unique teaching method: he would present and argue for several possibilities on a single issue, training his students in ijtihad. Understanding this origin is essential for a mufti to correctly weight opinions and avoid confusing historical development with the final mufta bihi position.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Teaching Method
Recognize that Abu Hanifa's teaching involved presenting multiple possible rulings for a single issue, debating them with proofs, and eventually settling on one view. This process is called tamhis (scrutiny).
This method trained students in analytical reasoning.
2
Trace the Attribution
Note that students like Abu Yusuf or Muhammad might adopt a possibility that Abu Hanifa had earlier considered but abandoned. Their opinion then traces back to the Imam in terms of origin, but it is not his final view.
Hence the phrase 'sayings of Abu Hanifa' can be ambiguous.
3
Apply to Fatwa Hierarchy
Understand that for a mufti, the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the one that settled after tamhis, not every transmitted opinion. This requires familiarity with the tabaqat (layers) of Hanafi scholarship.
Fatwa hierarchy prioritizes the final settled views.

تلخيص قواعد رسم المفتي
ومعناه على ما حققه العلامة الكوثري رحمه الله تعالى أن الإمام أبا حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى كان يُبدى أمام تلامذته احتمالات مختلفة في مسئلة واحدة، وكان أصحابه يأخذون بأحد هذه الاحتمالات. فكأن كل واحد منها رواية عنه، لأنه هو الذى أثار تلك الاحتمالات بأدلتها. ونحكى هنا كلام العلامة الكوثري رحمه الله تعالى بلفظه لما فيه من فوائد قال رحمه الله تعالى "ومنشأ ادعاء أن تلك الأقوال كلّها أقوال أبي حنيفة، هو ما كان يجرى عليه أبو حنيفة في تفقيه أصحابه من احتجاجه لأحد الأحكام المحتملة في مسألة وانتصاره له بأدلّة، ثمّ كرّروه بالردّ عليه بنقض أدلته، وبترجيحه الاحتمال الثاني بأدلّةٍ أخرى، ثمّ نقضها بترجيح احتمال ثالث بأدلة تدريباً لأصحابه على التفقه على خطوات ومراحل إلى أن يستقر الحكم المتعين في نهاية التمحيص، ويدوّن في الديوان فى عداد المسائل الممحصة، فمنهم من ترجح عنده غير ما استقر عليه الأمر من تلك الأقوال باجتهاده الخاص، فيكون هذا المترجح عنده قوله من وجه، وقول أبي حنيفة من وجه آخر، من حيث إنّه هو الذى أثار هذا الاحتمال ودلل عليه أولاً و إن عدل عنه أخيراً. ومصداق ذلك ما أخرجه ابن أبى العَوَّام عن محمد بن أحمد بن حماد بن محمد بن عبد الله
(۱) ابن أبي العوام: هو أبو القاسم عبد الله بن محمد بن أحمد بن يحيى بن الحارث بن أبي العوام السعدي، قاضي مصر، روى عن الإمام أبي جعفر الطحاوي، وأبى بشر الدولابي وغيرهما. وقد ذكر جملة من المترجمين ترجمة حفيده أبي العباس أحمد بشيئ من التفصيل، ونسبوا كتاب "فضائل أبي حنيفة" إليه، وأوضح الحال فضيلة الشيخ العلامة لطيف الرحمن البهرائيجي قائلاً: "أصل الكتاب لأبي القاسم جد أبى العبّاس... وأبو العباس روى عنه بواسطة أبيه أبي عبد الله محمد بن عبد الله. وجاء من قبله زيادات مثل "الموطأ" و "الآثار" للإمام محمد بن الحسن الشيباني رحمه الله " تُوُفِّي رحمه الله سنة ٣٣٥ هـ. . ليراجع مقدمة المحقق لكتاب "فضائل أبي حنيفة وأخباره ومناقبه لفضيلة الشيخ العلامة لطيف الرحمن البهر ائجي)
عن محمد بن شجاع سمعت الحسن بن أبي مالك وعبّاس بن الوليد وبشر بن الوليد وأبا علي الرازي يقولون: سمعنا أبا يوسف يقول: " ما قلت قولاً خالفت فيه أبا حنيفة إلا وهو قول قد قاله أبو حنيفة ثمّ رَغِب عنه. وحكى الكَرْدَري عن النيسابوري أن أبا يوسف لما ولي القضاء دخل عليه إسماعيل بن حمّاد بن الإمام، وتقدّم إليه خصمان، فلما جاء أوان الحكم قضى برأي الإمام. فقال له: كنت تُخالف الإمام في هذا. قال: إنّما كُنا نخالفه لنستخرج ما عنده من العلم فإذا جاء أوان الحكم ما يرتفع رأينا على رأي الشيخ اهـ ومثله عن محمد بن الحسن. وأخرج ابن أبي العوام عن إبراهيم بن أحمد بن سهل عن القاسم بن غسان عن أبيه عن أبي سليمان الجوزجاني عن محمد بن الحسن قال: كان أبو حنيفة قد حمل إلى بغداد، فاجتمع أصحابه جميعاً، وفيهم أبو يوسف وزفر وأسد بن عمرو وعامة الفقهاء المتقدمين من أصحابه، فعملوا مسألةً أيّدوها بالحجاج وتنو قوا في تقويمها، وقالوا نسأل أبا حنيفة أول ما يقدم. فلما قدم أبو حنيفة كان أول مسألة سُئل عنها تلك المسألة، فأجابهم بغير ما عندهم
(۱) راجع فضائل أبي حنيفة لابن أبي العوام، معرفة نسب أبي يوسف ص ٣٠٣ فقره ٦٩٨ طبع المكتبة الإمدادية ١٤٣١هـ (۲) الكَردَريّ (صاحب المناقب): هو محمد بن محمد بن شهاب بن يوسف الكردري البريقيني الخوارزمي الشهير بالبزازي: من أئمة فقهاء الحنفية. أصله من "كر در" بجهات خوارزم. تنقل في بلاد القرم والبلغار وحجّ، واشتهر. وكان يفتي بكفر "تيمورلنك" من كتبه الجامع الوجيز المعروف ب "الفتاوى البزازيّة"، و "المناقب الكردرية" في سيرة الإمام أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى، و "مختصر في بيان تعريفات الاحكام" و آداب "القضاء" توفّي رحمه الله سنة ٨٢٧ هـ. ليراجع الأعلام ٧ ٤٥) (۳) راجع مناقب أبي حنيفة لكردري ص ٤٠٥
(٤) أى تحوّدوا وبالغوا، كما في القاموس
Summary of the rules for the office of Mufti. Its meaning according to what Allama al-Kawthari (may Allah have mercy on him) verified: Imam Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) used to present different possibilities before his students on a single issue, and his companions would take one of these possibilities. So each one of them is like a narration from him, because he was the one who raised those possibilities with their proofs. We quote here the words of Allama al-Kawthari verbatim due to the benefits in them. He said: 'The origin of the claim that all those sayings are sayings of Abu Hanifa is the practice of Abu Hanifa in teaching his fiqh: he would argue for one of the possible rulings in a matter and support it with proofs, then they would refute him by rebutting his proofs, and he would prefer the second possibility with other proofs, then rebut that by preferring a third possibility with proofs, training his companions in fiqh step by step until the determined ruling settled at the end of scrutiny and was recorded in the diwan among the scrutinized issues. Some of them would find preponderance for other than what was settled upon from those sayings by their own ijtihad, so this preponderant one is his saying in one respect and Abu Hanifa's saying in another respect, because he was the one who raised this possibility and argued for it first, even if he later turned away from it. The evidence for that is what Ibn Abi al-Awwam narrated from Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Hammad ibn Muhammad ibn Abd Allah. (Footnote on Ibn Abi al-Awwam)... From Muhammad ibn Shuja: I heard al-Hasan ibn Abi Malik, Abbas ibn al-Walid, Bishr ibn al-Walid, and Abu Ali al-Razi say: We heard Abu Yusuf say: 'I never said a statement in which I disagreed with Abu Hanifa except that it was a statement that Abu Hanifa had said and then turned away from.' Al-Kardari narrated from al-Naysaburi that when Abu Yusuf became chief judge, Ismail ibn Hammad ibn al-Imam entered upon him, and two litigants came before him. When the time for judgment came, he ruled by the opinion of the Imam. He said to him: You used to disagree with the Imam on this. He said: We only used to disagree with him to extract what knowledge he had, but when the time for judgment comes, our opinion does not rise above the opinion of the Shaykh. Likewise from Muhammad ibn al-Hasan. Ibn Abi al-Awwam narrated from Ibrahim ibn Ahmad ibn Sahl from al-Qasim ibn Ghassan from his father from Abu Sulayman al-Juzjani from Muhammad ibn al-Hasan: Abu Hanifa was brought to Baghdad, and his companions gathered, including Abu Yusuf, Zufar, Asad ibn Amr, and all the advanced jurists among his companions. They worked on an issue, supported it with arguments, and refined it well, and said: We will ask Abu Hanifa as soon as he arrives. When Abu Hanifa arrived, the first issue he was asked about was that issue, and he answered them differently from what they had. (Footnotes)...
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage, from the chapter 'Summary of the rules for the office of Mufti', clarifies a crucial point in Hanafi methodology: how multiple, sometimes contradictory, opinions came to be attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa (d. 150 AH). The author, Muhammad Taqi Usmani, citing Allama al-Kawthari, explains that the Imam's teaching method involved presenting and arguing for multiple possible solutions to a legal problem, debating them with his students, and eventually settling on one view. The students, through their own ijtihad, might prefer a different possibility that Abu Hanifa had earlier considered but abandoned. This preponderated view is then attributed to the student but traces its origin to the Imam. This is supported by narrations from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, key companions of the Imam. Abu Yusuf explicitly states that any opinion he held contrary to Abu Hanifa was actually a view Abu Hanifa had once held and then abandoned. The story of the Baghdad trial illustrates this: the students prepared an issue expecting a certain answer, but Abu Hanifa answered differently, showing he had moved to a final position. This passage is foundational for understanding the tabaqat (hierarchy) of Hanafi scholarship and the nature of ikhtilaf within the madhhab. It guards against the misconception that every reported Hanafi opinion is directly and finally from the Imam, teaching muftis to carefully distinguish between the mufta bihi (relied-upon) and other views.

Key Terms
رسم المفتي (rasm al-mufti): The set of rules and conditions governing the practice of issuing fatwas.
تمحيص (tamhis): Scrutiny and sifting of evidence to arrive at the most correct ruling.
ممحصة (mumahhasa): Scrutinized issues that have been thoroughly examined and settled.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Allama al-Kawthari's explanation, what is the origin of many opinions attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa?
A) They are fabrications by later scholars.
B) They arose from the Imam's method of presenting multiple possibilities and debating them with his students.
C) They are independent ijtihad of his students with no connection to him.
D) They were revealed to him in dreams.

Key Takeaway
The multiple opinions attributed to Abu Hanifa often originated from his teaching method of exploring possibilities with his students; a mufti must distinguish these from his final settled views.

Adab al-Mufti — Ethics of the Mufti
intermediate
8 min
The Adab of Disagreement: Abu Yusuf's Deference to Abu Hanifa
Narration of Abu Yusuf's statement about his disagreements

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi principle that a mufti's disagreement with the imam is pedagogical and does not override the imam's ruling in practice.

Core Idea
Abu Yusuf's disagreements were to extract knowledge, not to oppose; in judgment, the imam's view prevails.

This passage from the works of al-Kardari and others presents a foundational adab for Hanafi muftis. It relates that Abu Yusuf, despite being a mujtahid and Chief Judge, considered his disagreements with Abu Hanifa as exercises to draw out the Imam's full reasoning. When actually judging, he would apply Abu Hanifa's position, not his own. This teaches us the hierarchy within the madhhab: the student's ijtihad serves the school, not the ego.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key figures and transmission
Note the chain of narrators and the two main figures: Abu Yusuf and Abu Hanifa. The narration is transmitted by multiple reliable students.
The multiple chains strengthen the reliability of this report in Hanafi adab.
2
Extract Abu Yusuf's core statement
Abu Yusuf says: 'I never said a statement in which I disagreed with Abu Hanifa except that it was a statement that Abu Hanifa had [previously] said and then abandoned.' This shows his disagreements were not original rejections.
The phrase 'رَغِب عنه' indicates that Abu Hanifa himself had moved away from that earlier view.
3
Understand the rationale for disagreement
In the second report, Abu Yusuf clarifies that the purpose of disagreeing was 'to extract what he had of knowledge' – a pedagogical method, not a challenge to authority.
This reflects the scholarly dialogue within the Hanafi school.
4
Apply the principle to practice
When appointed as judge, Abu Yusuf ruled by Abu Hanifa's opinion, even on matters where he had previously differed. This sets the rule for muftis: in fatwa and judgment, follow the relied-upon view of the madhhab.
The same is reported of Muhammad al-Shaybani, confirming the principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عن محمد بن شجاع سمعت الحسن بن أبي مالك وعبّاس بن الوليد وبشر بن الوليد وأبا علي الرازي يقولون: سمعنا أبا يوسف يقول: " ما قلت قولاً خالفت فيه أبا حنيفة إلا وهو قول قد قاله أبو حنيفة ثمّ رَغِب عنه. وحكى الكَرْدَري عن النيسابوري أن أبا يوسف لما ولي القضاء دخل عليه إسماعيل بن حمّاد بن الإمام، وتقدّم إليه خصمان، فلما جاء أوان الحكم قضى برأي الإمام. فقال له: كنت تُخالف الإمام في هذا. قال: إنّما كُنا نخالفه لنستخرج ما عنده من العلم فإذا جاء أوان الحكم ما يرتفع رأينا على رأي الشيخ اهـ ومثله عن محمد بن الحسن.
From Muhammad ibn Shuja': I heard al-Hasan ibn Abi Malik, 'Abbas ibn al-Walid, Bishr ibn al-Walid, and Abu 'Ali al-Razi saying: We heard Abu Yusuf say: 'I never said a statement in which I disagreed with Abu Hanifa except that it was a statement that Abu Hanifa had [previously] said and then abandoned.' Al-Kardari reported from al-Naysaburi that when Abu Yusuf was appointed as judge, Isma'il ibn Hammad ibn al-Imam entered upon him, and two litigants presented themselves to him. When the time for judgment came, he ruled by the opinion of the Imam [Abu Hanifa]. He [Isma'il] said to him: 'You used to disagree with the Imam in this.' He said: 'We only used to disagree with him to extract what he had of knowledge. When the time for judgment comes, our opinion cannot rise above the opinion of the Shaykh.' End quote. And similar is reported from Muhammad ibn al-Hasan.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage presents a key principle of Hanafi mufti adab: the relationship between the mujtahid imam and his students. Abu Yusuf, despite being a mujtahid in his own right (and later Chief Judge), affirms that his disagreements with Abu Hanifa were not true opposition. Rather, they were intended to draw out Abu Hanifa's full knowledge – to test and explore the reasoning. Al-Kardari's report emphasizes that in actual judgment, Abu Yusuf would adopt Abu Hanifa's position, even if he had previously argued differently. This illustrates the hierarchical deference within the madhhab: the student's ijtihad is subordinate to the imam's in applied rulings, especially in judicial and fatwa practice. The same is reported of Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms
قول (qawl): An opinion or statement of a jurist, specifically a ruling
رغب عنه (raghiba 'anhu): To abandon or turn away from an opinion, implying it is no longer held

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the narration, why did Abu Yusuf say he used to disagree with Abu Hanifa?
A) Because he believed his own opinion was superior.
B) To extract the knowledge that Abu Hanifa possessed.
C) Because Abu Hanifa had changed his opinion.
D) To establish his own independent madhhab.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi tradition, the disagreements of the Sahibayn were pedagogical, and a mufti must defer to the mufta bihi opinion of the school in practice.
